# PROJECT.md — Single Source of Truth

> **Status:** PRODUCT PIVOT (D35, 2026-06-25). New lead product = **Marker-Anchored AR Asset Platform** (§0). Prior stealth-glasses / 4D-splat-generation vision (§1–§9) is NOT discarded — it is **repurposed** (generation pipeline → authoring tools; mesh-first render reality → rendering guidance; glasses → deferred endgame surface) per the continuity map in §0a. Generation/library code exists and works (see §9c).
> **Last updated:** 2026-07-24 — **D105 (STRATEGIC PIVOT, tested both ways): DROP THE SPLAT for the body/face.** A textured mesh + real PBR skin renders **visibly sharper in the browser than our best splat at the same 10 MB** (`/skintest`, 27k tris + 2K maps, 1.2 s load; proof `motion_out/d105_splat_vs_mesh.png`) — and dropping the gaussian fit is *also* what unblocks the premium asset market, because every vendor (Epic, Reallusion, Daz, 3DScanStore) bars AI **training**, not AI **use**: an LLM driving a textured mesh is explicitly permitted, our fit + corrective MLP is explicitly not. Recommend: textured rigged mesh (Reallusion CC / Anny base + Audio2Face face + Kimodo motion + LLM director); splats demoted to an optional premium path. Prior: 2026-07-23 — **D104** (user-reported splat regression, root-caused and fixed; full detail in the Decision Log + SESSION_HANDOFF.md): the "distorted" splat was D102's FREE fit — its means had drifted **median 8.9 mm** off the mesh surface (gaussian spacing 2.5 mm) with hardened opacity; a control GT render proved the **real skin was never the problem**. Re-fit FROZEN on the real-skin 192-view capture → **held-out 27.29 dB, beats the free fit's 26.89 dB AND still animates**; swapped in as the live `poc_avatar.ply`. Also: **all five D100 SMOKEWORKS skins proven on the face** (the remaining weak link is face GEOMETRY + procedural irises, not texture); **MetaHuman's redistribution blocker disappeared in Epic's June-2025 relicence — D76 stands only on the AI-training clause now**; and **Meshy paid-tier clothing/hair is buildable today** because `mpfb_prefit.transfer()` binds raw garment meshes with no MHCLO metadata. Prior: D102–D103 (two "real ceiling" follow-ups, user-directed; full detail in SESSION_HANDOFF.md): **D102 (SPLAT DETAIL CEILING) — built the high-detail STATIC splat (`fit_gsplat_free.py`: means unfrozen + gsplat DefaultStrategy densification → `poc_avatar_hidetail.ply`, does NOT animate) and PROVED the D98 hypothesis wrong for our source: unfreezing+densifying does NOT beat mesh-anchored (control: free fit = frozen fit = 26.89 dB on identical real-skin GT). The detail wall is the SMOOTH CG SOURCE, confirmed from two angles now (more cameras D98, free densification D102). What DID help = the real D100 SMOKEWORKS skin (real brows/eyes/lips/nipples/navel/nails; added `--skin_*` flags to blender_render_skin.py). Remaining detail levers are SOURCE-side only: bake the D100 normal maps as displacement geometry, or real photo capture. D103 (CLOTHING REAL CEILING) — wired the MPFB2 fitting engine in as an offline bake (`mpfb_fit_blender.py`+`mpfb_prefit.py`, `fit_rest()` with affine fallback): subdivision gives 4-16× the polys (shirt 1095→4260v) = the geometry needed to DRAPE, plus programmatic ramped ease → t-shirt now reads as a loose tee with folds, not shrink-wrap; hair bun (excluded since D85) fixed + un-excluded. Fit accuracy ≈ affine; the win is geometry. Honest ceiling = the boxy proxy ASSETS themselves (no collars/seams/tailoring) — breaking it needs commissioned garments ~$300-1.5k, over budget. Wire-size flag: MPFB subdivided default outfit ~40MB (hair bun dominates). THROUGH-LINE: quality is now SOURCE-limited on both fronts, not code-limited — our fit/drape/collision/animation/render pipeline is no longer the bottleneck. Still owed: browser click-through.** ⟢ Prior batch D98–D101 (second four-front batch, user-directed; full detail in SESSION_HANDOFF.md): **D98 (SPLAT) — fixed the `/splat` zoom-in vanish (root cause: `zoomToCursor` dollied the camera along the cursor ray, so `minDistance` never bounded closest approach and off-body zooms flew through the thin body into the cloud; fix = straight dolly + per-model minDistance + target clamp). Built the user's multi-shell capture rig (`--rig shells`: 2 radii × 4 height-layers × 24 az = 192 views), but the refit was a WASH (28.39 vs 28.36 dB) — KEY FINDING: the fit is mesh-anchored with FROZEN means, so more views can't add geometric detail; the real detail lever is unfreezing the means + densification (sharper static splat, breaks animation binding — decision pending). Did NOT swap poc_avatar.ply. D99 (CLOTHING) — first DRESSED WALK live in the browser: new `dress_walk.py` + `/outfit_walk.bin` endpoint + `＋ Dressed walk` button; garment fit once at neutral, LBS-skinned per frame, mapped through the exact rigid native→display transform (verified 0.0001 mm). All four still owe a real browser click-through.** ⟢ Prior batch D95–D97 (three parallel subagents, user-directed): **D95 (SPLAT) — fixed the "gaussians are spheres/foam" problem. Root cause was the DATA not the custom renderer (confirmed by rendering the same .ply through gsplat's own reference rasterizer — same foam): the fit initialized every gaussian isotropically with identity orientation and exported an early checkpoint before anything flattened. Fixed the fit to initialize each gaussian as a thin surface-aligned disk (frame from the mesh normal, anisotropic scale, per-axis cap). Anisotropy ratio 1.13 → 7.85, disks lie flat on the surface (normal alignment 0.989), and held-out PSNR went UP 25.59 → 30.73 dB (a real quality gain, not a tradeoff). New poc_avatar.ply swapped in (old → poc_avatar_preD95.ply.bak), served live. Only fit_gsplat_poc.py changed. D96 (CLOTHING) — implemented the real fix flagged since D94: FIT-ONCE-AT-NEUTRAL + skeleton LBS. Fit the garment on Anny's raw T-pose (armpit open) where the clip is minimal, inherit each garment vertex's skinning weights from the barycentric blend of its 3 bound body vertices, then deform the garment with the SAME LBS the body uses (verified to reproduce anny's own posed body to 3e-16). Fold-clipping now SHRINKS with pose depth instead of growing (old shirt: 10%/−33mm at 40° growing to 10.7% at 80°; new: 8.2% at 40° shrinking to 5.3% at 80°). MILESTONE: demonstrated the same neutral-fit shirt+pants deforming across real WALK frames (motion_out/d95_walk_dressed.png) — first clothes-on-the-walking-avatar, no per-frame re-fit. Wired into the live ＋Outfit preview. Honest floor: the pose-INDEPENDENT ~4% affine-approximation blotch remains (needs the MPFB2 engine, out of scope) so the light surface-push (D94) is kept as a safety net. D97 (RESEARCH) — clean+affordable realistic-avatar asset sourcing (research/avatar-asset-sources-2026.md): the binding constraint is the no-AI/ML clause (nearly every high-end scan vendor added one 2023-25, and our gaussian-fit + corrective-MLP trips it), not redistribution. Clean shortlist: Lee Perry-Smith "Infinite" head (CC-BY 3.0, film-grade, free), SMOKEWORKS Skins Vol.0/1 (CC-BY 4.0, MakeHuman-drop-in), self-hosted Stable Diffusion for pore/detail, and commission-with-rights-assigned (~$300-1.5k head / ~$1.5-6k body) — notably Infinite-Realities already runs a splat capture service with an Inria commercial license. New BLOCKED-with-evidence: Triplegangers, Digital Emily (CC-NC despite mislabeled MIT), and Adobe Firefly (ToS bars using outputs to train/improve ML models). See Decision Log D95/D96/D97.** Earlier: D94: **User asked the RIGHT question — "why isn't it fitting properly, the clothes and hair still clip" — instead of accepting another patch. Actually diagnosed it with proper signed-distance-to-surface measurement instead of guessing: (1) the affine binding is approximate, so ~4% of a garment's vertices sit a few mm inside even on the neutral body; (2) far worse, the arms-down PoSE folds the body (the armpit closes), and garment vertices anchored to body points inside that fold get dragged deep inside — measured up to 33mm at the 40° arms-down pose, scaling almost linearly with the pose angle (−7mm at 0° → −33mm at 40°). Ruled out two tempting wrong explanations by direct test: it's NOT the offset direction (co-rotating the offset in the binding-triangle frame changed nothing) and NOT near-zero offsets (the deep verts have normal-sized offsets — it's their ANCHOR point that's in the fold). D93's push helped but used the nearest-VERTEX normal, which points the wrong way in a concave crease, so it left the deep armpit cases stuck. Fixed by rewriting the push to use the closest point on the body SURFACE and that triangle's own normal, iterated, measured against the actually-DISPLAYED body mesh — verified it drops interior vertices from 112→~0 at every pose angle and renders visibly clean at the full 40° (the blotchy skin patches from the user's screenshot are gone). Honest remainder: a handful of vertices (≤6 on the worst asset) can survive in the deepest armpit fold but are not visually significant; the truly complete fix is still the flagged one — fit at neutral and skin the garment with the skeleton rather than re-evaluating the affine binding at a posed state. See Decision Log D94.** Earlier: D93: **User sent a screenshot: a t-shirt with a symmetric blotchy pattern of skin-colored patches across the chest/torso, and asked directly whether the mesh has real gaps or is clipping into the body. Root-caused it as a THIRD, distinct bug from D90/D91: some vertices in a garment's own authored binding have a genuinely near-zero offset by design (seams, snug-fit lines) -- D91's `offset_boost` scales that offset, but scaling a near-zero number is still near-zero, so those specific vertices stayed glued to (or a hair's width inside) the body regardless of boost. Because rendering is OPAQUE (no blending), a vertex even slightly inside the body doesn't fade through softly -- the closer body surface wins that pixel outright, producing exactly the clean-edged blotchy islands in the screenshot. Confirmed by checking the D91 boost-value test renders already on file: those specific patches barely moved from boost 1.0 to 5.0, exactly what a near-zero base offset predicts and boost cannot fix. Added `outfit_lib.push_off_surface()` -- computes real outward body-surface normals and enforces a minimum clearance (4mm default) along them, independent of and complementary to `offset_boost`. Verified by rendering the exact shirt from the screenshot before/after: blotchy pattern gone, clean coverage. Also checked pants (one small persistent knee-area gap remains, unaffected by either fix -- likely a genuine hole in that asset's own mesh, a separate/different issue) and hair (bald center strip unchanged, confirming -- again -- that's a separate structural problem, not a clearance or sizing issue). Full 35-asset catalog re-validated, no regressions. See Decision Log D93.** Earlier: D92: **User asked directly: "clothing and hair need more adjustments... can I control it manually?" instead of another round of me guessing defaults. Added two sliders to the viewer's right panel ("Outfit sizing" — Hair, Clothing, 0.5x-6x) that override D91's per-kind offset-boost defaults live, refitting the ＋ Outfit preview on drag. Wired end-to-end: `viewer.html` sliders -> `?hair_boost=&clothing_boost=` query params on `/compose.bin` -> `build_compose_buffer(sel, boosts)` -> `fit_asset_checked(..., offset_boost=...)`, with D91's tuned values as the default when a slider hasn't been touched. Verified the plumbing actually works via the data layer (isolated the hair sub-range of the returned buffer and confirmed its bbox changes with the slider value; the overall buffer bbox is dominated by the body so a naive whole-buffer check falsely looked unchanged at first). See Decision Log D92.** Earlier: D91: **The user tried D90's fix and reported it made things WORSE — "fuzzy, distorted," not just bigger — and asked for exactly what D90 didn't deliver: a plain enlargement of the same correctly-shaped asset. Reverted D90's `den/10` reinterpretation (restored the D89 state, which the user confirmed was correctly SHAPED, just undersized) and added a genuinely uniform offset multiplier instead — one that can't introduce per-axis distortion since it scales x/y/z identically. Empirically tuned per asset KIND by rendering several candidate values, not guessed: clothing (tops/bottoms) needed ~3x to close the visible skin gaps cleanly with no distortion; hair, tested the same way, got visibly WORSE past ~1.5x (jagged/shard edges) with no real coverage improvement — its own gap (a bald strip down the back of the head) turned out to already be present even with NO boost at all, i.e. it isn't a sizing problem, a separate not-yet-solved issue, kept honestly unaddressed rather than papered over with a bigger multiplier. Wired as a per-kind default in `outfit_lib.fit_asset_checked` (clothing=3.0, hair=1.2, eyebrows=1.0) rather than one global constant. Re-validated the full 35-asset catalog (still 35/35) and re-rendered pants/shirt/hair before/after — confirmed via direct comparison, not assumed. See Decision Log D91.** Earlier: D90: **The user actually clicked through D89's fix and found it wasn't the whole story: every garment fit but visibly "a size smaller" — hair sinking into the skull with skin showing through, pants/shirts showing bare skin through the front like they belonged to a smaller body. Root-caused numerically (not guessed): the `.mhclo` file's per-axis offset-scale-calibration `den` value (D83) is recorded in MakeHuman's native unit, DECIMETERS (1 unit = 10cm), while the code compared it directly against Anny's basemesh distances in METERS with no conversion — shrinking every garment's outward-projecting offset to ~10% of its correct magnitude (measured: scale ratios of ~0.10 on every axis of every asset checked; dividing `den` by 10 alone moved them all to ~0.98-1.07). This bug predates D89 and was already present since D83 introduced the scale calibration — it was simply masked by the much bigger D89 index-space bug's chaos until that got fixed and this became the dominant visible symptom. Fixed in `mhclo_fit.py` (one-line unit conversion at parse time); re-rendered pants/shirt/hair before and after — confirmed the "size smaller" clipping is gone (full leg/torso coverage, full hair volume). The one D89 exception (the reverse-braid bun) is unaffected by this fix, confirming that residual issue really is a separate algorithmic gap, not a units problem. See Decision Log D90.** Earlier: D89: **Chased the clothing-fitting problem to its real root cause and fixed most of it. Installed the real MPFB2 Blender addon (GPL source / CC0 assets / explicitly-unrestricted output per its own license doc) as a DIAGNOSTIC tool and proved a previously-"unfixably broken" flowing-hair asset fits cleanly through MPFB2's own engine — confirming the asset was never the problem. Then found the actual bug: `mhclo_fit.py` was fitting garments against Anny's REDUCED, RENUMBERED 13,718-vertex default-topology array, while `.mhclo` files are authored against MakeHuman's RAW 19,158-vertex basemesh — a genuine INDEX-SPACE mismatch, not the "precision limit" D87 assumed. Fixed by fitting against `anny.Anny(topology="makehuman", remove_unattached_vertices=False)` instead — numerically verified to be an EXACT (0.00mm) surface match to the displayed body, so no MPFB2 runtime dependency was actually needed, just the right Anny call. Re-rendered every catalog asset (not just re-ran the numeric checks) against the fix: all 3 previously-excluded "shattered" tops are now genuinely clean garments — un-excluded. One asset (a reverse-braid bun) is honestly still broken — a flat ring instead of a bun, improved but not fixed, because even MPFB2's own basemesh + OUR fit code doesn't reproduce MPFB2's own correct result, meaning the residual gap is in the fitting ALGORITHM for this one extreme-extrapolation asset, not the basemesh — kept excluded rather than shipping a differently-broken result. See Decision Log D89.** Earlier: D88: **Actually executed the D87 refit (the prior session's background job never survived — no process, no output existed at session start) — the correct 96-view (4 elevation rings x 24 azimuth, `--frames` is TOTAL not per-ring, first attempt only produced 24) capture + gsplat fit, held-out PSNR 25.59dB (matches D83's quality tier, no overfit gap vs train 25.58dB). See Decision Log D88.** Earlier: D87: **The user pushed back hard on both remaining fronts and got honest answers + real fixes on both: (1) splat — found the renderer was collapsing every gaussian's real shape (rotation+per-axis scale) into a single isotropic circle, fixed it to render true anisotropic ellipses (the actual 3DGS technique), but HONESTLY this fit's gaussians measured almost perfectly spherical already (ratio ~1.1), so the deeper cause is the fit ITSELF — the offline PoC turntable only ever used a single elevation ring (never looks at the top of the head or underarms), unlike the live viewer's own multi-layer capture rig UI. Fixed the render script to support multiple elevation rings and re-rendered at 4 rings x 24 views = 96 (was 36, one ring), refitting now. (2) Clothing — said plainly that this ISN'T actually simple premade drag-and-drop the way it looks: MHCLO assets are an approximate per-vertex affine fit calibrated against MakeHuman's exact basemesh, ours is a close-but-not-identical reimplementation, so quality varies unpredictably per-asset; a real fix needs the actual MPFB2 Blender addon (not attempted yet, a genuinely bigger lift, offered as the next investment rather than another narrow patch). See Decision Log D83.** Earlier: D82: **Splat renderer REBUILT on the real root cause (D81's depth-sort fix was necessary but not sufficient — the renderer relied on gl_PointSize, and this box's ANGLE/Direct3D11 WebGL backend has unreliable/capped point-sprite sizing, so no amount of size/alpha tuning could fix "just floating points"). See Decision Log D82.** Earlier: D81: **Eyes fixed (the live viewer's SOMA-topology body had NO facial geometry at all -- switched to the DEFAULT topology, which does; added a procedural sclera/pupil vertex-color shade), splat "point cloud" fixed (per-frame depth-sort + bigger/brighter splats -- THREE.Points draws in buffer order not depth order, which was the real cause), and the MakeHuman/MPFB2 CC0/CC-BY asset ecosystem (hair, clothes, hands/nose/ear/cheek detail, eyebrows, eyelashes, beards -- the SAME family D71/D72's skin already comes from) found, license-verified (zero AI-training bars, zero caps, zero redistribution restrictions), and its MHCLO binding format decoded into a general, PROVEN fitter (dataset/mhclo_fit.py) -- downloaded real CC0 packs and empirically confirmed clothing + eyebrows fit Anny's native mesh with ZERO remapping (rendered proof in motion_out/mhclo_proof_*.png). See Decision Log D81.** Earlier: D80: **Splat-button bug FIXED (a silent WebGL shader-compile failure — the D79 shader referenced an undeclared `color` attribute after `vertexColors` was turned off; WebGL compile failures never throw, so nothing caught it) + a real QUALITY PASS: projected-pixel color init (each gaussian samples its own color from the views that face it, instead of flat grey) + a neighbor color-smoothness prior + best-held-out-PSNR checkpointing (root-caused why quality DEGRADED late in training: too few views to constrain high-order SH, so the optimizer used them to re-introduce marble — exporting the best checkpoint instead of the last one fixes it without hand-tuning) → held-out PSNR 20.2dB → 25.7dB, clean skin-toned body from every angle. Files: serve_viewer.py, viewer.html. See Decision Log D79.** Earlier: D78: **POC EXECUTED — the D74 Milestone-0 static gaussian fit RUNS END-TO-END on 100% CC0 assets. Pipeline (all on the 3090, no COLMAP since synthetic renders give exact poses): CC0-skinned Anny UV OBJ → Blender Cycles calibrated turntable (24 views @256px, NEW `--poses` intrinsics/extrinsics dump) → gsplat MESH-ANCHORED fit (gaussians init at mesh verts, near-frozen means + scale-clamp = surface shell) → standard 3DGS `.ply` + turntable. Result: recognizable correctly-posed full-body gaussian avatar; held-out PSNR 20.2dB ≈ train 20.3dB = genuine multi-view reconstruction, confirming the D74 'fitting = LOW risk' gate on a clean-license stack. Packages: pulled ONLY plyfile+tyro under a torch/numpy constraints file (did NOT run the examples' requirements.txt — it pins torch 2.9/numpy 2.0 and would break the D70 env). Bug fixed: Blender's OBJ importer rotates Y-up→Z-up (+90°X) so verts needed (x,y,z)→(x,-z,y) to match the camera frame. Honest quality gap: per-gaussian color speckle (24 views, no densification, grey init) → NEXT = densification + projected-color init + more views, THEN the real D74 bet (rig-anchor + pose correctives + fit to REAL capture). New: `dataset/fit_gsplat_poc.py`, `blender_render_skin.py --poses`. See Decision Log D78.** Earlier: D77: **BOUGHT-ASSET STRATEGY. User asked if they can just buy realistic meshes/textures from individual artists, start with a small set, ship a PoC, iterate. Answer: right shape, gated on WHAT you buy. Any bought asset must clear TWO gates — (1) the AI/ML-derivative clause (our gaussian bake + corrective MLPs trip it; the big marketplaces — TurboSquid/CGTrader/Sketchfab/ArtStation/Fab — ADDED this clause in 2023-25, so their STANDARD licenses fail by default like MetaHuman), and (2) redistribution in a hosted/browser product (helped by shipping only the derived SPLAT, not the original). The move that clears both = buy the RIGHTS not the asset: a custom addendum, or best, a commission/work-for-hire with rights ASSIGNED to you (you OWN it → zero clause risk). PoC: prove the pipeline on ship-safe CC0 (PolyHaven/AmbientCG/MPFB2, the D71/D72 path) so nothing is thrown away; standard-license marketplace assets prove the tech but force a full re-source to ship. Highest-leverage: CC0 for plumbing + commission ONE hero asset to prove the realism ceiling with rights that survive to production. See Decision Log D77.** Earlier: D76: **MetaHuman RECONSIDERED under the D74 "rig-not-train" pivot. User asked: if we're only RIGGING assets now (not training a model), why not use MetaHuman meshes directly + solve browser weight with view-dependent LOD? See Decision Log D69.** Earlier: D68: **RUNTIME AI-CONTROL ARCHITECTURE verified (survey of NVIDIA ACE / Inworld / Convai + primary sources) — the user's puppet/data-packet + separate-specialists + DeepSeek-MTP intuitions are all CORRECT and match the mainstream pattern. THE "TWO-CLOCK" SPLIT: (1) DIRECTOR = the LLM, runs PER TURN, emits text + emotion label + sparse gesture/action TAGS — NEVER joint angles/blendshapes, never per-frame; (2) ANIMATOR = on-device @30-60fps, FACE driven by AUDIO (audio→ARKit blendshapes), BODY driven by the tags (clip library + state machine). FACE = solved+clean+on-device: LAM_Audio2Expression (Apache, ONNX, CPU real-time, audio→52 ARKit) primary; Audio2Face-3D (NVIDIA Open Model, 30fps, 11 emotions) higher-fidelity; AVOID NeuroSync (CC-BY-NC). BODY = curated clean mocap library + state machine triggered by LLM tags (ACE knobs: posture/gesture/facial_gesture/position_state); NO shipping system LLM-generates joint angles; generative co-speech gesture (EMAGE/DiffSHEG/MotionGPT) is AUTHORING-TIME/desktop research + mostly NON-COMMERCIAL data → only Kimodo-SOMA-SEED is clean (NVIDIA Open Model, 288h open Bones-SEED; offline ~2-5s/clip). Non-robotic look = INERTIALIZATION on transitions + MOTION MATCHING for locomotion + always-on additive breathing/gaze (NOT a heavier model). DEEPSEEK MTP/SPECULATIVE DECODING: user right — it's LOSSLESS (full quality, ~1.8x), but it speeds SUSTAINED STREAMING (keeps TTS fed), NOT the initial response latency (that's ENDPOINTING/smart-turn VAD + warm connection + start-TTS-on-first-sentence), and it's LANGUAGE-LAYER ONLY (motion/face nets are frame-clocked, nothing to speculate). SEPARATE SPECIALISTS validated (each on its own clock; face stays audio-synced even while LLM is slow). Control packet ≈ 52 blendshapes + 163 joint angles/frame ≈ 25-30 KB/s (3 orders below video = the whole justification for on-device standalone gaussians). LLM placement: cloud director + on-device SLM fallback (Phi-3.5-mini MIT / Qwen2.5-1.5B Apache; AVOID Qwen2.5-3B custom, Llama-Community, Gemma-Terms = non-OSI; Nemotron-4-4B = purpose-built on-device digital-human SLM). Mixed-modality = decoupled front-ends → one reconstructor. HUMANOIDS upgraded from "avoid" to "deferred-but-viable": clean path = Anny (Apache-2.0 parametric body) + LHM architecture. Start narrow+deep, behind the D49 phone-playback gate. See Decision Log D55.** Earlier: D54: **Multi-modal "full-context" dataset (dense views + mesh GT + motions + physics + text) evaluated + L4GM-quality diagnosed. Of the 5 modalities only TWO are fidelity levers — dense angle images + 3D mesh GT; motions=coverage, physics/text=capability-not-sharpness. L4GM is blurry BY ARCHITECTURE (feed-forward amortized, low fixed gaussian budget, single-view), NOT a pixel-cap-for-smoothness (smoothness = temporal interpolation). Key reframe: a rich dataset is necessary but NOT sufficient — quality is capped by representation/budget, supervision resolution, input-view count, and feed-forward-vs-optimization (hybrid init+refine = biggest jump). "Rent GPUs, no problem" underestimates: training hours are ~⅓; the multi-TB dataset pipeline + architecture R&D iteration + eval harness are the real cost. See Decision Log D54.** Earlier: D53: **Synthetic-data (Unreal/Omniverse Replicator/Unity Perception → multi-view animated Objaverse → 4DGS) plan to train a clean-license feed-forward text/image/video→4DGS model evaluated — FEASIBLE (it's the L4GM recipe; synthetic ground truth dissolves D49's cross-view-consistency problem for free), but it improves only the GENERATION axis: cleanliness bottleneck moves OFF the engines onto MOTIONS (SMPL/AMASS=NC, Mixamo gray), CC0/CC-BY Objaverse filtering, gsplat-not-Inria fitting, and open patent FTO; "per-frame-fit-then-stitch" is the wrong supervision (prefer deformable rep / rendering-loss); sim-to-real gap → object-centric; foundation training unrealistic on the shared 5090. Runtime gates (D47/D48) untouched → still deferred-premium; D49 playback test still comes first. See Decision Log D53.** Earlier: D52: **SV4D 2.0 Stage-A RUNS end-to-end on the 5090** — `camel.gif` → 4 novel-view videos (`generation/sv4d2_out/`, ~7 min, clean). Reusable win = the Blackwell (sm_120) attention fix (monkeypatch `xformers.memory_efficient_attention`→torch SDPA, rank-aware for head_dim-512; `generative-models/run_sv4d2_patched.py`). **Stage A done; Stage B (multi-view video → dynamic splat, gsplat-rasterized) is the real remaining work.** Still gated by shared GPU (opportunistic windows; don't evict shnri's qwen). See Decision Log D52. Earlier: D51: **SV4D 2.0 self-host build COMPLETE on the 5090** (env from `trellis2` clone, 12GB weights, deps reconciled, `sgm` imports clean, validated to model-load). Key findings: (a) SV4D2's open release outputs **multi-view VIDEOS not splats** → a Stage-B 4D-gaussian recon (gsplat-rasterized, clean) is the real remaining work; (b) **license flag** — README says "research purposes," verify commercial terms; (c) box is a **shared multi-user server**, the 5090 is held by another user's live qwen3.6 service → SV4D run **parked, ready, resumes when GPU frees** (watcher armed; won't evict others' work). See Decision Log D51. Earlier: D50: **Tier-1 phone render-floor test PASSES empirically** — **~600k gaussians (3×200k objects) hold 45–60fps sustained over 2 min on an iPhone 14 @ DPR 2.0 with auto-orbit, no thermal decay** (via WebGL/mkkellogg, auto-orbit forcing per-frame re-sort) — exceeds §2's per-object budget with headroom on a 2022 phone. Refines D48's "rendering wall overstated" from argued → measured: the runtime floor is reachable. Caveats: floor only (4D adds deformation), one 200k object (multi-object TBD), one device (LOD tiers still mandatory), streaming untested. Deploy lesson: GS3D needs `worker-src blob:` + `wasm-unsafe-eval` CSP (Railway blocked both) or just GitHub Pages. Next: Tier-2 animated-deformation test, Tier-3 streaming sizes. See Decision Log D50. Earlier: D49: evaluated two image/video→4D papers. **SV4D (Stability, arXiv 2407.17470) = usable today for a pre-revenue startup** (Community License, commercial under ~$1M ARR; verify HF terms, check SV4D 2.0); **CAT4D (Google DeepMind, 2411.18613) = NOT usable** (no weights released). User's `image→multiview→per-view-videos→4DGS` pipeline is the correct SOTA shape, **but the crux is cross-view temporal consistency** — animating views independently → garbage; SV4D/CAT4D's contribution is enforcing it jointly, so use SV4D's core or retrain clean-room. Generation = per-scene optimization, **minutes/asset** (premium async, not instant), and quality doesn't touch the D48 runtime gates. **Action: de-risk in REVERSE — prove ONE SV4D output plays back on a real phone (WebGPU player, fps/thermal/size/iOS-AR) BEFORE building the generator.** See Decision Log D49. Earlier: D48: refined D47 after user due-diligence. **"Apple SHARP" = apple/ml-sharp = STATIC single-image 3DGS (non-commercial), NOT 4D**; the "4DGS-Video-Generator" repo fakes 4D by stacking per-frame SHARP PLYs (~63MB/frame, NC, no playback). **Correction owed: D47 overstated the mobile-rendering wall** — WebGPU GPU-sort shipped on iOS Safari (iOS 26) + Android Chrome, and the streaming-cost nightmare assumed continuous volumetric streaming, not our download-once-loop (~20–80MB on a free-egress CDN). **Clean-room "copy the model not the code"** = legal on copyright (gsplat precedent) but a months-long retrain gated on PATENT freedom-to-operate, not a loophole. **Still gates 4DGS to deferred-premium (not pivot):** iOS renders-in-canvas but can't world-anchor splats in AR (viewer-not-AR), ~5–30× heavier asset + mesh fallback needed, research-grade tooling, NC generation. **Updated verdict: 4DGS = a credible premium un-anchored WebGPU-device hero feature worth a spike AFTER the mesh MVP — not the foundation.** See Decision Log D48. Earlier: D47: a **pure-4DGS (4D Gaussian Splatting) animation pivot** (L4GM / "Apple SHARP" / 4D-GS → "pure 4DGS web viewer") was evaluated and **DECLINED**. Research verdict: **generation is feasible on the 5090, but RUNTIME PLAYBACK on consumer phones is a brick wall** — the most advanced commercial 4DGS streamer (Gracia) is WebGPU-desktop-only at ~80 Mbit/s, smartphones unsupported; iOS has no path at all; and the stack is non-commercial at every layer (L4GM NC, Inria rasterizer NC). It optimized the wrong latency (§3). "Apple SHARP" could not be confirmed to exist. **Mesh-first D46 stands; animated splats stay deferred R&D; today's premium "wow" = STATIC TripoSplat, not animated.** See Decision Log D47. Earlier: D46: generation architecture LOCKED. **Self-host = the user-facing ENGINE; Tripo API = back-office spare tire (overflow only, never in the user path — routing end-users' generation through a vendor IS the anti-resale violation, D45). Meshy DROPPED (UniRig rigs any category vs Meshy's humanoid-only).** Stack: mesh "Standard" lane = TRELLIS.2; splat "Photoreal" lane = **TripoSplat (MIT) self-host** (static hero tier, mesh-first still governs); rig = UniRig. **MVP animation = presets + custom-upload** (auto-rig→motion-library + transform anims + user-uploaded rigged GLB/FBX; keyframe studio + AI-assist deferred). **2D = billboard + 2D→3D** (Live2D-style 2D rigging deferred). See Decision Log D46. Earlier: D45: deep-research settled the Tripo-vs-Meshy "buy" comparison (the D43/D44 open item). Two findings reshape the call: (a) **neither sells Gaussian splatting via paid API** — Tripo's TripoSplat is MIT open-source you self-host, so "offload splatting" is impossible; (b) **our "customer uploads → we generate → they own it" reseller flow bumps both vendors' anti-resale/anti-compete clauses** (need a written white-label/enterprise agreement either way; Meshy §2.6(xi) also bars training a competing model on their output). Pricing is ~$0.30/textured mesh on both; Meshy is 4× cheaper on rig+animation (8cr vs 35cr). **Decision: KEEP self-hosted TRELLIS.2 as default ($0/asset, clean license, no anti-resale exposure); buy only for overflow — Tripo if one mesh vendor (transparent $0.01/cr + MIT TripoSplat ecosystem), Meshy only as a cheap rig/anim lever. Splatting stays self-hosted (TripoSplat MIT) regardless.** See Decision Log D45. Earlier: 2026-06-28 — D44: benchmarked TRELLIS.2-4B locally on the 5090 — EXCELLENT game-ready PBR (decisively beats our gsplat-bake), self-hosted, clean-license (with RMBG→u2net swap), $0/asset, ~80–145s/asset; **recommend adopting TRELLIS.2 as the geometry+texture backend** (Tripo "buy" comparison still pending credits). D43: our gsplat→bake is the WRONG texture method (commercial tools use multi-view PBR diffusion) — see [research/generation-texture-rigging.md](research/generation-texture-rigging.md). Earlier: 2026-06-27 — D42 deepens the no-code AUTHORING/GENERATION suite as the lead workstream (video+image→3D object/animation, animation editor + drag-drop motion + AI-assist, templates, AR scene/page editor + themes, splatting-made-easy); the four Phase-1 plumbing gaps (Stripe, R2/CDN, analytics, 2D-canvas) are recorded + deferred. See §0.5 + Decision Log D42. Earlier: 2026-06-25 (D36: a SEPARATE wearer-facing product — **AR Productivity Glasses** — was spun out into its own SSOT [GLASSES.md](GLASSES.md). Both projects are kept: this file remains the SSOT for the D35 platform; the glasses live in GLASSES.md. D35: PIVOT to a no-code, marker-anchored AR asset platform for businesses — two publish surfaces, un-anchored web "view in 3D" FIRST, anchored marker-pointer + owner-seeded per-location map SECOND. Carries D34 mesh-first + D32 library + D24–D29 generation as building blocks.)
> **Companion SSOT:** [GLASSES.md](GLASSES.md) — the personal AR productivity/dev cockpit glasses (gaze + confirm-ladder input, phone-offload). Distinct product from the platform below; shares phone-offload (§2) + cross-device discipline (§2a).
> **Maintenance rule:** This file is the canonical project log. Update it whenever a decision, plan, feature spec, or idea changes — in conversation OR in files. Append to the **Decision Log** when an idea evolves; edit the relevant section when a spec changes. Keep older decisions visible (strike-through or "superseded by") rather than deleting them, so the reasoning trail survives.

## 0. CURRENT PRODUCT DIRECTION — Marker-Anchored AR Asset Platform (D35, the lead product)

*A no-code platform where any business creates a 3D/AR asset and publishes it to two surfaces: **anchored** to a real place (via a physical marker that points to a cloud-hosted, owner-seeded map), or **un-anchored** as a "view in 3D" widget on a website or print.* One asset, two surfaces, no code.

### 0.1 The product in one paragraph
A restaurant owner designs an animated 3D sign (from a drawing, a product photo, or a template) and chooses how to publish. **Anchored:** scan the storefront once, place the sign in 3D, and the platform mints a **physical marker** (QR or branded image) to hang by the door — a passerby with AR glasses or a phone reads it and the sign appears welded to the storefront, staying put as they move. **Un-anchored:** the same asset becomes a "view in 3D / view in your space" widget for a website or print piece, viewable instantly in any browser — no app, no marker.

### 0.2 Why this shape (the core insight)
Precise, persistent, world-anchored AR normally needs a pre-built 3D map of the location, and building a global map is a planetary data problem. We avoid it entirely:
1. **The marker carries a POINTER, not a map.** A QR/image marker can't hold a multi-MB visual map, but it can hold a URL/ID pointing to the store's map+asset in the cloud. This turns "which of millions of world maps am I looking at?" into "load *this* map." Localization goes global→local.
2. **The map is owner-seeded and per-location.** Each business scans and publishes only its own storefront. The "global" map assembles itself one shop at a time, exactly where someone will pay to place a sign — no global scanning, no cold-start, no hard dependency on Google/Niantic.
→ A persistent AR platform that launches **today**, shop by shop, with no map infrastructure to build first.

### 0.3 Two anchoring concepts (kept separate)
- **Identity** — *which* asset belongs here. Solved entirely by the marker (read link → fetch asset). Needs no map.
- **Pose** — *where exactly in 3D* it sits and how it stays locked as the viewer moves. Solved by marker (momentary local pose) + on-device SLAM (short-range persistence) + stored map (durable, shared, multi-user persistence). The marker is excellent at identity and good at the *initial* pose lock; durability past the marker is the map's job.

### 0.4 Flows
**Owner (publish):** create asset → choose surface (anchored / un-anchored / both) → (anchored) guided phone scan of storefront (LiDAR stronger, plain camera works but lighting-sensitive) → cloud processes scan into a re-localizable map in a stable coordinate frame (bundle-adjusted, tied to coarse GPS for indexing) → place asset in 3D + preview → publish → platform stores a lightweight anchor record + **mints a marker** to print/hang.
> Stored per anchor (small): `{ anchor pose in map frame, asset ref, map ID, coarse GPS, owner, permission scope, spatial claim }`. The heavy map is stored ONCE per location, shared by every asset+viewer there.

**Viewer (consume):** device reads marker → gets map ID + asset ID → fetches that specific map+asset → localizes camera against the map (cm-accurate; owner+viewer share one coordinate frame) → renders at stored pose, welded to storefront → as marker leaves view, on-device SLAM carries the anchor; re-acquire storefront → map re-locks.
> **Coarse GPS** isn't required for the marker path (marker already IDs the exact map) but is stored for discovery/indexing ("anchors near you", pre-fetch the right map).

**Un-anchored path:** no scan, no marker, no map. Asset shown on a turntable or placed on a surface via standard WebAR/surface-tracking. Works in any modern browser on billions of phones today; embeds anywhere a link/iframe goes.

### 0.5 Authoring tools (no-code suite) — EXPANDED (D42, the lead workstream)
> **D42 (2026-06-27)** promoted this from "build one beachhead pipeline, add on demand" to the **core product surface**: a full no-code creation studio spanning generation → animation → AR scene composition. Original beachhead-first bullets are kept (marked) for the trail; the active build now leads with deepening authoring (rationale + the deferred Phase-1 plumbing in D42).

**Asset generation (input → 3D):**
- **Product-image upload** — photo → 3D object (static) **or animated 3D** (rigged). *(LIVE: `/generate_static` textured GLB; **`/generate` rigged path now productized (D42, 2026-06-27)** — a Static/Animated toggle + motion-preset picker in the dashboard produces a **high-fidelity 1024² UV-textured**, rigged GLB with a baked motion that auto-plays in `<model-viewer>` and survives the one-track USDZ bake. **NOW BACKED BY TRELLIS.2 (D44, 2026-06-28):** the muddy gsplat-bake is REPLACED — generation runs through [generation/server_t2.py](generation/server_t2.py) (TRELLIS.2-4B native-PBR, conda `trellis2`, :8077). Static = textured PBR GLB; animated = TRELLIS.2 mesh → UniRig → rig-transferred onto the textured mesh. Game-ready PBR, verified in the product viewer. Commercial-clean (u2net bg-cut instead of gated RMBG-2.0; "Built with DINOv3" attribution). )*
- **Video upload → 3D object or 3D animation** *(NEW, D42)* — reconstruct an animated asset, or extract motion from the video to drive a rig (see AI-assist). Research-grade for arbitrary subjects; humanoid/simple-rig first (see [[animax-reimplementation-findings]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]]).
- **2D canvas / drawing** — flat sign/graphic → 3D-presented asset. *(beachhead bullet, kept)*

**Animation (no-code):**
- **Animation editor** — keyframe/timeline + interaction triggers, no JS; built on the studio's already-working in-browser GLB skinning. *(D46: keyframe STUDIO deferred to post-MVP; MVP ships **presets + custom-upload** instead — auto-rig→motion-library + transform anims, plus user-uploaded rigged GLB/FBX.)*
- **Drag-and-drop motion library** — reusable motion clips retargeted onto an asset's rig (lowest-risk, high-value lever).
- **AI-assisted motion** — (a) **replicate movement from a video** (monocular mocap → retarget onto the rig); (b) **describe the scene/motion in text**, AI proposes keyframes. An AI helper threaded through the studio.
- **Templates** — per-use-case starting points (signage, menu items, mascots, product turntables).

**AR scene / page editor** *(NEW, D42)* — a page where the owner composes **what the viewer sees in AR**: placement/layout of one or more assets plus **backgrounds / themes** for use cases like **restaurant menus** (themed menu boards, specialized backdrops). The published-experience composer — distinct from per-asset authoring; it produces the scene the un-anchored/anchored viewer renders.

**Splatting (made easy) — re-prioritized (D42):** static splats for hero/photoreal assets, kept easy to use; **animated splats stay the hard/fragile tier (D34)** — finish the D33/SPIKE animated-splat POC (GPU/browser validation) before exposing it. Mesh-first runtime still governs (D34). *(D46: the "Photoreal" lane = self-hosted **TripoSplat (MIT)**, single-image feed-forward — neither Meshy nor Tripo sells splatting via API (D45), so GS is self-host regardless; mesh "Standard" lane = TRELLIS.2 default.)*

- **Custom marker design** — style your QR/link shape, or use a **branded image marker** (logo/sign registered as the trackable target — prettier + doubles as branding).
- **Quality tiers** — every asset ships with detail levels so weak devices keep frame rate.
> Rendering guidance baked into the tools (carries D34): **mesh-first**, static splats only as hero elements, and (anchored) design that respects depth/occlusion.

### 0.6 Architecture components
- **Authoring web app** — no-code editor + asset manager.
- **Asset store** — versioned assets w/ quality tiers (glTF/mesh, optional static splat, animations, interactions).
- **Map service** — ingests owner scans → re-localizable per-location maps; indexed by coarse GPS + marker ID.
- **Anchor registry** — lightweight records (pose, asset ref, map ID, GPS, **owner, permission scope, spatial claim**).
- **Marker service** — mints/styles markers (QR or image targets); resolves marker → {map ID, asset ID}.
- **Viewer runtime** — on glasses/phone: read marker, fetch map+asset, localize, render; handle SLAM persistence + device-specific projection.
- **Delivery/CDN** — compression + streaming of assets and maps.

**Build vs rent localization:** MVP — **rent** a map service to ship fast (**Immersal** = closest fit: REST + owner-seeded mapping + private deploy; or **ARCore Geospatial API**, free but Street-View-coverage-only + Android-only), *or* run the **marker-pointer + per-location map** path. **BUILD the owner-seeded map (COLMAP + hloc) as the long-term moat** — landmine (per D39): hloc's default SuperPoint/SuperGlue weights are **non-commercial → swap for LightGlue/DISK/R2D2 before ship** (a §4a-class trap). Azure Spatial Anchors is **retired (Nov 2024)** — don't design on it.
> **Engine — CORRECTED (D38, supersedes the earlier "open-sourced 8th Wall engine" claim):** the 8th Wall **SLAM engine was NOT open-sourced.** Only a scene-framework + Face/Image/Sky *glue* was released MIT (`github.com/8thwall/8thwall`); the actual SLAM/image-target binary (`github.com/8thwall/engine`) ships under a **restrictive, revocable "XR Engine License"** (5-day revocation, no decompile) whose **anti-compete clause explicitly targets products "whose value derives substantially from the Software" / "substantially similar or competitive" — i.e. a no-code AR-builder SaaS exactly like ours.** → **Do NOT put the 8th Wall binary at the core.** Replacement stack: un-anchored = `<model-viewer>` (Apache-2.0) + **Scene Viewer (Android) / AR Quick Look + a pre-baked USDZ (iOS — which has NO WebXR at all)**; anchored web-MVP in-browser SLAM = **Blippar or Zappar** (MindAR/AR.js as free lower-quality marker fallback); native ARKit/ARCore = the phase-two premium tier (LiDAR occlusion + durable persistence) and the glasses on-ramp. **8th Wall's VPS/Maps were NOT open-sourced either** — so owner-seeded per-location maps remain the defensible piece *we* build (moat thesis CONFIRMED, even stronger than §0.9 stated). Verified hard constraint: vanilla WebXR cannot localize against a custom cloud map on any browser, and iOS has no WebXR → the anchored surface forces WASM-SLAM or native.

**Cross-device rendering (carries §2a/D34):** don't render to a display size — describe assets in **world units (meters)** and let each device's **OpenXR/WebXR** runtime handle FOV/resolution/lens/IPD. Our job = design/budget discipline: (1) **min-FOV-safe layout** (keep key content in a central angular safe zone for narrow-FOV glasses), (2) **LOD/quality tiers** (weak HW picks cheaper tier; never drop a frame — a dropped AR frame reads as nausea; static-first, splats only where budget), (3) **additive-display design** (see-through glasses can't render black → favor bright, saturated, high-contrast assets).

### 0.7 The honest hard problem — relocalization robustness *(primary technical risk)*
Owner scans at noon in summer; passerby arrives at dusk in winter with a truck out front. A casual one-pass scan often won't re-localize. Mitigations: **guided multi-condition capture**, robust server-side map processing, **ongoing re-capture** (every marker scan is a fresh ground-truthed mapping sample that improves the map), graceful fallback to marker-only local pose when the map can't lock. Bounded engineering, not a planetary data problem — but it IS *the* technical risk to invest in.

### 0.8 Occlusion + spatial governance (build into the data model from day one)
- **Occlusion/depth** — the map must carry enough 3D geometry so assets are hidden by real walls (a sign floating *through* its wall breaks the illusion).
- **Spatial rights** — anchor records carry **owner + permission scope + a claim on a region of real space**, decided at registration, to stop competitors anchoring over a shop and AR spam at popular corners.
- **Moderation** — we're responsible for content placed onto the real world (often property the owner doesn't control) → review/permission model from day one.
- **Privacy** — owner scans + viewer cameras capture public space → process on-device, discard raw frames where possible, respect regional biometric/privacy law.

### 0.9 Go-to-market (the core strategic bet = sequencing)
1. **Ship un-anchored "view in 3D" + authoring tools FIRST.** Monetizable immediately, works on every phone/browser, proven e-commerce demand ("view in your room" lifts conversion), zero dependency on glasses or maps. Funds the business + builds the asset/creator library.
2. **Capture the 8th Wall migration.** Niantic retired hosted 8th Wall (Feb 2026); thousands of brands need a no-code home *now*. Be that home; out-execute fast-followers (ARLOOPA, HOVARLAY).
3. **Add the anchored layer as an UPSELL** to existing un-anchored customers ("you already made this sign for your site — now anchor it outside your real shop"), launched **marker-first** in dense commercial districts.
4. **Stay glasses-architected** throughout: phone is the bridge surface that funds survival; glasses are the endgame where ambient anchored AR becomes a habit, not a one-off.

**Beachhead:** one dense commercial district + a clear paying use case — storefront signage / promotions / wayfinding for local businesses, plus e-commerce product viewers for the un-anchored surface. A shop can join in minutes with a printer.
**Pricing:** un-anchored = per-seat / per-asset SaaS (proven willingness to pay); anchored = subscription per active location + creation/marker fees; premium tiers for splat capture + richer animation.
**Competitive position:** the authoring/un-anchored layer is crowded and partly free — it's the on-ramp, NOT the moat. Differentiation = **(a) capturing the 8th Wall migration with the best no-code UX** + **(b) owning the persistent, marker-indexed, owner-seeded geospatial anchoring layer** — the exact capability the market keeps proprietary and the incumbent walked away from serving brands with.

### 0.10 MVP (v1)
**In scope:** no-code authoring with **1–2 pipelines** (2D canvas + product-image = cheapest, highest-demand) · **un-anchored "view in 3D"** publishing (web embed + shareable link + print QR) · **anchored** publishing via marker-pointer + owner-seeded per-location map, viewable on **phone WebAR** first (glasses-ready architecture, phone is the day-one viewer) · **guided capture flow** w/ quality checks · **anchor registry** with owner/permission/spatial-claim fields · **cross-device output** in world units with ≥2 quality tiers.
**Out of scope (phase two):** splat capture pipeline (premium, later) · full glasses viewer app (architecture-ready, not the launch surface) · discovery / "anchors near me" browsing · rich multi-user shared experiences.
**v1 success test:** a local business can, unaided, create an asset, publish it as a web "view in 3D" widget *and* anchor it outside their shop with a printed marker, and a passerby's phone reliably shows it welded to the storefront across normal lighting conditions.

### 0.11 Key risks
- **Relocalization robustness** *(primary technical)* — must re-localize across lighting/season/occlusion/device. Mitigate: guided capture, ongoing re-capture, marker-only fallback.
- **Glasses timing** *(primary strategic)* — ambient-AR endgame depends on glasses at scale; mitigated by the phone bridge funding the wait.
- **Stickiness** — AR has been campaign-deep, not habit-deep; bet is anchored + glasses makes it ambient/recurring (unproven until glasses exist at scale).
- **Crowded authoring layer** — differentiation must come from the anchoring moat + migration capture + execution, not the authoring tools alone.
- **Spatial rights / moderation / privacy** — governance built into the data model from day one.

> *Caveat (mid-2026): AR platform pricing, 8th Wall open-source licensing terms, and geospatial API capabilities are moving fast — verify current terms + competitor feature sets before committing architecture.*
