- **D22 — Benchmark FIRST RESULTS: core assumption validated.** iPhone 14 = ~200k splats stereo @ locked 60fps @ glasses res (2400×1200), thermally stable → one photoreal object (D21 range) runs realtime on phone-class HW. Laptop AMD iGPU ~350k @ glasses 60fps (beats phone). ≤200k is count-bound not fill-bound. Caveats: benchmark optimistic (no per-frame sort → real budget lower); 60Hz cap hides true edge (test 250k/300k); validate later with real renderer. (§9a)
- **D21 — Framerate = two tiers (45 rich / 60 motion); per-object counts are modest.** Stable capped framerate beats fluctuating. 45fps+max-splats (static heroes, reprojection-dependent) = stretch tier; 60fps = safe default until warp engine proven. Single AR object looks high-res at ~100–300k splats (not millions — that's scene-scale); budget = total on-screen splats. Splat size: hold fixed for count sweep (correct), do ONE size-sensitivity pass at budget count to bound fill-rate vs count-bound. (§2)
- **D19 — Hand tracking processed on PHONE, not glasses.** Two kinds of real-time: head reprojection = hard (<10ms, local/glasses); hand interaction = soft (~50ms, phone round-trip fits). Hand CV runs on phone w/ SLAM; glasses stay minimal. Budgets layer (phone = object world-pos, glasses reprojection = head-lock → no swim). Failure: bad link → object trails hand; mitigate fast link + optional on-glasses prediction. (§6b)
- **D18 — Input DECIDED: dual-mode = silent speech (stealth) + full hand motion (power).** Silent speech = discreet all-day command grammar; hand motion = spatial direct-manipulation for private use, covers objects AND general HUD. Complementary by context. RISK: silent-speech IN is least-proven tech → mitigate by prototyping stealth mode with ordinary VOICE (identical grammar, swap to EMG at HW phase); optional temple-touch backstop. Mode-switching = open sub-decision. (§6b)
- **D17 — Input/interaction was a gap; now spec'd (§6b).** Camera hand-gestures feasible but fight stealth as PRIMARY nav (conspicuous + gorilla-arm + power). Split: HUD nav = DISCREET vs hand-gestures for 3D OBJECT manipulation. *(Primary modality resolved in D18.)*
- **D16 — Architecture is CHIP-AGNOSTIC (not locked to Snapdragon).** Glasses never render (phone does) → only need display+warp+sensors. Options cheapest→turnkey: FPGA/warp-ASIC (best fit) → general ARM SoC (MediaTek/Rockchip/NXP) → dumb USB-C display (no SoC) → Snapdragon AR2 (turnkey, pricey, NDA). Phone side also any-chip (iPhone prototype, any phone production). Silicon = production-phase decision, irrelevant to current phone software. (§7)
- **D15 — Glasses-side compute scoped = split/distributed AR (= Snapdragon AR2 philosophy).** Glasses do only stream-receive + display-drive + reprojection (the "one hard job"); phone does heavy render. Target = thin-AR-co-processor tier, but it's reference-design/ODM/NDA = a months-long HW program → LAST phase. Prototype phone-only now; optional cheap feel-prototype = drive off-the-shelf Xreal/Rokid USB-C display (~$300–500) from phone. Don't spend on the glasses chip yet. (§7)
- **D14 — Software-first committed + cost claim corrected.** Path: software → iPhone prototype → hardware LAST. Phone = prototype display AND real offload compute (not throwaway). Snap's win = integration/miniaturization (single integrated lens, untethered via dual SoCs), not new optics. CORRECTION to D13: $2,200 is mostly the onboard dual SoCs, not the display; phone-offload deletes that compute → our target is the ~$800 display-glasses class, not $2,200. Derived §2a software requirements from hardware constraints. (§1, §2a, §8b)
- **D13 — Snap Specs ($2,200) = validation, not kill shot; compete on SOFTWARE not hardware.** Their "advanced display" is waveguide + electrochromic = the D12 contrast recipe (no occlusion miracle). Local rendering → 4h battery (our phone-offload = legit differentiator). ~~Adopting their display = $2,200 me-too~~ *(cost claim superseded by D14)*. Moat = agent + asset library. Strategy A (preferred): be the platform-agnostic software/content layer; Strategy B: deliberately-different stealth/agent-first/longer-battery device. (§8b)
- **D12 — Solid-looking objects via contrast, not occlusion.** True compact per-pixel occlusion is unsolved frontier optics (defocus + relay-optics bulk = why segmented dimming is bulky). Compact path = contrast-based solidity: dynamic global electrochromic dimming + high-brightness microLED/LBS + rendering tricks (shadows/opacity). Solid indoors, weaker vs bright backgrounds. Dimming mildly fights stealth → use dynamic dimming. True occlusion = research to monitor, not a dependency. (§7)
- **D11 — Environment manipulation is display-incompatible with stealth.** "Recolor walls / hide bed / replace real objects" = Diminished/Mediated Reality, needs VIDEO PASSTHROUGH (per-pixel editable). Stealth HUD is optical see-through = ADDITIVE-ONLY (adds light, can't subtract/remove/darken). So the stealth track is additive-only (add virtual objects ✅, remove/repaint real ones ❌); full redecoration = separate passthrough product (v-future fork). (§7)
- **D10 — Benchmark slice spec'd.** Stack = WEB / WebGL2 / Three.js (mkkellogg renderer), not native — one build everywhere, conservative perf floor. Scope = static cloud + rigid-body only (rigid object = one transform matrix; skeletal skinning & full AR deferred). Devices: iPhone 14 (mid) + integrated-GPU laptop (low anchor, likely weaker than the phone). Measure sustained (5min) fps vs splat-count sweep, mono then stereo → per-tier budget table. (§9a)
- **D34 — RENDER-COST REALITY CHECK + why practical AR glasses don't exist (strategic, 2026-06-25).** Stepped back to pressure-test the splat premise. (1) **Traditional rigged textured meshes are an order of magnitude CHEAPER to render on mobile than splats — not close.** Mesh = rasterize triangles + PBR, z-buffer occlusion FREE, GPU skinning ~free, compact mipmapped textures, 30yr HW maturity. Splat = per-frame depth SORT (O(n log n)) + heavy overdraw (alpha blend) + occlusion NOT free (needs the sort) + bigger memory. **Our rigged-mesh-splat hybrid is the MOST expensive option of all** (mesh skin cost + splat sort + per-splat skin + covariance rotation + re-sort every frame). Splats win on exactly ONE axis: fidelity/photoreal-capture/view-dependent appearance/fuzzy materials (hair/fur/skin) with ZERO material authoring — NOT on render cost. → confirms [[project-goal-4dgs]] "mesh path over splats." **Implication: meshes = default real-time render path; splats = a per-object HERO/luxury for photoreal capture, never the baseline.** (2) **Why no practical daily-wearable phone-offload AR glasses exist: rendering was NEVER the bottleneck.** The wall is (a) OPTICS — bright wide-FOV full-color into a thin eyeglass is unsolved; diffractive waveguides throw away >95–99% of light (hot/power-hungry microdisplays), ~30–50° FOV, rainbow/uniformity artifacts; (b) OCCLUSION — optical see-through is additive, can't subtract light → ghosts not solids (§2a/D12); (c) REPROJECTION POWER — you CANNOT offload everything; head-lock needs <20ms motion-to-photon so the glasses MUST do onboard tracking+timewarp = a co-processor drawing watts on your face, fighting the thin form factor (D15/D19); (d) power/heat/social. **Market has already bifurcated along this exact line:** practical phone-offload thin glasses EXIST (Xreal/Rokid/Viture) but DROPPED real AR — they show a floating flat video screen, birdbath optics, weak world-lock, no occlusion. HUD glasses (Even Realities, Ray-Ban Meta) skip spatial rendering entirely. Real spatial AR (HoloLens/Magic Leap/Quest passthrough) stays bulky/hot. Best evidence: **Meta Orion (2024)** = exactly the offload-to-wireless-puck thin-AR-glasses idea, shipped as a PROTOTYPE not product — Meta cited SiC-waveguide cost (~$10k/unit), yield, ~70° FOV = OPTICS+COST, not rendering compute. **Strategic conclusion: cheaper rendering does NOT unlock the product (the wall is a hardware-era optics/power problem), so the splat track is NOT on the critical path. This validates the agent/HUD Track-A-first, hardware-last ordering (D14/§1). Lead with meshes for any real-time render; keep splats as a capture/fidelity hero-feature; don't let either block agent-first.** (§1, §2a, §3, §4a; builds on D12/D14/D15/D19, [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]])
- **D33 — ANIMATED-BEAUTIFUL-SPLATS re-opened with a concrete path (deep research, 2026-06-24; partially reverses D31's "deferred").** D31 framed beautiful animated splats as "research-grade, genuinely hard." A fan-out deep-research pass (76 claims adversarially verified, 69 high-confidence) found it's **less hard than framed — we already built the hard 80%.** Key reframes:
  - **The "dots" are a RENDERER gap, not a skinning gap.** `bind_splat.py` (D29) + studio's GPU-skin shader is *already* the 2025–26 SOTA architecture ("per-splat LBS bound to a skinned mesh"). Two specific, fixable gaps remain: (1) studio draws `THREE.Points` (round dots) instead of anisotropic ellipsoids — purely the renderer; (2) the skin shader transforms splat **position only**, not the Gaussian's **rotation/covariance** → splats would smear under articulation even with a real rasterizer.
  - **The LBS rotation bug is named in the literature.** "On the Skinning of Gaussian Avatars" (arXiv 2509.11411): naive LBS is invalid for a Gaussian's non-linear rotation. Fix tiers: (a) apply blended transform's rotation to the splat `R_o = T·R_d` (3DGS-Avatar, CVPR 2024, simplest/proven); (b) weighted **quaternion-averaging** of bone rotations + rotate SH basis (2509.11411, most correct, "patch the LBS step, use any rasterizer"); (c) +pose-dependent corrective MLP for wrinkles (HuGS/SqueezeMe, optional, needs training). If our TRELLIS splats use SH order>0, must rotate SH coeffs with the bone too or shading looks "stuck."
  - **Decisive open-source hit: Gaussian-VRM** (arXiv 2510.13978, SUI 2025, github.com/naruya/gaussian-vrm) — three.js skinned-splat avatars **built directly on top of mkkellogg/GaussianSplats3D** (the renderer we already use in splat.html) + three-vrm. **MIT** (source; sample assets research-only — doesn't touch our own generated assets). Splats become standard `THREE.Object3D`s → kills the "2× three.js instances" conflict (D31). Key trick: *sort on canonical positions, render on skinned positions* (skips per-frame re-sort, the expensive part). Caveat: the paper has NO formal eval section — its FPS numbers (iPhone 40–50, Quest3 3-avatars@72) are author claims, not benchmarks (the only thing the adversarial verifier refuted). Treat method as sound, numbers as "validate ourselves."
  - **Renderer = a LAYER decision, not a product pick.** 3 layers: (1) renderer/engine, (2) skinning method, (3) rig format. Spark, mkkellogg, Visionary, UniMGS's rasterizer are all Layer 1; gaussian-vrm is Layer-2 glue (bundling mkkellogg); UniMGS is Layers 1+2 fused. Pick ONE renderer + ONE skinning recipe.
    - **Spark** (World Labs, github.com/sparkjsdev/spark, **MIT**) = the strategic Layer-1 bet: an *engine* (not a model/generator), `SplatMesh extends THREE.Object3D`, programmable per-splat GPU "dyno" modifiers, optional `SplatSkinning` with **dual-quaternion** skeletal anim (structurally avoids the LBS-rotation bug), + raycasting/lighting/particles/painter/reveal/transitions/env-maps. Bigger rewrite; write the rig→splat glue ourselves (or use SplatSkinning). "Spark + VRM" = re-implement gaussian-vrm's binding on top of Spark — but we don't even need VRM (our GLB rig + `bind_splat.py` weights already do it).
    - **Visionary** (arXiv 2512.08478, **Apache-2.0**) = WebGPU+ONNX, SMPL-X FK+LBS in ONNX, claims ~135× SparkJS at 6M splats — future bet, narrower device support, heavier pipeline.
    - **UniMGS** (AAAI 2026, arXiv 2601.19233) = NOT humanoid-specific (corrected a user assumption); its edge is **single-pass mesh+splat co-rasterization with correct occlusion/transparency** = our exact AR compositing need. Research code, not a web renderer → a SPIKE only if mesh+splat compositing visibly breaks. For humanoids specifically the avatar papers (3DGS-Avatar/SqueezeMe/SV-GS) beat it.
  - **Licensing (extends §4a/D20):** clean = gaussian-vrm (MIT), Spark (MIT), Visionary (Apache-2.0), MaGS (CC BY 4.0). ☠️ non-commercial (Inria-rasterizer-derived, never ship the academic code): SuGaR, GaMeS, D-MiSo; ⚠️ mixed: 3DGS-Avatar (own files MIT, rest Inria) — use as math reference only. **Our renderer touches none of this** — our splats are TRELLIS, our skinning is our own shader, our candidate renderers are all permissive.
  - **Decisions taken (2026-06-24):** subject = **both/mixed** → generic per-splat LBS on our own GLB rig is the tool; humanoid priors stay optional. Renderer = **decide after spikes.** Plan = **gaussian-vrm proof-of-concept first** (cheapest, ~1–2 days, de-risks the concept on our existing bound PLY) → **Spark spike** (the likely ship target, ~3–5 days) → **UniMGS only if compositing breaks.** Don't run all three in parallel; each result decides whether the next is needed. (§3, §4a, supersedes D31's "deferred" for the rendering question; builds on D29)
  - **Spike step 1 DONE (2026-06-24) — inspected gaussian-vrm source (MIT) vs our pipeline (`generation/SPIKE_animated_splat.md`).** Findings: (a) gaussian-vrm's whole trick = mkkellogg `SplatMesh` + a vertex-shader patch (`gsCustomizeMaterial`) that skins each splat's **center + covariance** (`rotatedVrk = transpose(R)*Vrk*R`, R from `skinMatrix*inverse(skinMatrix0)`) — exactly our Gap-2 fix. (b) **Patch is compatible with mkkellogg 0.4.7, the version splat.html already pins** (all shader anchors + `splatDataTextures`/`updateDataTexturesFromBaseData`/`dynamicScene` present) → NO renderer migration. (c) SH concern moot — our skinned PLY is SH order 0 (`f_dc` only). (d) gaussian-vrm is VRM/humanoid-coupled (three-vrm, `J_Bip_*`, hardcoded bone idxs, `.gvrm` zip, binds splats to mesh VERTICES reading mesh skin-weights) — we DON'T need that path: `bind_splat.py` already bakes per-splat j0..j3/w0..w3, so we skin each splat directly (simpler, works for arbitrary rigs). We lift only the MIT cov-rotation snippet + rest-pose boneTexture0 capture. (e) **BUG found:** `bind_splat.py:113-131` transforms only x,y,z into mesh frame but copies `rot_0..3`/`scale_0..2` UNCHANGED — invisible for dots, but a real anisotropic renderer would mis-orient every ellipsoid by the registration rotation R; must rotate quats by R + scale by s before step-2 PoC. Decided NOT to run gaussian-vrm's own VRM demo (humanoid path we won't use; needs gated sample assets).
  - **Spike step 2 IN PROGRESS (2026-06-24): bind fix DONE+verified, PoC BUILT, awaiting browser validation** (`generation/SPIKE_animated_splat.md`). (a) **`bind_splat.py` fixed** to bake the registration rotation+scale into each splat's covariance (was position-only → the Gap-2 latent bug); numerically verified (clean similarity, per-splat cov scaled by exactly the registration factor 1.985 with zero variance, anisotropy preserved). (b) **`split_by_bone.py`** (new) splits the skinned PLY into one plain-3DGS PLY per dominant bone → 25 scenes for gen_3594c97a. (c) **`poc_splat_anim.html`** (new): mkkellogg DropInViewer (real ellipsoids) with per-bone-group RIGID skinning `D_b = bindMatrixInverse·boneMatrices[b]·bindMatrix` (the exact transform studio's working dot-shader uses → correct-by-construction; seams at joints = known rigid limit, removed later by the per-splat covariance-skinning shader). Served at **/out/poc_splat_anim.html** (no TRELLIS restart) + **/poc** route added. **NEXT: user validates in browser (GPU)** — ellipsoids-not-dots, orientation vs mesh-ref (confirms bind quaternion convention), animation tracks skeleton. Then step-2b = per-splat covariance shader for smooth (seamless) skinning (lift gaussian-vrm's MIT `rotatedVrk` snippet).
  - **Spike step 2 VALIDATED in browser (2026-06-24).** Confirmed: (1) renderer now draws REAL anisotropic splats (mkkellogg), not dots — the headline "low-res dots" problem is solved at the renderer level; (2) the splat ALIGNS with / sits on the mesh ref → binding + frame conventions + the bind_splat.py orientation fix are all correct (the riskiest part); (3) it animates with the skeleton. Two separate issues surfaced, NEITHER about the renderer: (a) **the splat ASSET (gen_3594c97a, 4-view TRELLIS) is low quality** — blur/noise/hallucinations baked in at generation time → a GENERATION-quality workstream, orthogonal to this spike; (b) **rigid per-bone skinning breaks at joints** (legs split, parts move independently) — the known limitation, fixed by step-2b per-splat smooth skinning. Also softened the PoC sway (was ~30°/joint compounding → gentle slider, default 0.06 rad) since the aggressive default exaggerated the joint seams. CONCLUSION: the gaussian-vrm-style approach is PROVEN for our pipeline; renderer decision still "decide after Spark spike" but mkkellogg-path is validated end-to-end. NEXT: step-2b (smooth skinning) to remove joint breaking; separately, improve generation quality (more/better views, cleanup) — pick a better asset to demo.
  - **Spike step 2b BUILT (2026-06-24): smooth per-splat skinning + walk, on the dwarf (`generation/poc_splat_smooth.html`, /poc-smooth).** User picked the dwarf (`gen_3a259c3d`, 28-bone clean biped) as the cleaner asset — confirmed it renders + aligns. Re-bound with fixed bind_splat (note: dwarf registration is a REFLECTION, det −7.6 — the covariance-reextraction method handled it). Skeleton analyzed from geometry (UniRig bones unnamed): legs thigh=20/24 shin=21/25, arms upper=7/14, spine 1-4, head 5. Smooth viewer: loads the FULL skinned PLY as ONE mkkellogg scene; uploads per-splat j/w as RGBA-float textures (indexed by splatIndex = PLY order); patches the SplatMaterial vertex shader (`onBeforeCompile`, anchors verified in 0.4.x vendored module) to skin each splat by its 4 weights — center `splatCenter = D·rest` and covariance `Vrk -> R·Vrk·Rᵀ`, `D = bindInverse·Σ(w·boneMatrix)·bindMatrix` (same geometry-local convention as the proven rigid PoC). Walk cycle driven from geometry-derived per-bone swing axes (world-lateral X in each bone's rest frame); UI sliders for speed/leg/knee/arm + "flip knee". **NEEDS BROWSER VALIDATION (user):** /out/poc_splat_smooth.html — success = limbs bend SMOOTHLY (no joint gaps) under walk. Known iteration risks: splatIndex==PLY order assumption (else weights scrambled), covariance-rotation convention (transpose/sign), GLSL scope of `splatSkinRot` across the two shader anchors, knee bend direction (flip button).

- **D37 — Market + GTM research report produced ([research/market-and-gtm.md](research/market-and-gtm.md), 2026-06-25).** Deep web-sourced research on the D35 platform (landscape, failures, e-commerce ROI, GTM/pricing, market size/timing). Key findings validating/refining D35: (1) **Anchored AR is the moat AND the market is withdrawing from it** — Niantic retired hosted 8th Wall (access ended Feb 28 2026) and did NOT open-source VPS/Maps/Hand-Tracking, redirecting its VPS to defense/robotics; Adobe killed Aero (Dec 2025); Meta killed Spark AR (Jan 2025, 600k creators). Confirms hosted un-anchored WebAR is a thin standalone business → the owner-seeded per-location anchoring layer is the only candidate moat (§0.9 reaffirmed). (2) **E-commerce 3D/AR ROI is partly real but vendor-inflated** — the famous "94% conversion lift" (Shopify), "11x" (Houzz), "65%" (Rebecca Minkoff) are selection-biased vendor marketing, NOT causal lift; the credible, mechanism-backed effect is **~20–40% return reduction for high-uncertainty categories** (furniture/home/eyewear/footwear/cosmetics) + a modest single-to-low-double-digit conversion lift. Build the un-anchored business case on returns + a conservative lift, demand a real A/B test. (3) **The "free anchored, convert on analytics" hypothesis is mis-sequenced** — storefront/awareness QR scan rates are low single digits, so a scan-analytics dashboard will often show a number too small to justify a charge (kills the upsell). **Convert anchored on CAPABILITY gates** (branded image-marker, persistent per-location map, multi-location, watermark removal), analytics as support only. (4) **8th Wall migration wedge is real but crowded + time-boxed** (≥8 vendors already running migration campaigns; refugees skew enterprise) → treat as a launch accelerant/SEO+credibility play, not the franchise. (5) **Timing: phone-now is right, glasses-later slips to ~2028–2032 for world-anchored AR** — display-LESS AI glasses (Ray-Ban Meta ~9M sold) can't render anchored AR; the endgame needs display+world-tracking glasses (Orion prototype-only, Snap Specs $2,195 niche). Underwrite on phone-only economics. (6) **Bottoms-up SAM ≈ $0.5–1.5B/yr ARR** (online-store + local-business beachhead), 2–3 orders of magnitude below top-down "$2–3T AR" hype; ~$10–50M obtainable ARR at 1–5% penetration over 5 yrs. **Pricing rec:** un-anchored = charge day-one, card-gated trial, **unlimited views (never meter on views)**, Starter ~$19–29/Growth ~$99–149/Enterprise; anchored = free seeding tier (one location, watermark, generic marker) → ~$29–79/location/mo on a capability trigger. Refines §0.9/§0.10 GTM + pricing; no spec change yet, flagged for the user to fold pricing/sequencing into §0.9. (§0.9, §0.10; builds on D35)
- **D36 — Glasses spun out into [GLASSES.md](GLASSES.md); two projects kept in parallel (2026-06-25).** User articulated a distinct **wearer-facing product**: AI smart glasses as a **personal AR productivity / dev cockpit** — binocular AR screens/widgets (PDF/docs, IDE + agentic coding, web, AI chat, live transcribe/translate), voice commands, **phone-offload** (consistent w/ §2), **hands-free** nav. Decisions taken: **keep BOTH products** — this file stays the SSOT for the D35 B2B platform; the glasses get their own SSOT [GLASSES.md](GLASSES.md) (same directory, same maintenance rule). v1 **input = eye-tracking cursor + a discreet confirm ladder** (dwell-to-click → silent-speech "select" → temple-tap → optional sEMG wristband); **"think-to-click" BCI = research line to MONITOR, not a v1 dependency** (in-frame EEG is noisy/unproven; NextMind shelved; only Meta's sEMG-wrist ships). Hand input dropped. This **reframes the original stealth Track A (§1)** toward a less-stealthy binocular cockpit and **supersedes D18's input model for the glasses product** (D18 still stands for any stealth-agent framing). Full spec + feasibility grading + decision log (G1) in GLASSES.md. (§1, §2, §2a, §6b/D18, D34, D35; [[stealth-agent-glasses-product]])
- **D35 — PRODUCT PIVOT: Marker-Anchored AR Asset Platform (2026-06-25). New lead product, full spec in §0; continuity map in §0a.** The project reframes from "stealth agent glasses + summon-an-animated-splat-into-my-room" to a **no-code platform where any business publishes a 3D asset two ways: (1) an instant un-anchored "view in 3D" web/print widget, and (2) a real-world anchor placed via a physical MARKER that points to an owner-seeded, cloud-hosted per-location map.** Core insight = the marker carries a POINTER not a map (global localization → trivial local "load *this* map"), and the map is owner-seeded per-location (the "global" map assembles one paying shop at a time → launches today, no planetary scanning, no Google/Niantic dependency). Two surfaces are sequenced by difficulty: **un-anchored ships FIRST** (works on every phone/browser today, proven e-commerce demand, funds the business, builds the creator library) → **capture the 8th Wall migration** (Niantic retired hosted 8th Wall Feb 2026; brands need a no-code home now) → **anchored as an upsell** (marker-first, dense commercial districts) → **glasses as the architected endgame** (phone is the bridge viewer). Moat = NOT the crowded authoring layer but (a) best no-code migration capture + (b) the owner-seeded, marker-indexed geospatial anchoring layer (the piece 8th Wall did NOT open-source). Primary technical risk = **relocalization robustness** (re-localize across lighting/season/occlusion/device → guided multi-condition capture + ongoing re-capture + marker-only fallback); primary strategic risk = **glasses timing** (mitigated by the phone bridge). **What carries forward (§0a):** the working generation pipeline (D24–D29) becomes the authoring image-to-3D/animation backend; the library/dedup work (D32) becomes the asset store; **D34's mesh-first / splats-as-hero-luxury becomes the baked-in rendering guidance** (animated splats explicitly DEFERRED to premium/static-only); cross-device/additive-display/world-units discipline (§2a) carries as §0.6. **What's deferred/out of current scope:** stealth-glasses hardware, the autonomous-agent Track A, physics (§5), humanoid telepresence (§6). MVP (§0.10): no-code authoring (2D canvas + product-image) · un-anchored publish (embed/link/print QR) · anchored via marker-pointer + per-location map on phone WebAR · guided capture · anchor registry with owner/permission/spatial-claim · cross-device world-units output w/ ≥2 quality tiers. Engine basis = open-sourced 8th Wall engine + WebXR/three.js; localization = rent VPS where coverage exists OR the no-VPS marker-pointer path (the differentiator). Governance (spatial rights / moderation / privacy) built into the data model from day one. (§0, §0a; supersedes §1's lead framing; builds on D32/D34, [[stealth-agent-glasses-product]], [[asset-library-architecture]])
- **D38 — 8th Wall due-diligence: the "open-sourced engine" assumption is WRONG; corrects §0.6 ([research/8thwall-deep-dive.md](research/8thwall-deep-dive.md), 2026-06-25).** Primary-source dig (repos + LICENSE files): (a) hosted 8th Wall (editor/Studio/hosting) retired **Feb 28 2026**; already-published experiences run until **Feb 28 2027** then die; the project moved to 8thwall.org / github.com/8thwall as "community-driven" with **no Niantic maintenance commitment.** (b) **The valuable SLAM/world-tracking engine was NOT open-sourced** — it ships only as a **closed-source binary** (`github.com/8thwall/engine`) under a restrictive **"XR Engine License"** (NOT MIT): revocable on 5 days' notice, no modify/decompile, and it **prohibits products "whose value derives substantially from the Software" and forbids building "a substantially similar or competitive product"** — a no-code AR-builder SaaS (our §0 shape) is the named likely-prohibited case. The MIT repo (`github.com/8thwall/8thwall`) is only the ECS/scene framework + Face/Image/Sky glue + tooling; **SLAM is explicitly excluded.** (c) **VPS / Lightship Maps / Hand-Tracking were not released at all** → owner-seeded per-location maps remain genuinely defensible (D35 moat thesis CONFIRMED, even stronger). **Decision: do NOT build on the 8th Wall binary as the core** (revocable + anti-compete clause aimed at us); if used at all, keep it abstracted/replaceable + get written license clarification. Replacement stack folded into §0.6. Context: Niantic acquired 8th Wall Mar 2022; sold games to Scopely ($3.5B, closed May 29 2025); 8th Wall now sits in the spun-out **Niantic Spatial Inc.** **NOTE: this contradicts D39's tech-stack report, which mistakenly assumed 8th Wall SLAM is "now MIT" — D38 (read the actual LICENSE) is authoritative; trust D38 over D39 on this point.** (§0.6; corrects §0.6 + the "Engine basis = open-sourced 8th Wall engine" line in D35; builds on D35/D37)
- **D39 — Tech-stack + architecture research ([research/tech-stack-architecture.md](research/tech-stack-architecture.md), 2026-06-25).** Component-by-component architecture (no code) for both surfaces, web-sourced + cited. Key resolutions: (1) **Un-anchored = web forever** — `<model-viewer>` (Apache-2.0) → Scene Viewer on Android, **AR Quick Look + a pre-baked USDZ on iOS** (native ARKit, which sidesteps the verified **iOS-Safari-has-no-WebXR** wall). The glTF↔USDZ split is real → **bake a curated USDZ per asset at publish** (auto-conversion is lossy: one animation track). (2) **Anchored = web (WASM-SLAM) for MVP → native ARKit/ARCore as a phase-two premium tier** (LiDAR occlusion + durable persistence) and the OpenXR-glasses on-ramp. Hard constraint: **vanilla WebXR cannot localize against a custom cloud map on any browser** → anchored forces WASM-SLAM or native. (3) **Map = the build-vs-rent crux:** RENT **Immersal** (or ARCore Geospatial) to ship; **BUILD owner-seeded COLMAP+hloc as the moat** — landmine: hloc's default SuperPoint/SuperGlue weights are non-commercial → **swap LightGlue/DISK/R2D2 before ship**; Azure Spatial Anchors retired Nov 2024. (4) **Existing pipeline plugs in unchanged** — `generation/server.py` (TRELLIS-resident + UniRig + `bind_splat`, RTX 5090) becomes the authoring image-to-3D backend behind an async job queue; mesh-first (D34) is the authoring default, static splats = hero tier, animated splats deferred. (5) **Biggest technical risk = relocalization robustness** (one-pass owner scan often won't re-lock) → guided multi-condition capture + every marker scan as a fresh re-mapping sample + map-baked occluder mesh + marker-only fallback (= §0.7, reaffirmed). Report has two text architecture diagrams + a consolidated stack bill with licenses. **CAVEAT: its "8th Wall SLAM is now MIT" premise is wrong — see D38.** All of this is recorded research, **no §0 spec rewrite yet beyond the §0.6 correction** — flagged for the user to ratify the web-vs-native phasing + map build-vs-rent into §0.6/§0.10. (§0.6, §0.7, §0.10; builds on D35, corrected-by/corrects D38)
- **D40 — Phased implementation plan created ([IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md](IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md), 2026-06-25).** Companion build plan for the D35 platform, sequenced by the §0.9 GTM bet + the corrected stack (D38/D39). Six phases: **0 Foundations** (auth/store/CDN/Stripe/job-queue fronting the existing `generation/server.py` pipeline) → **1 Un-anchored "View in 3D" MVP** (the revenue wedge — product-image + 2D-canvas authoring, `<model-viewer>` with Android-WebXR/iOS-USDZ split, embed/link/print-QR, charge day-one, never meter views) → **2 8th Wall migration capture** (time-boxed acquisition into the paid un-anchored tier) → **3 Anchored MVP** (marker service + RENTED map [Immersal] behind a swappable `MapService` iface + anchor registry with owner/permission/spatial-claim + guided capture + abstracted web WASM-SLAM, NOT the 8th Wall binary; free-seed → capability-gated ~$29–79/loc/mo) → **4 Anchored moat** (own COLMAP+hloc map with LightGlue/DISK/R2D2 not NC weights + occlusion + native ARKit/ARCore = the glasses on-ramp) → **5 Glasses-ready** (deferred ~2028–2032, underwrite on phone-only economics).
