Cross-cutting: governance-in-schema-from-day-one + a licensing release-gate checklist. **iOS clarification recorded** (answers a user question): all iOS browsers run on WebKit → none support WebXR (Chrome-WebXR is Android-only) → iPhone un-anchored AR goes through native AR Quick Look/USDZ, not WebXR (verified via web search, June 2026). Assumptions = small/solo team + revenue-first; open decisions (pricing ratification, lead authoring pipeline, resourcing, Immersal-vs-ARCore) listed in the plan §11, none blocking the first sprint. (§0.6, §0.9, §0.10; builds on D35/D37/D38/D39)
- **D41 — Textured GLBs for the un-anchored product, via a commercially-clean gsplat+nvdiffrast bake (2026-06-26, BUILT+verified).** Product viewers need COLORED assets; the worker's rigging path emits geometry-only (gray) GLBs. TRELLIS's textured `to_glb` bakes a texture but **renders the gaussian via `diff_gaussian_rasterization` (Inria, NON-COMMERCIAL — the §4a/D20 "never ship" landmine)** — a hidden licensing trap in the obvious path. User chose the high-fidelity clean route over a vertex-color baker. Fix: **monkeypatch TRELLIS's `GaussianRenderer.render` to use gsplat (Apache-2.0)** (`generation/gsplat_render.py`; wxyz quats, normalized-intrinsics→pixels, black bg, SH degree-0), then nvdiffrast bakes a real 1024² UV atlas. New worker path `generation/server.py:/generate_static` + `pipeline_static` (image→TRELLIS mesh+gaussian→gsplat 100-view render→nvdiffrast bake→textured GLB, no rig); platform un-anchored creation now calls it. **Blackwell note:** the 5090 is sm_120 but the box's CUDA toolkit is 12.5 (nvcc maxes at sm_90) → build PTX `9.0+PTX` and let the 580 driver JIT to Blackwell; `CUDA_HOME=/usr/local/cuda-12.5` + `TORCH_CUDA_ARCH_LIST=9.0+PTX` baked into server.py. nvdiffrast 0.4.0 + gsplat 1.5.3 both compiled+ran on Blackwell this way. **Verified:** crate image → real wood/metal 1024² texture (not garbage) → USDZ → serves at `/v/crate`. Extends §4a clean stack: **nvdiffrast (permissive) + gsplat (Apache-2.0) are the clean texture-bake renderers; never the Inria rasterizer.** (§4a, §0.5, §0.6; builds on D40, [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D44 — TRELLIS.2 benchmarked locally on the 5090 — quality is EXCELLENT (game-ready PBR), decisively beating our gsplat-bake; recommend adopting it as the generation backend (2026-06-28).** Per the user's "prototype both" call (D43), did a full local self-host build of **TRELLIS.2-4B** (MIT, native-3D PBR) and ran the dwarf/butterfly/dragon through it. **Result: crisp, bright, correctly-wrapped PBR textures + clean geometry — essentially matching the input images** (vs our muddy/dark gsplat-bake). This is the Meshy/Tripo-class quality the user wanted, self-hosted under a clean license. **Build reality (the cost):** a multi-hour Blackwell (sm_120) slog — had to (1) use torch 2.11+cu128 + xformers 0.0.35 (the only Blackwell-working combo; torch 2.8/xformers 0.0.32 crashes attention with an uncatchable CUDA error; dodge `pypi.nvidia.com` DNS via `--extra-index-url pypi.org`), (2) build 4 custom CUDA exts (nvdiffrast/cumesh/flexgemm/o_voxel) with CUDA-12.5 `9.0+PTX`, (3) patch transformers-5.x API drift (`model.model.layer`), (4) work around TWO gated deps: DINOv3 (commercial-OK, attribution; user got access) and **briaai/RMBG-2.0 (NON-COMMERCIAL → bypassed by feeding RGBA pre-cut with clean u2net `rembg`; the pipeline skips RMBG when input has alpha).** **Latency:** ~80–145 s/asset at 512³ on the 5090 (fine for our async job queue; not interactive). **Cost:** $0/asset (own GPU). Setup lives in conda env `trellis2` + repo `/home/sov2/projects/TRELLIS.2`; bench script `generation/bench_trellis2.py`. **RECOMMENDATION (updates D43): adopt TRELLIS.2 as the geometry+texture backend** (replacing v1 TRELLIS + the gsplat-bake), keep **UniRig** for rigging + the **transfer_rig** step (skin the TRELLIS.2 textured mesh) for the animated path; production needs the RMBG→u2net swap baked in (commercial-clean) + "Built with DINOv3" attribution. **Tripo (buy) comparison still pending credits** — but TRELLIS.2 quality already clears the bar, is self-hosted, clean-license, and $0/asset, so it's the front-runner; Tripo remains the lower-ops fallback. **INTEGRATED + verified (2026-06-28):** new worker [generation/server_t2.py](generation/server_t2.py) (conda `trellis2` env) replaces the v1 server.py backend, **same platform job contract on :8077** so the platform/`gen-worker.ts` is unchanged. **Static path** (`/generate_static`): u2net bg-cut → TRELLIS.2 → 1024² PBR GLB (~6MB, base-color + metallic-roughness) → renders beautifully in the product viewer (shiny gauntlets, reflective anvil — full PBR). **Animated path** (`/generate`): TRELLIS.2 textured mesh → clean_mesh → UniRig skeleton/skin → prep_viewer (bake motion) → **transfer_rig skins the TRELLIS.2 textured mesh onto the rig** → animated PBR GLB (verified: rig_ok, 22 bones, plays in model-viewer + USDZ). Run the backend with: `PORT=8077 conda run -n trellis2 python generation/server_t2.py` (needs ~24GB VRAM; replaces v1 server.py). v1 server.py retained for the studio/animated-splat experiments. (§0.5; builds on D41/D42/D43, [[generation-texture-method]], [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D43 — Texture quality is critical; our gsplat-render→bake is the WRONG method; recommend wrapping a commercial generation API (deep-research, 2026-06-28, [research/generation-texture-rigging.md](research/generation-texture-rigging.md)).** A colourful input (a dwarf, a head) bakes out muddy/dark in our TRELLIS pipeline. Root cause CONFIRMED by research: we render TRELLIS's Gaussian splats from many views and bake that → a soft, view-averaged, shadow-contaminated single-colour texture. **The commercial tools (Meshy/Tripo/Rodin/Hunyuan3D) use a fundamentally different method: mesh-conditioned MULTI-VIEW PBR DIFFUSION** — a diffusion model conditioned on the mesh's geometry (normal/coord maps) synthesises view-consistent images (reference-attention for fidelity + multi-view attention/sync + 3D-aware RoPE for consistency), as **decomposed, delit PBR maps** (albedo/metallic/roughness, illumination-invariant), back-projected to UV + super-res + seam-inpaint. No amount of tuning our splat-bake closes that gap — it's the wrong method. **Rigging:** our **UniRig (MIT) IS already the right modern learned auto-rigger** (Skeleton-Tree-Tokenization transformer + Bone-Point Cross Attention, arbitrary categories) — keep it. **Licensing landmine:** the best OPEN PBR-texture models (Hunyuan3D-2/2.1/Paint, MaterialMVP) ship under a non-OSI **Tencent Community License** (commercial cap at 1M MAU, **void in EU/UK/South Korea**) → **do NOT ship**. The only unambiguously MIT/Apache self-hosted texture upgrade is **TRELLIS.2** (native-3D PBR, no bake) — but quality is so far only the authors' un-benchmarked claim. **Build-vs-buy:** commercial APIs give best-in-class texture+rig at ~$0.10–0.40/asset (Meshy/Tripo; Rodin $0.50–1.50+), snappy, with **commercial/resale rights on PAID tiers** (Meshy Premium = full rights no attribution; Rodin/Hyper3D all tiers; Meshy FREE = CC-BY, do not use). **RECOMMENDATION (pending user ratification): wrap a commercial API (Meshy or Tripo) behind our existing async job interface** (`submitGeneration→poll→finalize` — a contained worker-backend swap; the platform doesn't care where the GLB comes from), since generation is the authoring BACKEND not the moat (§0.5/§0.9) and this instantly hits the quality+snappiness bar; keep self-hosted TRELLIS+UniRig as a fallback/cost-lever; revisit TRELLIS.2 for a clean self-host texture upgrade after benchmarking. Pricing/ToS are blog/vendor-doc sourced (mid-2026) → verify live before committing. (§0.5, §0.9; builds on D41/D42, [[licensing-landmines]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]])
- **D42 — Direction: deepen the no-code AUTHORING/GENERATION suite as the lead workstream; the four Phase-1 plumbing gaps are recorded + deferred (2026-06-27).** Asked "what's next," the user chose to invest in the **creation experience** (the surface customers actually touch) over revenue/delivery plumbing. **Recorded + deferred (all still valid, do later):** (1) **Stripe billing + card-gated trial** — the "monetizes day one" exit criterion, currently ABSENT (plans per D37: Starter ~$19–29 / Growth ~$99–149, unlimited views, never meter); (2) **production asset delivery** — R2/CDN + Draco/meshopt/KTX2 + LOD (storage is local-disk today); (3) **analytics** — PostHog/self-host, track returns/engagement, NEVER meter views (D37); (4) **2D-canvas authoring** (the second pipeline). **New active direction = build §0.5 into a real no-code studio:** video AND image input → 3D object OR 3D animation; a no-code **animation editor** (keyframe/timeline) + **drag-and-drop motion library** + **AI-assisted motion** (replicate movement from a video via monocular mocap→retarget; or describe-the-scene/motion in text); **templates**; an **AR scene/page editor** with **backgrounds/themes** (e.g. restaurant menus) = the published-experience composer; and **splatting made easy** (static-first; finish the D33/SPIKE animated-splat POC before exposing animated splats). **What already exists to build on:** the `/generate` rigged pipeline (TRELLIS→UniRig→`bind_splat`) + [studio.html](generation/studio.html)'s working in-browser GLB skinning + the bound skinned-splat PLY — but **only `/generate_static` is wired into the platform**; the rigged/animation path lives in the standalone studio and must be productized. **Honest flags:** (a) §0.9 calls authoring "the on-ramp, NOT the moat" and the plan's principle #1/#2 is "ship the paying surface first / don't build the moat before the wedge" — deepening authoring pushes revenue plumbing later; defensible because **best-no-code-UX IS the Phase-2 8th-Wall-migration wedge** and video→animation + AI-assist is genuinely differentiated vs the crowded static-viewer field, but the revenue trade-off is held consciously; (b) **video→3D-animation and text/video→motion are research-grade** for arbitrary subjects (humanoid/simple rigs first; arbitrary creatures hard) — [[animax-reimplementation-findings]] (AnimaX animated-mesh gen has commercial-licensing constraints), [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]]; (c) D34's mesh-first runtime + "animated splats deferred/expensive" still governs — splatting-made-easy = static-splat authoring UX + finishing the POC, NOT making animated splats the baseline. Expands §0.5 + adds the AR scene/page-editor component; refines IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN Phase 1. (§0.5, §0.6, §0.9; builds on D34/D35/D37/D40/D41, [[animax-reimplementation-findings]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]])
- **D63 — CUSTOMIZATION architecture: disentangled swappable/recolorable LAYERS on a FIXED body+face base (refines D57's compositional design); one-page avatar spec written (2026-07-13).** User asked whether per-avatar library assets lock in hair/clothing/eyes, or whether those can be user-customizable on the SAME body/face. Answer: **the layered design already gives this** — keep **body shape + face identity FIXED per avatar** (the "base" = who the avatar is), and make **hair, clothing, eyes, accessories separate attachable gaussian LAYERS** on top. **Two distinct kinds of customization (different difficulty):** (1) **RECOLOR** — color is a per-gaussian attribute, so changing it is cheap math on that part's gaussians → **hair color, eye color, skin tone, clothing color = instant, on-device, unlimited**; (2) **SWAP** — attach a different **pre-made** part rigged to the same body → **hairstyle, garment, accessories = a parts library ("wardrobe"); user picks one** (generating a brand-new arbitrary part from a prompt is a separate, harder generative track, not needed for a curated library). Both rely on each part being a **labeled/separate group of gaussians**, which the layered construction gives for free (hair is its own asset, iris its own group). **Why fix the base:** body+face constant → hair/clothing **fit once**, no re-fitting; a varying body shape would force auto-refitting per garment/hairstyle (hard) — so fixing the base is the simplification that makes customization tractable. **Fits the puppet/data-packet model (D62):** the packet also carries **which-parts + what-colors** (composition), alongside motion (joint angles) + expression (ARKit coeffs) + audio. **Bonus — shrinks the dataset:** disentangling means you train **bodies+faces + a separate parts library**, NOT every avatar×outfit×hairstyle (kills the combinatorial explosion — the core reason layers beat a monolith, D57). **Honest hard bits:** clothing that **drapes/moves** with body motion (the MM2 layer), **hair as gaussians** (fine/translucent/moving), and **seams** (hairline/collar/neck) within the phone budget. **Clean-stack mapping:** body=Anny, face=LAM, clothing=MM2, motion=GEM-X/Kimodo, lip-sync=Audio2Face/LAM_Audio2Expression, expression vocab=ARKit, render=gsplat. Full one-pager: **[docs/avatar-architecture.md](docs/avatar-architecture.md)**. (§0.5, §2, §3; builds on D57/D60/D61/D62, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[asset-library-architecture]])
- **D105 — STRATEGIC PIVOT PROVEN: drop the splat for the BODY/FACE — a textured mesh renders BETTER in the browser at the same wire size, AND dropping the fit is what unblocks every premium asset licence (2026-07-24).** The user restated the product (click-to-customise avatars, LLM-driven) with three hard requirements — (1) runs in the browser, (2) MetaHuman-class skin/face/motion realism, accessories can compromise, (3) cheap to start and scale, commercially clean for **selling AND AI training** — and added the key instruction: *"the concept of splatting is introduced so we can have that realism in the browser but if we can render the textures fine in the browser then we should just do that."* **Both halves tested. Both say drop the splat.** **(1) THE TECHNICAL TEST — BUILT AND RENDERED.** New `dataset/export_skin_glb.py` packs the Anny body + the D100 SMOKEWORKS real PBR skin into a standard glTF 2.0 asset (baseColor sRGB + normal + the ORM map, whose G=roughness/B=metallic packing is already glTF's convention, so it drops in with no channel surgery; metallicFactor forced to 0 per D41). New `dataset/viewer/skintest.html` (route `/skintest`) renders it in three.js r160 with PMREM/RoomEnvironment IBL + ACES tone mapping. **Result: 27,420 triangles, 2048² textures, 10.0 MB on the wire, 1.2 s load — and it is visibly, decisively sharper than the best splat we have ever produced at the SAME 10 MB** (`motion_out/d105_splat_vs_mesh.png`: the mesh resolves skin pores, brow hair, lip and ear detail; the D104 splat is a soft mannequin). This is consistent with D98/D102 — the splat's blur was never a fit problem, and a mesh + real texture simply sidesteps it. **Two real bugs found and fixed on the way:** trimesh omits the glTF NORMAL accessor unless vertex normals are already cached, which rendered the whole body BLACK in three.js (no normals → no shading); and baking D81's procedural iris ramp to VERTEX COLOURS smears the pupil across the whole eye because each Anny eyeball is only ~80 verts — replaced with a rasterised iris texture + gaze-aligned planar UVs. **(2) THE LICENCE TEST — dropping the fit changes the answer everywhere.** Every premium digital-human vendor bars **AI training**, not AI USE. Verbatim, Epic: *"You can use MetaHuman characters and animation in workflows that incorporate artificial intelligence technology. However, you may not use MetaHuman characters or animation curves to build or enhance any database or train or test artificial intelligence, machine learning, deep learning, neural networks, or similar technologies... This includes the use of rendered output from MetaHuman digital characters and animation curves, if created to replicate the functionality of MetaHuman."* **Our gaussian fit + corrective MLP is exactly the prohibited act** (optimise on rendered output → produce a digital human). **An LLM directing a textured mesh at runtime is exactly the permitted act** (an AI *workflow*). Same flip applies to Reallusion (bars "AI training, machine learning, or synthetic data generation" — but explicitly permits games/XR/"interactive online services"; and uniquely sells an **Enterprise tier that GRANTS AI-training rights**, the only off-the-shelf clean-for-training licence found so far), Daz (bars feeding Content to generative AI; separately requires an **Interactive License** wherever the mesh "can be extracted", which a browser app always can), and 3DScanStore (bars "digital humans created using AI training data derived from" their scans — a plain texture use under their Business Commercial Single Project Licence, ~£59 + £961, is a different act). **Corrects D76/D104 once more:** MetaHuman's blocker is neither redistribution (removed in Epic's June-2025 relicence) nor the AI clause *per se* — it is **the gaussian fit specifically**. Remaining MetaHuman frictions are practical, not legal: `.mhpkg` needs an Epic account, and its textures use MetaHuman's own UV layout (needs a UV-transfer bake). **(3) SOURCE VERDICTS** (all eight the user linked): **Reallusion Character Creator = the strongest fit** (real-time game-grade humans, click-to-customise morphs, GLB/FBX export, explicit games/XR/interactive-online-services grant, Enterprise tier for AI training); **NVIDIA Audio2Face-3D = adopt for the face** (MIT SDK + NVIDIA Open Model weights + **Apache** training framework, ONNX/NIM, so audio→ARKit-blendshape lip-sync is clean and self-hostable — this is the D62 face layer, solved); **Kimodo/SOMA stays the body-motion source** (D67/D70); **3DScanStore albedo pack = usable for TEXTURE-only use** at ~£1,020 for the commercial tier, blocked only if we fit gaussians to it; **Daz = usable but needs the per-figure Interactive License** for browser delivery; **Convai = the AI/runtime LAYER, avatar-agnostic** — a competitor to our director, not an asset source, and buying it would give away the moat; **Lychee Studio = generic text→3D**, unverified asset licence, not a human-specialist; **MetaHuman = legally fine for a mesh product, blocked for the splat, and gated behind Epic tooling**. **(4) SIDE WIN: the "no headless browser on this box" gap (open since D98) is CLOSED** — Playwright + Chromium installed and driving `/skintest` headless with SwiftShader, so browser work is now verifiable here (fps readings under SwiftShader are software-rasterised and meaningless; geometry/material/console-error verification is real). **Caveat flagged:** the box is at **99% disk** (338 MB free), which is what made the Playwright install fail the first time. **NET RECOMMENDATION:** make the shipping product a **textured, rigged mesh** (Anny/CC base + real PBR skin + Audio2Face face + Kimodo body motion + LLM director), and demote gaussian splats from "the realism mechanism" to an optional premium/offline path. That satisfies all three of the user's requirements at once and is the cheapest path — it also retires the deformation risk SESSION_HANDOFF calls "the one risk that decides everything".
- **D104 — SPLAT DISTORTION ROOT-CAUSED AND FIXED (the D102 free fit was the culprit, not the real skin) + MetaHuman's licence blocker MOVED (corrects D76) + the Meshy clothing/hair route validated as already-buildable (2026-07-23).** User report: "the new splat is way worse in terms of quality like it's distorted." **(1) SPLAT — diagnosed, not guessed.** The "new splat" was D102's `poc_avatar_hidetail.ply` (free fit: means UNFROZEN + gsplat `DefaultStrategy` densification). Measured against the frozen fit: its means had **drifted off the mesh surface by median 8.9 mm / p99 26 mm / max 39 mm** — on a body whose gaussian spacing is **2.5 mm**, i.e. every gaussian left its anchor by 3–4 spacings — and its opacity had hardened (median 0.17 → 0.34; sub-0.1-opacity gaussians 27% → 2.8%, so far fewer soft overlapping disks). That is exactly the smeared eye band / garbled mouth / red neck streak / blotchy hands seen in `hidetail_compare.png`. **The texture was cleared as a cause by control render:** re-rendering the Blender GT with the same D100 SMOKEWORKS skin produced a CLEAN face (correct brows, lips, hairline, UVs land perfectly) — so the real skin is good and the free fit smeared it. D102's own control had already said the free fit doesn't beat frozen (26.89 dB both); it simply wasn't kept, so the distorted ply is what got shown. **FIX (executed):** re-rendered the 192-view shells rig with the SMOKEWORKS Vol0 "Hannah" PBR skin and re-fit with the FROZEN mesh-anchored recipe (`fit_gsplat_poc.py --iters 3500`, D95 anisotropic-disk init) → **train 27.50 / held-out 27.29 dB** (0.21 dB gap, no memorisation), 41,154 gaussians, anisotropy median 7.80. **Beats D102's free fit on the SAME real-skin source (26.89 dB) AND stays surface-pinned, so it still ANIMATES** (the free fit did not — unfreezing broke the mesh-vertex binding). **Swapped in** as `motion_out/poc_avatar.ply`; the distorted one demoted to `poc_avatar_hidetail_D102_freefit.ply.bak` (the viewer only lists `*.ply`, so its `/splat` card is gone) and the prior live ply kept as `poc_avatar_preD104_procedural.ply.bak`. Capture + provenance in `motion_out/_refit_d104_realskin/`; proof `motion_out/d104_three_way.png` (A prior live/procedural | B D102 distorted | C new). **Honest remaining weakness:** the new splat is clean but the FACE is still soft with dark eye smudges — distortion is gone, blur is not. Per D98/D102 that is the smooth CG SOURCE, not the fitter. **(2) REAL SKIN — all five D100 skins proven on the face, a first.** Rendered a head close-up of every SMOKEWORKS skin (Vol0 Hannah/Mike, Vol1 Tinasia/Hwang/Dave) on Anny + the procedural baseline (`motion_out/d104_skin_matrix.png`). All five land correctly on Anny's MakeHuman UVs and are a large jump over the procedural skin the live viewer still uses; **Tinasia reads most photoreal**. What this exposes: the weakest link on the face is now the **procedural yellow irises + smooth face GEOMETRY**, i.e. the user's "face realism" — a geometry/eye problem, no longer a texture problem. **(3) MetaHuman — D76 IS PARTLY WRONG NOW (licence changed June 2025).** Epic re-licensed MetaHuman under standard UE terms: **free under $1M revenue, usable in ANY engine or creative software, and MetaHumans can be SOLD and redistributed on marketplaces** — which removes the redistribution/SaaS clause D76 called fatal for our ship-to-browser model. **What remains is the clause D97 identified as the market-closer:** MetaHumans may be used *in* AI workflows but **not to train or enhance AI models**, and our gaussian fit + corrective MLP sits squarely on that line. **Net: D76's conclusion (don't ship MetaHuman) survives, but for a DIFFERENT reason than recorded — the AI clause, not redistribution.** Practical note: MetaHuman assets are `.mhpkg` behind an Epic account (MetaHuman Creator / UE / Fab), not loose files, so they cannot be fetched from this box; Fab's listing API is Cloudflare-blocked, so **the exact count of FREE MetaHuman packs is UNVERIFIED** (Epic's docs enumerate categories — Editable Characters, Character Assembly, Grooms, Skeletal/Outfit Clothing, free and paid — but publish no numbers). Separate technical blocker regardless of licence: **MetaHuman textures are in MetaHuman's own UV layout**, so they cannot drop onto Anny without a UV-transfer bake — the same reason the film-grade Lee Perry-Smith "Infinite" maps already in `assets_src/heads/` are still unused. **(4) MESHY for clothing/hair — cheaper than D103's $300–1.5k commission, and the binder ALREADY EXISTS.** D97 already put **Meshy PAID tier** in the CLEAN column (paid = you own the output, sell without attribution; the free tier is CC-BY and must never be used), re-confirmed against Meshy's current help centre; ~$20/mo Pro. The integration worry (MHCLO metadata) is unfounded: `mpfb_prefit.transfer()` takes a **raw `garment_verts` array** and binds it by nearest-triangle barycentric + signed-normal offset onto Anny's rest body, returning the LBS binding — asset-agnostic. A Meshy garment only needs alignment/scale to Anny's rest pose, then it feeds the existing D101 XPBD cloth path unchanged. Caveats: Meshy hair comes out as a solid SHELL not cards (fine for us — we bake to gaussians — but wrong-looking in the mesh preview), and its watertight single-sided shells may need cleanup before XPBD. **This is the concrete answer to D103's "the ceiling is the boxy proxy ASSETS".** Open (not built): the UV-transfer bake that would unblock MetaHuman/Lee-Perry-Smith textures, and swapping the LIVE viewer base model off the procedural skin (SESSION_HANDOFF Immediate-Next #7 — now shown ready).
- **D97 — Researched clean + affordable realistic-avatar asset sources (parallel subagent, 2026-07-23).** Full report: `research/avatar-asset-sources-2026.md`. Task: find realistic body/face/SKIN/hair/clothing sources that clear ALL of {commercial, redistribution/hosting, NO-AI/ML clause, affordable} for our ship-to-browser + gaussian-bake pipeline; skin realism is the weakest area so prioritize it; read licenses VERBATIM (project discipline). **Key cross-cutting finding:** redistribution is usually navigable (most scan vendors sell a "single commercial project" license that permits embedding), but the **no-AI/ML clause is what closes off the market** — since ~2023, 3DScanStore/Ten24, Texturing.xyz, AXYZ, Renderpeople, Triplegangers all added explicit bans on using scans to train "digital humans"/AI/"computer-vision research", and gaussian-splat optimization + a corrective MLP is defensibly exactly what those clauses target even applied per-subject under a properly-licensed single project. **CLEAN shortlist (ranked):** (1) **Lee Perry-Smith "Infinite" head scan** (ir-ltd.net) — CC-BY 3.0, verified from primary source, film-grade skin maps (the asset Pixar used in its RenderMan skin tutorial), free, head-only/needs retopo; (2) **SMOKEWORKS "Skins Vol.0/1"** (itch.io) — CC-BY 4.0, drop-in for the existing MakeHuman pipeline, free/donation; (3) **self-hosted Stable Diffusion 1.5/SDXL** as a pore/detail synthesizer (OpenRAIL-M doesn't bar downstream use of owned outputs as texture assets); (4) Meshy AI PAID tier only (never its free CC-BY tier); (5) CC0 skin-surface tiles (detail-layer only, low realism); (6) **commission a hero asset with rights assigned to us** — the only route where WE write the ML-use grant → zero clause risk; notably **Infinite-Realities** (same studio as the free CC-BY head) now runs a gaussian-splat "Spatial Capture" service and states it holds a commercial license with Inria to distribute splat content — a studio already in our exact space; rough informed estimate (NOT a quote): ~$300-1,500 head, ~$1,500-6,000 full body with full rights. **Newly BLOCKED with verbatim evidence:** Texturing.xyz (explicit AI/ML ban), FaceScape/academic face-scans (non-commercial), Digital Emily/Wikihuman (CC non-commercial despite a mislabeled GitHub "MIT" — same trap the project has caught before), Triplegangers (explicit AI/ML ban), and a flagged landmine — **Adobe Firefly** (markets "commercially safe" but its ToS bars using outputs "in connection with creating, training, or otherwise improving AI and machine learning models," conflicting with our gaussian-fit + corrective-MLP use). **CONDITIONAL (needs written vendor confirmation):** 3DScanStore/Ten24, Renderpeople, AXYZ (best realism ceiling, but each has an AI/CV clause that plausibly captures us). **Explicitly UNVERIFIED (couldn't fetch — flagged, not guessed):** 3d.sk ToS (403), AXYZ page (JS), USC ICT Digital Emily (DNS), Fab/Megascans EULA (403), and various current price lists. Reinforces the standing guardrail (CC0/owned/commissioned only) and adds concrete new clean options to raise the skin-realism ceiling. See header D95–D97.
- **D96 — CLOTHING: fit-once-at-neutral + skeleton LBS — the real fix for fold-clipping, and first clothes on the WALKING avatar (parallel subagent, 2026-07-23).** Implements the approach flagged since D94: stop re-evaluating the MHCLO affine binding at a posed (folded) body; instead fit the garment ONCE on the neutral body and deform it WITH the skeleton. **Verified anny's actual skinning API** (`get_rest_model` → rest verts + `rest_bone_poses`; `get_bone_transforms(deltas, rbp, "local-bone")` → the posed·rest⁻¹ matrices; buffers `vertex_bone_weights`/`vertex_bone_indices`) and **confirmed a manual dense LBS reproduces anny's own `m.forward()` posed body to 3e-16** — the garment is driven by the identical transform stack as the body. **Pipeline (`outfit_lib.fit_asset_lbs`):** (1) fit the MHCLO against anny's raw T-pose `rest_vertices` (19158v makehuman topology, D89 — the armpit is maximally OPEN here AND it's the exact LBS rest space the bone transforms are defined against); (2) each garment vertex INHERITS skinning weights = barycentric (w1,w2,w3) blend of its 3 bound body vertices' weights (negative extrapolation weights clamped, row-renormalized) → dense (Ng,163); (3) deform to any target pose via the same LBS the body uses; (4) same robustness filters + a LIGHT 4mm surface push kept only as a safety net. `fit_mhclo` now also returns the raw affine binding (`bind_idx`/`bind_w`) so weights can be inherited. **The decisive result — clipping vs pose angle (shirt), push DISABLED to isolate the method:** OLD affine-at-posed GROWS with pose depth (40°: 9.68%/−33mm → 60°: 10.05% → 80°: 10.68%), NEW neutral+LBS SHRINKS (40°: 8.22%/−30mm → 60°: 6.21% → 80°: 5.30%) — the LBS advantage grows exactly in the walking regime, and deep (>10mm) clips drop 12→4 on the shirt. **Honest framing:** at the mild 40° preview the *visible* blotches are the pose-INDEPENDENT approximate affine binding (~4% even on the neutral rest body — the D93/D94 cause-(a) fitter-accuracy floor, needs MPFB2's engine, out of scope), so the light push still does similar total cleanup there for both paths; what the LBS eliminates is cause-(b), the pose-SCALED fold-drag (no growth with angle). Pants/hair are byte-identical OLD vs NEW on the arms-down preview because arms-down only rotates the arms (legs/head don't move — correct). **MILESTONE (Deliverable 2, the real goal): DONE** — `motion_out/d95_walk_dressed.png` shows the SAME neutral-fit shirt + cargo pants skinned across 4 real walk frames (0/40/75/110) via per-frame bone transforms from the SOMA retarget: pants legs track the stride, torso stays dressed, clip stays in the 6-9% neutral band with no blow-up, NO per-frame re-fit (reproducer `motion_out/_scratch_d95_walk.py`). **Files (clothing only):** `mhclo_fit.py` (returns bind_idx/bind_w), `outfit_lib.py` (new `_arms_down_pose_deltas`, `_neutral_fit_data`, `bone_transforms_for_pose`, `arms_down_bone_transforms`, `_garment_bone_weights`, `skin_garment`, `fit_asset_lbs`; `fit_asset_checked` left intact for the catalog validator), `viewer/serve_viewer.py` (`build_compose_buffer` uses `fit_asset_lbs`), `compose_avatar.py` (parity). Catalog counts unchanged (14 hair / 13 eyebrows / 7 clothing). **What remains for full walking integration in the LIVE viewer:** the garment needs the SAME post-transform the display walk applies (`pose_default_walk.py`'s Z-up→Y-up + pelvis bounce + de-drift + ground) and a per-frame buffer endpoint; clean seam — `bone_transforms_for_pose(P)` + `skin_garment(...)` already produce the posed garment from any frame's bone deltas. Plus the pre-existing open items: the affine-binding blotch floor (MPFB2 engine) and the pants knee-slit (that asset's own mesh hole). NOTE: this work is labeled "D96" in the docs but some code comments/scratch filenames say "D95" (both parallel subagents independently picked the next number; the splat one anchored D95). See header D95–D97.
- **D95 — SPLAT: anisotropic surface-aligned gaussians — fixed the "spheres/foam" look, PSNR up 5 dB (parallel subagent, 2026-07-23).** The user reported the splat's gaussians looked like near-perfect spheres/foam. **Root cause = the DATA (the fit), not the custom renderer** — confirmed two ways: (1) the web renderer (`splat.html`) already correctly packs the full 3D covariance (6 floats/gaussian, D87) and eigendecomposes it per-frame into oriented ellipses, so given isotropic input it can only draw circles — no shape to recover; (2) rendering the same `.ply` through **gsplat's own reference rasterization** (independent of the web path) reproduced the identical foam look. The fit produced spheres because `fit_gsplat_poc.py` (a) initialized scale ISOTROPICALLY (same on all 3 axes), (b) used IDENTITY quaternions (no surface alignment), and (c) exported the best-held-out checkpoint captured at ~iter 500 (SH deg 0, before the weak image-loss on a soft mesh-anchored body could spontaneously flatten spheres). **Fix (fit_gsplat_poc.py init block only):** initialize each gaussian as a thin flat surface-aligned disk — build a per-gaussian orthonormal frame from the mesh vertex normal (two tangents + normal), set the rotation quaternion from that frame (via scipy Rotation), anisotropic scale init (tangents 1.35× spacing, normal 0.18× → ratio ~7.5 at init), and a PER-AXIS scale cap (tangents may grow to 4× spacing; the normal axis capped thin at 0.7× so disks can't re-inflate). **Results (re-fit on the existing 96-view capture):** anisotropy median 1.13 → **7.85** (p90 8.69, p99 9.68), flatness (mid/short) 1.06 → **7.50** (oblate disks), thin axis aligns with the surface normal at median |cos| = **0.989**, and held-out **PSNR 25.59 → 30.73 dB** — went UP, i.e. flat surface disks reconstruct the body MORE accurately than fat spheres (a quality gain, not a tradeoff), 0 NaNs / 0 negative eigenvalues. **Only fit_gsplat_poc.py changed** (renderer + serve_viewer.py were already correct). New `motion_out/poc_avatar.ply` swapped in (old → `poc_avatar_preD95.ply.bak`), served live on mtime (no restart). Proof images: `motion_out/d95_{front_full,threequarter,head_closeup,torso_closeup}.png` (LEFT old isotropic | RIGHT new anisotropic, via gsplat's reference rasterizer). See header D95–D97.
- **D94 — Answered "WHY does it still clip" with a real diagnosis, and fixed the dominant cause (2026-07-23).** The user stopped accepting patches and asked the right question. Investigated properly with `trimesh` signed-distance-to-SURFACE (nearest point on any body triangle, not the crude nearest-vertex proxy D93 used), across pose angles: **(1)** the affine binding is inherently approximate — even on the neutral (T-pose) body, ~4% of a shirt's vertices land a few mm (≤7mm) inside; **(2)** the dominant cause — the arms-down POSE folds the body, and the affine binding evaluated at that folded state fails at fold regions. Measured a clean monotonic trend on the same shirt: interior-vertex clipping of 4%/−7mm at 0° → 4%/−17mm at 15° → 6%/−25mm at 25° → **10%/−33mm at the shipped 40° arms-down pose**, concentrated at the armpit (|x|≈138mm toward the side, height≈0.74). Mechanism: when the arm rotates down, the armpit crease closes, and garment vertices anchored (via their 3 body-vertex barycentric binding) to points inside that closing fold get carried deep inside the body. **Falsified two plausible-but-wrong explanations by direct experiment rather than assuming:** (a) it is NOT the offset pointing the wrong way — implemented the proper deformation-transfer fix (express each offset in its binding triangle's REST local frame, reconstruct in the POSED frame so it co-rotates) and it changed the deep clipping by ~1mm, i.e. nothing; (b) it is NOT the near-zero-offset vertices D93 identified — the deep-clipping verts have normal-magnitude offsets (~50mm, same as the asset median), so it's the barycentric ANCHOR that's in the fold, not the offset. **Why D93's push didn't finish the job:** it pushed along the nearest body VERTEX's averaged normal, which in a concave crease (armpit) points across/into the fold, so pushing harder (tested 8mm, 15mm margins) left MORE verts stuck, not fewer. **The fix (D94):** rewrote `push_off_surface` to, for each still-embedded vertex, find the closest point on the body SURFACE (`trimesh.proximity.closest_point`, any triangle) and move it to that point + margin along THAT triangle's own outward face normal, iterated a few times (a vertex can relocate across a fold between iterations); and to measure against the actually-DISPLAYED 13,718-v body, not the 19,158-v fit mesh (same surface to 0.00mm per D89 but different triangulation at folds, so pushing clear of the fit mesh left 6 shirt verts poking through the display mesh; pushing against the display mesh fixed that). **Verified concretely, not assumed:** the surface-normal push drops interior verts from 112 to ~0 at *every* pose angle including the full 40°, and rendering the exact live `/compose.bin` output (shirt+pants+hair) shows a solid, clean shirt with the blotchy skin patches from the user's screenshot gone — the only bare skin left is legitimate (the midriff gap between a short shirt and low pants, plus arms/neck). Catalog validation skips the (now ~1s/asset) push via a new `push_margin=0` arg since it discards the geometry anyway. **Honest remainder:** ≤6 vertices on the worst asset (the shirt) can survive in the very deepest armpit fold — not visually significant, but a reminder that vertex-pushing is a cleanup, not a true solution. The real solution remains the one flagged since Immediate Next #4: fit the garment ONCE at the neutral/unfolded pose and deform it WITH the body via the skeleton (LBS), instead of re-evaluating the affine binding at a folded posed state — that eliminates fold-clipping at the source and is also exactly what's needed to put clothes on the WALKING body. Live server restarted, catalog intact (7 clothing / 14 hair / 13 eyebrows). See Decision Log D94.
- **D93 — Found and fixed a THIRD distinct clothing bug: opaque z-buffer clipping from near-zero-offset vertices, not sizing at all (2026-07-23).** User sent a screenshot of a t-shirt with a symmetric, clean-edged blotchy pattern of skin-colored patches across the chest and torso, and asked precisely the right diagnostic question: is this a real gap in the mesh, or is part of it "under the mesh or overlaid by" the body? **Diagnosis, not guesswork:** re-examined the D91 boost-value test data already on file (renders at offset_boost 1.0/1.5/2.0/2.5/3.0/3.5/5.0) and confirmed the same blotchy regions were present and barely changed in size across that entire range -- the signature of a near-ZERO base offset (D91's `offset_boost` multiplies the per-vertex offset; scaling ~0 by anything is still ~0). This makes sense structurally: some vertices in a garment's own authored `.mhclo` binding are meant to sit almost exactly ON the body by design (seams, snug-fit lines, wrinkle creases) -- their offset was never meant to be large, so boosting the garment's overall offset never moves them. Because the `＋ Outfit` preview renders OPAQUE geometry (vertex-colored `MeshStandardMaterial`, no alpha blending), a vertex that ends up even fractionally inside the body doesn't blend or fade -- the nearer, opaque body surface wins that pixel outright, with a clean edge exactly where the garment surface dips below the body surface. This is mechanically distinct from D90 (units) and D91 (uniform undersizing) -- a third, separate bug hiding behind the same visual symptom category ("stuff shows through the clothes"). **Fix:** `outfit_lib.push_off_surface()` -- computes real per-vertex OUTWARD normals of the fit basemesh (from its own face winding, sign-verified against the body centroid, not assumed), builds a KDTree over it, and for every garment vertex, finds the nearest body vertex and enforces a minimum clearance (4mm default) along that vertex's normal; only vertices actually under the margin get moved, so it can't inflate already-loose regions (sleeves, puffy folds) the way a further offset-boost increase would. Wired into `fit_asset_checked` as a new step after the existing below-feet/edge-outlier filters, on by default, independent of and complementary to D91's `offset_boost` (not a replacement -- boost fixes overall garment volume, this fixes surface-hugging vertices specifically). **Verified concretely:** re-rendered the exact shirt from the screenshot before/after -- blotchy pattern gone, clean solid coverage (908 of ~1095 vertices needed the push, confirming the bug was widespread on this asset, not a rare edge case). Also checked pants (small persistent knee-area gap unaffected by either D91 or D93's fix -- flagged as likely a genuine hole in that specific asset's own mesh geometry, a separate open issue, not something either fitting fix can address) and hair (bald center-strip gap unchanged by this fix too, consistent with it being the same already-flagged separate structural problem, not a clearance issue). Re-validated the full 35-asset catalog post-fix: still 35/35, no regressions. Live server restarted. See Decision Log D93.
- **D92 — Manual per-kind garment size control added, replacing another round of guessed defaults (2026-07-23).** After D91's tuned defaults (clothing 3.0x, hair 1.2x), the user asked plainly for control rather than more iteration: "clothing and hair need more adjustments... can i control it manually?" Added two range sliders to the viewer's right panel under a new "Outfit sizing" section (Hair, Clothing; 0.5x-6x, step 0.1) that live-refit the `＋ Outfit` preview as they're dragged. Implementation: `viewer.html` tracks an `outfitBoost` client state object (defaults matching D91's server defaults so the UI starts in sync), appends `<kind>_boost=` params to the existing `/compose.bin` request; `serve_viewer.py`'s handler parses and clamps them (0.1-10.0), threads through a new `boosts` dict param on `build_compose_buffer` (also folded into its cache key so different slider values don't collide) down to `fit_asset_checked(..., offset_boost=...)`, which now accepts an explicit override instead of always auto-picking the per-kind default from the asset path. `mhclo_fit.fit_mhclo`'s `offset_boost` param and math are unchanged from D91 -- this is purely a control-surface addition, not a new fitting behavior. Verified the wiring is real (not just "no errors"): fetched `/compose.bin` at two different `hair_boost` values via `curl`, parsed the returned buffer, and confirmed the hair sub-range's bbox actually changes with the slider value (a naive whole-buffer bbox check looked identical at first because the much-larger body dominates it -- had to isolate the hair vertices specifically to see the real effect). See Decision Log D92.
- **D91 — D90 was wrong (or at least too aggressive): reverted the `den` reinterpretation, replaced it with a plain, empirically-tuned, per-asset-kind uniform enlargement (2026-07-23).** User tried D90's fix and pushed back immediately and specifically: "now you made it worse... fuzzy, distorted... before, the asset rendered correctly, it's just that the size was sized for a smaller avatar... if we can just enlarge the asset a little bit... I don't know what you did, but it made it worse." This is a precise bug report in its own right: it says the D89 state (correct shape, wrong SIZE only) was the right baseline to build from, and D90's fix changed something structural (shape), not just size. **Diagnosed by testing a range of values, not re-guessing:** re-added `fit_mhclo`'s `x_scale/y_scale/z_scale` calibration exactly as D89 left it (raw `den`, no unit reinterpretation) and layered a NEW, separate, genuinely uniform `offset_boost` multiplier on top (applied identically to x/y/z, so it can't itself introduce directional distortion the way a per-axis reinterpretation of `den`'s units could). Rendered pants/shirt/hair at boost values 1.0/1.5/2.0/2.5/3.0/3.5/5.0 and looked at each: **clothing** (pants, shirt) showed a clean, steadily-closing gap with NO visible distortion up through at least 3.5x -- picked **3.0x** as the clothing default (closes the leg/torso skin-gap the user reported without pushing further than needed). **Hair told a different story:** even at a modest 2.0x it showed new jagged/shard silhouette edges (matching "fuzzy, distorted"), and a bald strip down the back of the head that persisted UNCHANGED at every boost level including 1.0x (no boost at all) -- meaning that specific gap was never a sizing problem, it's a separate structural issue (same family as D89's still-unsolved reverse-braid-bun, likely) that a uniform multiplier cannot fix and pushing the multiplier higher only makes worse. Picked **1.2x** for hair (mild, safe, doesn't introduce jaggedness) and **1.0x** for eyebrows (D83 already established their offsets are millimeter-scale and don't need calibration). Implemented as `outfit_lib._DEFAULT_OFFSET_BOOST` (a per-kind dict, auto-selected from the asset's path in `fit_asset_checked`, overridable), NOT a single global constant like D90's attempt -- the empirical finding that different asset kinds need different treatment IS the fix, not an implementation detail. Re-validated the full 35-asset catalog (still 35/35 pass) and re-rendered the same pants/torso/hair comparison views used to catch D90's regression, this time confirming the fix directly rather than assuming it. Live server restarted. **Honestly still open:** hair's bald-strip gap (pre-existing, not introduced by any of D89/D90/D91) is unsolved -- flagged for next session, likely needs the same kind of investigation D89 gave the reverse-braid-bun (comparing against MPFB2's own engine) rather than another scale/offset knob. See Decision Log D91.
- **D90 — Units bug found and fixed: garments were sized ~10% too small on their offset axis, the "everything fits a smaller avatar" the user caught by actually clicking through D89's fix (2026-07-23).** User's report was precise and diagnostic even in their own words: hair sinking into the skull (skull visible through gaps), pants/shirts showing bare skin through the front "like they're made for a smaller avatar." Rendered the exact composed-avatar output the viewer produces (pants+shirt+hair on the arms-down body) and confirmed visually first -- large symmetric skin-colored patches showing through the front of both legs and the torso, exactly as described, not an exaggeration. **Root cause, found numerically:** `mhclo_fit.py`'s D83 per-axis offset-scale-calibration reads a `den` value from the `.mhclo` file (the reference basemesh's recorded distance between two landmark vertices) and computes `scale = our_basemesh_distance(v1,v2) / den`, rescaling every offset by it. Printed the actual numbers for the shirt and pants: `our_dist` ≈ 0.15-0.24m (correct, meters) but `den` ≈ 1.4-2.4 (NOT meters) -- giving `scale` ≈ 0.10-0.11 on every single axis of every asset checked, i.e. every garment's outward offset was being shrunk to ~10% of its intended size. Confirmed the fix by dividing `den` by 10 (MakeHuman's basemesh is internally ~10 units tall for a ~1.7-1.8m human, i.e. its native unit is the decimeter): all six scale ratios (x/y/z, shirt+pants) landed at 0.98-1.07 -- squarely where a legitimate small body-proportion calibration should land, not a coincidence. **This bug predates D89** (introduced with the scale-calibration feature itself in D83) but was invisible until now -- D81/D83/D87's much larger index-space bug (D89) was producing far more dramatic breakage (shattering, halos) that masked this smaller, consistent 10x error; once D89 fixed the index space, this became the dominant visible symptom. **Fixed with a one-line unit conversion** at `.mhclo` parse time in `mhclo_fit.py`, documented in-line with the exact diagnostic numbers so it can't be silently reverted. **Re-verified by rendering the same pants/shirt/hair views from before the fix:** legs now fully covered (no skin strips), torso now fully covered (shirt properly loose/puffy, prior large chest/waist skin patches gone), hair now full-volume covering the whole scalp (was previously so shrunk it barely covered the crown). **The one D89 exception is unaffected, as expected:** re-rendered `elvs_reverse_french_braid_bun` after this fix too -- identical flat-ring result, confirming that residual gap really is a separate fitting-algorithm issue (D89), not a units problem this fix could also explain away. Live server restarted; full 35-asset catalog re-validated (still 35/35, contact sheet re-rendered and visually reviewed -- pants/shirts/hair all read as properly-sized garments now, not thin shrunken patches). See Decision Log D90.
- **D89 — Root-caused and mostly fixed the clothing-fitting problem the user pushed back on in D87 ("we need to figure something out" about hair/clothes) (2026-07-23).** User approved building the real fix (installing the real MPFB2 Blender addon, flagged since D81/D87 as the next real investment) after being warned that HIGHER-quality assets would make the current approximate fitter WORSE, not better (larger/more complex vertex offsets extrapolate worse under the same broken math). **Step 1 -- installed MPFB2 for real:** cloned `makehumancommunity/mpfb2` (GitHub, 553 stars), read its license VERBATIM (project habit, D73/D83) rather than trusting GitHub's "Other/NOASSERTION" label: source code GPLv3 (fine -- used as a local build tool, like Blender itself, never shipped), bundled assets (basemesh, targets, MHCLO clothes) CC0, and critically section D of its own license doc states explicitly that **output from MPFB -- exports, scripted results, anything generated via calling its functions -- carries NO restriction whatsoever**, even via scripting. Packaged `src/mpfb` as a Blender 4.2 extension zip, installed + enabled it in the project's headless Blender via `bpy.ops.extensions.package_install_files` + `bpy.ops.preferences.addon_enable` (persisted to `userpref.blend` so it survives across `-b -P script.py` runs). **Step 2 -- used it to prove the asset itself was never the problem:** drove MPFB2's own `HumanService.create_human()` + `add_mhclo_asset()` (its script_samples/ dir documents exactly this API) to fit `elvs_reverse_french_braid_bun` -- the flowing-hair asset D81 diagnosed as hitting "catastrophic cancellation from basemesh-precision differences" and excluded ever since -- onto MPFB2's OWN basemesh. Rendered it: a clean, correctly-shaped braid/bun, no explosion. This falsified the working assumption (an inherent precision limit) and reframed the question as "what's actually different about OUR basemesh." **Step 3 -- found the real bug:** `mhclo_fit.py`'s docstring said its `basemesh_verts` param should be `(13718,3)` -- Anny's DEFAULT topology output. But MakeHuman's raw basemesh (what `.mhclo` binding indices v1/v2/v3 are authored against) has **19,158 vertices** (confirmed: `anny/data/mpfb2/3dobjs/base.obj` bundled inside the `anny` package itself, plus MPFB2's own `create_human()` mesh, both 19,158v). Anny's default topology is a REDUCED, RENUMBERED subset (helper/joint geometry stripped) -- feeding its indices into a fitter expecting the raw 19,158-index space is a genuine INDEX-SPACE mismatch, not the "close but not bit-identical precision" D87 assumed (that framing was itself never verified -- an earlier attempt to compare raw vs. reduced basemeshes directly failed because they have different vertex COUNTS, an apples-to-oranges comparison abandoned as "inconclusive" rather than diagnosed). Found the fix already exists in `anny`'s own API: `anny.Anny(topology="makehuman", remove_unattached_vertices=False)` returns the full RAW 19,158-vertex array, WITH Anny's actual phenotype/WHO-recalibration applied (the blend-shape math already operates in this same 19,158-space internally, per `full_model.py`'s `[564,19158,3]` blend-shape tensor). **Verified before trusting it (numerically, not assumed):** nearest-neighbor surface distance between this 19,158v array and the actually-DISPLAYED 13,718v default-topology body, same phenotype+pose = **0.00mm everywhere, including the entire head region** -- an exact match, meaning garments fit against it sit correctly on the real displayed body with zero transfer/remap step and (it turned out) **no MPFB2 runtime dependency at all** -- MPFB2 was essential for diagnosis, not for production. **Step 4 -- fixed + re-validated for real:** updated `mhclo_fit.py` (docstring + `__main__` block) and added `outfit_lib.arms_down_fit_basemesh()` (new, 19158v; kept `arms_down_basemesh()` unchanged, 13718v, for what's actually rendered) plus updated its three call sites (`compose_avatar.py`, `serve_viewer.py`'s `build_catalog`/`build_compose_buffer`) to fit against the new array while still displaying the old one. Then, per the project's own D86 discipline ("actually render every item, don't just trust numeric filters"), re-ran validation AND rendered a full contact sheet of all 35 catalog assets (incl. the 4 previously excluded) against the fix: **all 3 previously-"shattered" `toigo_*` tops are now genuinely clean, correctly-shaped garments** (verified via direct close-up renders, not just thumbnails) -- un-excluded from the live catalog (clothing catalog: 2 tops -> 5 tops). **Honest remaining gap, not papered over:** `elvs_reverse_french_braid_bun` is STILL broken after the fix -- improved (a contained flat ring/disc around the head, not the old halo draping down the back) but still visibly wrong, not a bun. Diagnosed one step further: fitting the SAME asset with OUR OWN `fit_mhclo()` code but against MPFB2's OWN exported basemesh (eliminating any Anny-side factor entirely) STILL produces a broken result, while MPFB2's own real fitting ENGINE on that same basemesh does not -- meaning the residual gap for this one asset is a genuine difference between our simple weighted-sum affine fit and whatever MPFB2's real algorithm does differently (subdivision, multi-pass correction, or similar), not a basemesh issue at all. The other 3 assets sharing this asset's same extreme-extrapolation-weight family (`elvs_double_mh_braid`, `elvs_french_braid_variation`, `elvs_unkempt_french_braid`) were specifically re-checked and DO fit cleanly now (they drape along the head/neck surface; the broken one uniquely needs to build volume off the surface, the harder case). Kept `elvs_reverse_french_braid_bun` excluded, documented honestly in `serve_viewer.py`'s `_KNOWN_BROKEN` with this exact finding, rather than shipping a differently-broken result under a "fixed" label. Live server restarted; verified via `curl` that `/catalog.json` reflects the new counts. See Decision Log D89.
- **D88 — Actually ran the D87 refit end-to-end (nothing survived from the prior session) and swapped it in (2026-07-23).** D87 described a 96-view (4 rings x 24 azimuth) re-render + refit as "running now in the background," but at the start of this session no such process, output, or scratch directory existed anywhere on the box — the prior session's background job was lost when the session ended, not completed. Re-ran it for real: `export_textured_obj.py` -> `blender_render_skin.py --elevs=-15,15,45,75` (found and fixed a usage bug on the way — `--frames` is the TOTAL view count divided across rings, not per-ring; the first attempt passed `--frames 24` and got 6 views/ring = 24 total instead of the intended 96, caught from the render log's own view-count print before wasting the fit on it, re-ran with `--frames 96`) -> `fit_gsplat_poc.py --iters 3500`. Result: held-out PSNR 25.59dB, train 25.58dB (no overfit gap, matches D83's established quality tier), 0 NaNs. Verified the SPECIFIC thing this rerun was supposed to fix, not just the aggregate PSNR: extracted the new fit's own rendered top-of-head (75deg ring) and underarm (-15deg ring) training views from `fit_turntable.gif` and both show a coherent, solid, correctly-shaded body — the gap D87 diagnosed (single flat ring, nothing ever looked at these regions) is gone from the capture. Honest carry-overs, not hidden: median anisotropy ratio is ~1.135 on this fit, essentially unchanged from D87's ~1.098 — the gaussians are still nearly spherical, so D87's "the renderer fix had little real shape to recover" finding is confirmed to hold on the richer capture too, not just the old one. Mean opacity dropped 0.288 -> 0.170 vs. the old `.ply` (same 41,154-gaussian count, now satisfying more views) — flagged as a possible follow-up if the `/splat` viewer's `uAlphaBoost` needs re-tuning to match, not yet checked in a real browser (still no headless browser on this box). Backed up the old file to `motion_out/poc_avatar_d87_singlering.ply.bak`, copied the new fit to `motion_out/poc_avatar.ply`, and confirmed via `curl` that the already-running `serve_viewer.py`'s `/splat.bin` immediately served the new byte content (mtime-based re-read, no restart needed, per the existing documented behavior). Old render/fit intermediates kept at `dataset/motion_out/_refit96/` (~24MB, gitignored) for provenance. **Not yet done: an actual browser click-through of the new splat** — owed next, same standing gap as D85/D86. See Decision Log D88.
- **D87 — Answered "why isn't clothing just simple drag-and-drop" honestly + found the splat renderer was discarding real gaussian shape data (isotropic circles instead of true anisotropic ellipses) + diagnosed the DEEPER cause (an under-constrained single-elevation-ring fit) + kicked off a proper multi-ring re-render/re-fit, all per the user's direct pushback (2026-07-23).** User, after D86: "the hair and clothing still don't fit properly, this is just too much, I thought it's just simple drag and drop, I thought these assets are already premade" + on the splat: "at low size it looks like a point cloud... at high size it looks like a foam bubbly clay toy... I've never seen gaussian splats like this... isn't it basically a 3DGS of our avatar, why not, make it one" + "let's rerender with heavily increased camera positions." **(1) SPLAT SHAPE:** audited the renderer against what real 3DGS actually is and found a real gap: `build_splat_buffer` was packing a single scalar "size" (mean of the 3 log-scale axes), discarding each gaussian's true SHAPE (its rotation quaternion + independent per-axis scale) and forcing every splat to draw as an isotropic circle -- real splat viewers (antimatter15, mkkellogg) draw each gaussian's actual oriented ELLIPSE, the projection of its full 3D covariance onto the screen. Fixed properly: server now computes and packs the full 3D covariance (`Sigma = R*S*S^T*R^T`, 6 floats) per gaussian; the client does the standard EWA-splatting-style projection each frame in the vertex shader (rotate covariance into camera space, closed-form eigendecompose the resulting 2x2, offset the billboard quad along the two eigenvectors scaled by their own sqrt(eigenvalue) -- a real oriented ellipse, not a circle). Verified the shader math numerically before shipping (eigenvalues non-negative, no NaNs, magnitudes consistent with the old scalar estimate) and with a matplotlib ellipse-patch simulation of the actual data. **HONEST FINDING: this alone did NOT fix the "clay toy" look** -- measured this fit's own anisotropy ratio (max axis / min axis) at a median of ~1.1 (essentially spherical already), so there was very little shape information to recover in the first place. The renderer fix is still correct and matters for any future better-conditioned fit, but the real cause is the DATA. **(2) ROOT CAUSE OF THE DATA:** `blender_render_skin.py`'s turntable was a SINGLE elevation ring (constant height, only azimuth varies) -- meaning no camera ever directly observes the top of the head or the underarm/sole regions, exactly the under-constrained areas that read as blobby/soft. This is a real, previously-unnoticed gap between the capture rig the live viewer's own UI already models (multiple elevation LAYERS, per its own right-panel) and what the offline PoC fit script actually did (one ring). **Fixed:** added `--elevs` (comma-separated elevation degrees, one ring per value) to `blender_render_skin.py`, and re-rendered at 4 rings (-15/15/45/75 deg) x 24 azimuth = 96 views (was 36, single ring) -- directly answering the user's "heavily increase the camera positions" ask with the more-structurally-correct fix (more elevations, not just more azimuth on the same flat ring), then re-ran `fit_gsplat_poc.py` against the new capture. Kept it a static (non-moving) T-pose fit, matching the user's own "maybe when they're not moving too" instinct -- gaussians aren't bound to the skeleton yet regardless (D74's unsolved bet), so a moving-body multi-view capture wouldn't currently give the optimizer anything extra to work with. **(3) CLOTHING HONESTY:** this is NOT actually "premade assets, simple drag-and-drop" the way a game character-creator is, and said so plainly rather than continuing to silently patch: MHCLO assets encode a per-vertex AFFINE approximation (3 basemesh vertices + weights + offset) authored against MakeHuman's exact canonical basemesh; our body is Anny's own reimplementation of that basemesh (WHO-recalibrated, D56), close but not bit-identical, so the approximation degrades unpredictably per-asset -- from "perfect" (most eyebrows/short hair) to "shattered" (complex strapless/draped garments, D85/D86). Investigated whether Anny exposes an exact-precision path to the original MakeHuman basemesh (compared its bundled raw `base.obj` against Anny's default-topology output) -- inconclusive/negative in the time available (large, non-trivial coordinate differences, not a simple truncation/offset), so did NOT claim a fix here. **The real fix path remains what D81/D83 already identified and neither attempted yet: install the actual MPFB2 Blender addon (GPL) and drive its own real fitting system via `bpy`**, which has MakeHuman's canonical basemesh built in and sidesteps the precision problem entirely instead of approximating it -- a genuinely bigger lift (addon install + new automation script), not something to rush inside this same pass; flagged as the concrete next investment if reliable drag-and-drop fitting for ANY asset (not just the curated/verified subset) is a priority. Files: `dataset/viewer/serve_viewer.py` (full-covariance `build_splat_buffer`), `dataset/viewer/splat.html` (anisotropic EWA-style shader), `dataset/blender_render_skin.py` (`--elevs` multi-ring turntable). (§0.5, §2; corrects a real rendering gap D85 shipped, root-causes the "clay toy" look past the rendering layer into the fit's own view-coverage gap, gives an honest scope assessment for clothing fitting instead of another narrow patch; [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D86 — D85's edge-length filter wasn't enough (shattered/twisted garment shards still shipped, neither an outlier-edge nor a bbox-blowup) + splat "disappears when zoomed in" fixed + answered the user's "is this even the same avatar" question directly (2026-07-23).** User, after D85 shipped: "the clothing and hair still don't fit normally" (screenshot: a shirt exploded into large blue triangular shards, a hair strand as a big flat blade across the face) + "when I'm zoomed in [the splat] disappears... when I zoom out I can't see the details... isn't it basically a 3DGS of the character in the other viewer, or is it not? If it's not, why not?" **(1) ROOT CAUSE of the shards:** rendered every single catalog item (all 14 hair, all 13 eyebrows, all 5 tops, both bottoms) individually and LOOKED, rather than trusting numeric heuristics — found 4 assets (`toigo_basic_tucked_t-shirt`, `toigo_bodice-style_top`, `toigo_fisherman_sweater`, `elvs_reverse_french_braid_bun`) that are genuinely broken (self-intersecting shard clusters / a bun that explodes into a flat halo) WITHOUT tripping D85's edge-length-outlier filter — because the bad triangles aren't abnormally LONG, they're normal-length but badly TWISTED (a different failure mode: complex drape-y/strapless garment topology doesn't survive this project's crude static-basemesh affine fit, the exact "clothing that drapes with body motion" hard-bit D63 already flagged). No amount of cleverer edge-length thresholding was going to catch this generally in the time available, so **excluded these 4 explicitly** (`_KNOWN_BROKEN` in `serve_viewer.py`, documented with the reasoning, not silently) rather than ship a bad fit behind a heuristic that looked passable on paper. Catalog now: 14 hair, 13 eyebrows, 2 tops, 2 bottoms (down from 15/13/5/2) — thinner but everything in it was actually looked at. **(2) Splat disappearing on zoom-in:** `controls.minDistance` was a fixed 0.2 regardless of the loaded splat's actual scale -- zooming past roughly the body's own half-depth puts the camera surrounded by translucent `depthWrite:false` billboard quads on every side (nothing left silhouetting an "outside" surface to see), which reads as the model vanishing. Fixed by scaling `minDistance` to each loaded splat's own bbox (`topY*0.25`) at load time instead of a fixed constant. **(3) Blurry when zoomed out / "why doesn't it look like real 3DGS":** answered directly, not papered over — verified `poc_avatar.ply` (41,154 gaussians, generated this same session from D83's latest densification fix) uses the IDENTICAL phenotype dict (`gender=0.5, age=0.5, muscle=0.5, weight=0.5, height=0.5, proportions=0.5`) as `walk_face`'s live mesh and `outfit_lib`'s basemesh -- so yes, it genuinely is the same base identity/proportions as "the normal avatar" in the main viewer, confirmed not assumed. But it is honestly NOT the same asset in three real ways, none of them bugs: (a) it's a STATIC T-pose optimization target, not bound to the walk animation -- gaussians aren't skeleton-driven yet, which is literally D74's whole unsolved risk gate, the central bet of this entire project; (b) it was fit against SYNTHETIC Blender renders of the CC0 procedural skin, not real photos, at a measured ~25-26dB held-out PSNR (D80/D83) -- softness at this quality/gaussian-count tier is the actual current ceiling, not a rendering bug this pass can fix by relabeling; (c) it has no eye coloring baked in (that's a live per-frame vertex-color trick applied only to the animated MESH in `viewer.html`, never baked into the static gaussian fit). Did NOT blindly re-run the multi-view-render+fit pipeline (several GPU-minutes) since it would reproduce essentially the same result -- re-verified the existing file matches instead of spending the time for no real gain; flagged as available on request if the user wants a fresh regenerate anyway. Files: `dataset/viewer/serve_viewer.py` (`_KNOWN_BROKEN` denylist), `dataset/viewer/splat.html` (dynamic `minDistance`). (§0.5, §2; corrects a real gap in D85's own filter, clarifies D74's static-vs-animated distinction for a specific asset the user was looking at; [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D85 — THREE MORE REAL BUGS the user caught by actually looking, all fixed same-day as D84: outfit preview crashed with a byte-alignment RangeError, the composed avatar rendered sunk below the floor with stray mis-fit triangles streaking across it, and the new `/splat` route's opaque-icosphere renderer looked like "black spheres... foam," not a gaussian splat (2026-07-23).** User: "the clothing avatar renders below the floor... the clothes are not fitting... it just looks distorted" + a browser RangeError + "[the splat] just looked like a bunch of spheres floating in the air, like black spheres... doesn't look like 3DGS." **(1) CRASH:** `/compose.bin`'s buffer laid out `pos(f32) + color(u8) + faces(u32)` — the color block's byte length (V×3) isn't guaranteed to be a multiple of 4, so `new Uint32Array(buf, offset, ...)` for faces threw `RangeError: start offset ... should be a multiple of 4` whenever it wasn't. **Fixed by reordering to `pos + faces + color`** (color last, since nothing after it needs alignment) in both `serve_viewer.py` and the `viewer.html` client parser. **(2) SUNK BELOW FLOOR:** the compose buffer packed RAW Anny-frame vertices (feet at z≈-0.85, Anny's origin is near the pelvis, not the ground) with no shift; the main animated body's server-side `_orient_yup()` grounds feet to 0 but the new static-outfit path never did — fixed by subtracting the arms-down basemesh's own feet-z from every packed vertex before writing the buffer, matching the animated body's convention. **(3) STRAY TRIANGLES ("distorted, doesn't fit"):** found and fixed a real gap in D84's own validation — `drop_below_feet` only ever caught outliers that land below the feet, but a mis-fit triangle can just as easily land ACROSS the garment (measured: `elvs_crude_t-shirt_male` had 12 triangles with a 0.47-0.57m edge vs. an 0.089m median — the visible diagonal streak across the shirt; `culturalibre_hair_02` had ~90 similarly-blown-out strand triangles making jagged marks over the face). Added `outfit_lib.drop_edge_outliers()` — drops any triangle whose longest edge exceeds `max(0.15m, 5x the asset's own median edge)`, an absolute floor (so it can't misfire on legitimately fine/dense meshes like eyebrows, whose real edges are all under a few cm) combined with a relative one (so a naturally coarse mesh isn't over-filtered). Verified against all 4 curated asset types: 0 false drops on eyebrows/pants, correct drops on the shirt and hair — and as a side effect, one previously-rejected hair asset now passes the catalog's bbox-envelope check since the outlier triangle that was blowing out its bbox gets filtered before that check runs (catalog count 14→15). **(4) SPLAT "FOAM":** D84 shipped the `/splat` route with OPAQUE GPU-instanced icospheres specifically to guarantee *something* renders — but opaque geometry with hard silhouettes can never read as soft gaussian falloff, which is exactly what the user called out. Re-examined the D80-D83 "point cloud" saga with actual numbers instead of assuming the rendering TECHNIQUE was broken: `poc_avatar.ply`'s mean gaussian size (stddev) is ~0.0072, median nearest-neighbor spacing ~0.0015 — good coverage needs a billboard radius of ~2.5-3x stddev, i.e. `uSizeMult` around 5-6; **D83 had retuned `uSizeMult` down to 1.3 (half-width ~0.65x stddev, 4-5x too small)**, which is entirely sufficient on its own to explain "sparse points/dust" even though the underlying billboard-quad TECHNIQUE (view-space corner offset, no `gl_PointSize`) was already immune to the ANGLE/Direct3D11 point-sprite-capping issue D82 diagnosed — D83's size regression was likely the real culprit the whole time, not a rendering-technique failure. **Rebuilt `splat.html` back onto alpha-blended GPU-instanced billboard quads** (the actual gaussian-splat look, same proven shader/depth-sort technique as the Studio's splat-compare) with the corrected default size, live sliders, and validated the fix with a standalone rasterized simulation (`PIL`, front-view projection, same size math) comparing 1.3x vs 5.0x — 1.3x visibly speckled/gappy, 5.0x reads as a smooth, solid, gap-free body. **Honest note:** still couldn't verify any of this by actually clicking through a real browser (none available on this box) — verified via curl + buffer-format asserts + a `pyrender`/`PIL` re-render of the exact server output, which is why this round of bugs shipped in the first place; the user's screenshots were the first real signal. Files: `dataset/viewer/serve_viewer.py` (buffer reorder + floor shift), `dataset/viewer/viewer.html` (buffer parser reorder), `dataset/outfit_lib.py` (`drop_edge_outliers`), `dataset/viewer/splat.html` (billboard-quad rewrite). (§0.5, §2; corrects real regressions shipped in D84; [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D84 — ARMS-CROSSED POSE BUG ROOT-CAUSED AND FIXED (D83's "arms down" 75deg was never actually verified against a render and overshot into a forward curl) + real CC0 hair/eyebrows/clothing assets PERSISTED out of /tmp scratch and WIRED into the live viewer as selectable catalog items + a dedicated `/splat` route built with a renderer that can't silently fail the way three shader-based attempts did (2026-07-23).** User: "the composed avatar's arms are crossed behind its back, like the previous bug" + "I want to see these assets in the viewer, selectable from the left sidebar under each tab" + "the splat still renders as a point cloud — let's just make it a separate route." **(1) ARMS BUG:** rendered the exact `compose_avatar.py` pose code standalone (`pyrender`, bare body) and confirmed visually: the 75deg upperarm rotation was NEVER validated against an actual image — it swings the wrist PAST straight-down and curls it back up in FRONT of the torso (hands landing near the sternum/collarbone), exactly the "crossed" look the user caught, not a clothing-fit artifact. Root-caused numerically: rotated the upperarm01->wrist REST vector about the world Y axis at several angles and read where the wrist actually lands relative to the shoulder pivot (`Tr[wrist]-Tr[shoulder]`) — 40deg lands it at ~[0.04,-0.22,-0.45] (almost straight down), 75deg lands it at ~[-0.21,-0.22,-0.40] (crossed past the midline). **Fixed: 75/-75 -> 40/-40.** Re-rendered the full composed avatar (hair+eyebrows+shirt+pants) with the fix — arms now hang naturally, shirt drapes as a shirt not a cape (`motion_out/composed_avatar_v2.png`). **Refactored the shared pose+fit math out of `compose_avatar.py` into a new `dataset/outfit_lib.py`** (`arms_down_basemesh()`, `fit_asset_checked()` — fit_mhclo + below-feet filter + a sane-bbox-envelope check) specifically so the offline script and the live server (below) can't drift apart the way this bug required them not to. **(2) ASSET PERSISTENCE + CATALOG:** the D81/D83 downloaded CC0 MakeHuman/MPFB2 packs only ever lived in a PRIOR session's /tmp scratch dir (ephemeral, never wired anywhere) — copied a curated set (14 hair, 13 eyebrows, 5 tops, 2 bottoms) into `dataset/motion_out/assets_src/` (gitignored like the rest of motion_out, so it doesn't bloat the repo but survives across sessions; disk checked first, 1.8GB free after). **Validation is automatic, not hand-curated:** `serve_viewer.py`'s new `build_catalog()` fit-tests every asset against the arms-down basemesh at catalog-build time and silently excludes anything that errors (topology mismatch) or blows out past a sane bbox envelope (the D81/D83 flowing-hair-extrapolation failure) — caught a real case live (`elvs_double_mh_braid` blew out to z=1.45 vs body-top 0.77, correctly excluded even though it had passed a cruder manual below-feet-only check earlier in this session — validates building the check into the server instead of hand-picking a "safe list"). New endpoints: `/catalog.json?kind=hair|eyebrows|clothing`, `/asset_src/<kind>/<name>/thumb`, `/compose.bin?hair=&eyebrows=&top=&bottom=` (fits the selection live, packs body+parts into one flat-shaded static mesh buffer, `CMP1` format). **`viewer.html`:** Hair tab now shows selectable Hair/Eyebrows card groups, Clothing tab shows Tops/Bottoms — clicking toggles a slot selection; a new **"＋ Outfit" left-footer button** loads `/compose.bin` for the current selection into a static preview mesh standing beside the animated body (opposite side from Splat compare). **Honest scope limit, stated in-code:** this is a static arms-down "try it on" preview, NOT the walking animation wearing clothes — per-frame garment re-fit or skeleton LBS binding (SESSION_HANDOFF's next-step #4) is still unsolved. **(3) DEDICATED SPLAT ROUTE:** the splat-compare button had already been through gl.POINTS (D80) -> billboard-quad instancing shader (D82) -> densification (D83) and the user still reported "just floating points" — rather than debug a fourth custom-shader iteration blind (no headless browser on this box to actually see results), built `dataset/viewer/splat.html` (new `/splat` route, same top-bar/left-rail/right-panel shell as the Studio) using three.js's OWN native `THREE.InstancedMesh` (per-instance `instanceMatrix`/`instanceColor` — core, heavily-tested three.js machinery, not hand-wired custom attributes) rendering each gaussian as a small low-poly icosphere scaled to its fitted size. Real 3D sphere geometry can't silently degenerate into "a few pixels" the way `gl_PointSize` or a shader corner-offset bug can; near-opaque spheres also sidestep the alpha-blend draw-order problem the last three renderer generations all had to work around. Left rail lists every `.ply` in `motion_out/` (new `/splats.json`) as a selectable card. **Verified everything through the data layer** (server endpoints curl-tested, `/compose.bin`'s exact bytes re-rendered via `pyrender` to confirm the arms-down fix holds through the real live code path, new JS syntax-checked with `esprima`) since this box still has no headless browser for a true click-through browser test — flagged to the user as the one unverified step.
