- **D83 — SPLAT DENSITY FIXED (still-hazy after D82's renderer rewrite -> root cause was DATA sparsity, not just the renderer) + a REAL DRESSED AVATAR ASSEMBLED end-to-end from CC0 MakeHuman assets, with two genuine clothing-fitting bugs found and fixed along the way (2026-07-23).** User: "still hazy point cloud" + "check the GitHub links more properly, e.g. thebasemesh.com" + "start pulling from those libraries and putting the avatar together." **SPLAT:** D82's billboard-quad rewrite was necessary but not sufficient -- 13,718 gaussians (1/mesh-vertex, no densification) is genuinely too sparse to read as solid, however correctly it's rendered. Fixed in `fit_gsplat_poc.py`: (1) **3x densification** -- each mesh vertex now seeds 3 tangent-jittered gaussians (surface-tangent jitter via the vertex normal, not along-normal = stays a shell not a puff) instead of 1, ~41k gaussians total; (2) **found and fixed a self-canceling bug**: the initial gsplat SCALE/size was computed from the NEW finer post-densify spacing, so each of the 3x-more gaussians was also ~3x smaller -- net coverage barely changed until the init/cap were switched to reference the ORIGINAL pre-densify spacing instead. Result: genuinely solid, gap-free body silhouette from every angle (visually confirmed before a later tool outage -- see below). Also retuned the viewer's `uSizeMult`/`uAlphaBoost` down since the underlying gaussians are now properly sized (was compensating in the shader for what should be fixed in the data). **GITHUB LINKS RE-CHECKED PROPERLY** (raw awesome-cc0 README fetched directly, not summarized): thebasemesh.com / M3-org/base-meshes = genuine CC0 but PROP-focused (250+ models: furniture/weapons/food/tools; a "Clothing" category exists but as standalone unrigged meshes, no MHCLO-style auto-fit) -- not useful for the current need; **madjin/100avatars found to be MISLABELED "CC0" in the aggregator** -- its own stated terms are "not to sell...without major modification," a real resale restriction, NOT CC0 (validates the project's "verify verbatim, don't trust the label" discipline, D73); a companion PolygonalMind repo claims the SAME content IS CC0 -- an unresolved conflict, treat as unusable until directly clarified. Neither changes the D82 conclusion (MakeHuman/MPFB2 remains the right pipeline for realistic human parts). **AVATAR ASSEMBLED** (new `dataset/compose_avatar.py`, general-purpose, reusable): body + CC0 hair (`culturalibre_hair_02`, chosen via the D81 weight-range-screening method) + CC0 eyebrows + CC0 t-shirt + CC0 cargo pants, all real downloaded assets, fit via `mhclo_fit.py`. **TWO REAL BUGS found and fixed while assembling clothing (mhclo_fit.py had only been proven on eyebrows/hair/one stocking before this):** (1) **missing offset-scale calibration** -- mhclo files carry `x_scale/y_scale/z_scale v1 v2 den` directives (a per-axis correction: current-basemesh-distance(v1,v2)/den) that `mhclo_fit.py` was silently ignoring; harmless for small-offset assets (eyebrows) but produces ~9x-too-large offsets on anything with large offsets (sleeves/hems) -- now applied. (2) **T-POSE clothing distortion, the actual root cause of a first broken shirt render** (a huge cape/tent shape) -- traced via direct vertex inspection to CORRECT barycentric binding against genuinely-T-pose wrist vertices (Anny's raw `forward()` output has arms straight out) -- a sleeve spanning shoulder-to-outstretched-wrist inherently looks like a cape; not a fitter bug. Fixed by posing the arms down (~75 degrees, Anny's own `pose_parameters`/'local-bone' bone API, same mechanism as `pose_default_walk.py`) BEFORE fitting clothing -- shirt width dropped from ~0.96m (arm-span-wide) to ~0.4m (torso-width) after the fix. Also added a **stray-outlier filter** (drop any fitted triangle landing below the body's own feet -- caught 6 rogue hair-strand faces + 6 rogue pants faces, both tiny fractions of their totals) to handle the residual D81-class precision-sensitivity tail that survives even on "safe" low-extrapolation assets. **HONEST CAVEAT: the final composed render (`motion_out/composed_avatar.png`) was verified via numerical/color-channel analysis (correct blue-shirt/skin-arms/dark-pants bands in the correct vertical order and plausible proportions) because the image-viewing tool was down for the second half of this session** -- a genuine tool outage, not a skipped step; visual confirmation is still owed next session. `compose_avatar.py` writes a combined multi-material `.obj` (`motion_out/composed_avatar.obj`) -- the next step is running this through `blender_render_skin.py`-style texturing and the D80 gaussian fit for a fully dressed splat avatar. Files: `dataset/mhclo_fit.py` (+scale calibration, +max_offset clamp), `dataset/compose_avatar.py` (new), `dataset/fit_gsplat_poc.py` (+densify), `dataset/viewer/viewer.html` (retuned shader uniforms). (§0.5, §2; executes on D81's proven fitter, corrects D82's renderer-only diagnosis, extends D73/D82's licensing map with the thebasemesh.com/100avatars findings; [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D82 — SPLAT REBUILT on the actual root cause (gl_PointSize is unreliable on this box's ANGLE/Direct3D11 WebGL backend — size/alpha tuning alone couldn't fix it) + the VRM/Quaternius/itch.io sources the user found EVALUATED against the MPFB2 pipeline D81 just proved (2026-07-23).** User: "it's still a point cloud, nothing there, just floating points" + shared 5 more asset sources (Open Source Avatars VRM registry, madjin/awesome-cc0, ToxSam/open-source-avatars, PolyHaven, itch.io CC0 filter). **SPLAT ROOT CAUSE:** D80/D81's size+alpha+depth-sort fixes were real but sat on a broken foundation — the renderer used `gl.POINTS` + `gl_PointSize`, and this box's WebGL context is **ANGLE-over-Direct3D11** (confirmed in the boot `slog`), a backend with long-documented unreliable/capped point-sprite size support — the GPU driver can silently clamp point size to a few px regardless of what the shader requests, independent of any uniform tuning. **FIX: rebuilt the splat renderer as GPU-INSTANCED CAMERA-FACING BILLBOARD QUADS** (`THREE.InstancedBufferGeometry` + per-instance `instancePos/instanceColor/instanceSize/instanceAlpha`; vertex shader offsets each quad corner directly in VIEW SPACE, where XY is already screen-aligned — no gl_PointSize, no point-sprite extension, renders identically on every GPU backend). This is the same technique real production splat viewers (antimatter15, mkkellogg) use, for the same reason. Depth-sort updated to match: instancing has no separate index-for-draw-order (instance i always = attribute-array slot i), so `updateSplatSort()` now physically reorders the 4 instance attribute arrays by camera distance each frame (from an untouched `splatSrc` original, cheap at ~14k gaussians). **ASSET SOURCES EVALUATED:** PolyHaven = already-clean (D73), materials/HDRIs not character-specific; **madjin/awesome-cc0 = a curated LINK LIST, not independently verified per-item** (aggregates PolyHaven/ambientCG alongside others needing individual license checks, same rigor as always); **ToxSam/open-source-avatars = a REGISTRY pointing to VRM files hosted elsewhere** (not a file host), per-collection license varies CC0/CC-BY per its own `projects.json`, nothing checked yet at the individual-collection level; **Quaternius = genuinely CC0 confirmed**, but stylized/low-poly GAME asset packs (nature/vehicles/fantasy), not realistic human hair/face/clothing; **itch.io CC0 filter = a marketplace tag, not an enforced guarantee**, same per-asset verification burden as anything else. **THE DECISIVE POINT: VRM is a fundamentally different avatar FORMAT** — its own topology + skeleton standard, one unique mesh per avatar, **zero compatibility with the D81 MHCLO vertex-binding pipeline** (which only works because Anny's mesh IS MakeHuman's basemesh). Using a VRM asset means either adopting it as a wholesale Anny replacement, or manually re-rigging extracted parts onto Anny by hand — real separate engineering, not the automatic fit D81 proved. **DECISION: stay on the MakeHuman/MPFB2 pipeline for hair/clothing/face-detail** (proven, automatic, zero extra work per D81); treat VRM/Quaternius/itch.io as supplementary sources for what MakeHuman doesn't cover (stylized props/environment), not the primary route for realistic human assets. Files: `dataset/viewer/viewer.html` (splat renderer rewrite: `THREE.InstancedBufferGeometry`, billboard-quad shaders, instance-array depth sort). (§0.5, §2; corrects D81's splat depth-sort fix which was necessary but insufficient; extends D73/D81's licensing map; sources: github.com/ToxSam/open-source-avatars, github.com/madjin/awesome-cc0, quaternius.com; [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D81 — EYES FIXED (the LIVE viewer's SOMA-topology body has NO facial geometry at all — switched the default model to the DEFAULT topology which does) + SPLAT "point cloud" FIXED (depth-sort + bigger/brighter splats) + MPFB2/MakeHuman CC0 asset ecosystem FOUND, LICENSE-VERIFIED, and PROVEN TO FIT onto Anny's native mesh with ZERO remapping — hair/clothes/eyebrows/hand-face-detail all available; clothing+eyebrows fit CLEANLY today, flowing hair hits a real precision-sensitivity limit (diagnosed, not hidden) (2026-07-23).** **(1) EYES:** root cause was NOT a shader/material bug — the LIVE animated body (`render_soma_motion.py`'s SOMA-resampled 18,056-v topology, `faces = layer.faces` with no segmentation step) was rendered+confirmed via a pyrender headshot to have **literally no facial geometry** (no eye sockets, no nose, smooth blob) — SOMA's topology is optimized for body motion transfer, not facial detail; the D72 eyeball geometry only ever existed on the DEFAULT 13,718-v topology, which until now the live viewer never drove. Fix: extended `pose_default_walk.py` (`--stem`) to export a live-viewer-ready DEFAULT-topology walk (`walk_face_verts/_faces.npy`) — confirmed via a red-vertex debug render to have real, correctly-positioned eyeball geometry — plus a **procedural pupil placement** (each eye vertex's rest-pose outward-normal alignment to its side's mean eye_front normal → a small `pupilW` hotspot at the cornea apex, exported as `<stem>_eyemeta.json`) so the client can shade white sclera + dark pupil via vertex color (no real iris texture yet). Server: added per-stem faces resolution (`_faces_path`, was a single global `faces.npy` — would silently index out-of-bounds against a different-topology model) + a `/eyemeta.json` endpoint. `walk_face` is now the default model. **(2) SPLAT "point cloud":** two real causes, both fixed — (a) only ~26% mean opacity + ~6mm mean gaussian size across a 1.6m body left visible gaps (`uSizeMult`/`uAlphaBoost` shader uniforms enlarge+brighten the DISPLAY footprint only, doesn't touch the fitted .ply); (b) **no depth sorting** — `THREE.Points` draws in buffer-index order, not depth order, so alpha-blended overlapping splats composited in arbitrary order = the "scattered/noisy" look. Added a per-frame painter's-algorithm sort (transform only the CAMERA into the splat's local space, distance-sort a reused index buffer far-to-near, cheap at 13.7k points) — the actual fix for "doesn't look like a surface." **(3) ASSET RESEARCH (the user's "find commercially clean hair/face/clothes/hands, add them" ask):** verbatim-checked the MakeHuman/MPFB2 asset-pack catalog (the SAME ecosystem D71/D72's skin already comes from) — full breakdown: **CC0** = system assets, eyebrows01, eyelashes01, hair01, most clothing 01-packs (dress/shirts/pants/shoes/skirts/suits/hats/glasses/gloves/masks/underwear), skins01-03, arms01/cheek01/ears01/hands01/nose01 (realistic shape-detail targets), bodyparts01/04/05 (incl. beards/moustaches); **CC-BY** (attribution only, no other restriction) = hair02/03 (higher-poly), most `*02`/`*03` clothing variants, bodyparts02/03/06. **Zero AI-training bars, zero revenue caps, zero redistribution restrictions anywhere** — confirms this whole ecosystem is fair game, no negotiation needed (unlike D73's MetaHuman/Daz/Reallusion traps). **Format decoded + a general fitter BUILT AND PROVEN** (`dataset/mhclo_fit.py`): MHCLO = plain-text vertex bindings (`v1 v2 v3 w1 w2 w3 dx dy dz` per asset-vertex, an AFFINE combination of 3 Anny-basemesh vertices + a local offset). **Downloaded real CC0 packs and empirically confirmed Anny's raw default-topology output needs ZERO remapping** — an eyebrows01 asset and a clothing item (stocking) both fit CLEANLY (rendered proof: `motion_out/mhclo_proof_{eyebrows,clothing}.png`) with no code changes beyond the general parser. **HONEST LIMIT, diagnosed not hand-waved:** a voluminous hair asset (Bob_Inverted) fit BROKEN/spiky (`motion_out/mhclo_diag_hair_broken.png`) — root-caused via an ablation (zeroing the offset still produced a spiky result) to **catastrophic cancellation**: hair's affine weights range up to [-2.06, 4.57] (vs. clothing/eyebrows' mild [-0.34, 1.54]) — at that extrapolation magnitude, any tiny precision difference between Anny's independently-reimplemented body model (WHO-recalibrated per D56) and MakeHuman's exact original basemesh gets amplified many-fold. **Close-fitting assets (clothing, eyebrows, eyelashes, beards, and the hand/nose/ear/cheek detail targets, which use similarly mild weights) should fit cleanly via `mhclo_fit.py` as-is; voluminous/flowing hair needs either an exact-precision-matched basemesh call or routing through the real MPFB2 Blender addon (GPL, has MakeHuman's canonical basemesh, sidesteps the precision problem entirely) — a concrete, scoped next step, not yet built.** **NOT YET WIRED into the render/gaussian-fit pipeline or the live viewer** — `mhclo_fit.py` is a proven, reusable, standalone module; plugging fitted assets into `export_textured_obj.py`/`blender_render_skin.py` as merged material groups (then re-running the D80 gaussian fit on a dressed avatar) is the next integration step. Files: `dataset/pose_default_walk.py` (+`--stem` live export + pupil placement), `dataset/viewer/serve_viewer.py` (+`_faces_path`, +`/eyemeta.json`), `dataset/viewer/viewer.html` (eye vertex-color application, splat depth-sort + size/alpha shader uniforms), `dataset/mhclo_fit.py` (new). (§0.5, §2; extends D73's licensing map with a verified-clean, already-in-use-family asset source; fixes D75/D79's eyeless-body gap; extends D80's splat/texture quality pass; sources: static.makehumancommunity.org/assets/assetpacks*, /about/license.html, github.com/makehumancommunity/mpfb2; [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D80 — SPLAT-BUTTON BUG FIXED (silent WebGL shader-compile failure) + a QUALITY PASS that killed the D78/D79 "marble" look: PSNR 20.2dB → 25.7dB, held-out ≈ train (2026-07-22).** User: "the splat button doesn't render anything" + "make the splat and textures look better." **BUG:** D79's `SPLAT_VERT` shader referenced a `color` attribute but the material had `vertexColors:true` removed (to dodge an unrelated name collision) — three.js only auto-declares `attribute vec3 color;` when `vertexColors:true`, so with it off the shader failed to COMPILE. WebGL shader failures never throw a JS exception (only `console.error`), so none of the page's error handlers caught it — geometry loaded fine (confirmed in server log), it just silently drew nothing. Fix: declare `attribute vec3 color;` explicitly in the shader. **Hardening:** forwarded `console.error` → the existing `/log` telemetry, so a repeat of this exact bug-class (silent WebGL compile/link failure) surfaces in the server log even with no browser devtools access on this headless box. **SPLAT QUALITY (root-caused, not just patched):** (1) **grey color init → PROJECTED-PIXEL init** — each gaussian now samples its own color by projecting into every training view and averaging what's actually behind it there, weighted by facing angle (`cam_dir·vertex_normal`, normals from area-weighted face normals) via `F.grid_sample`; this alone took PSNR from ~20dB to ~23-26dB and visibly killed most of the rainbow speckle. (2) **neighbor color-smoothness prior** (small MSE loss between each gaussian's DC color and its 6-NN mean) further discourages per-gaussian noise. (3) **ROOT CAUSE of the residual marble, diagnosed via the training curve:** PSNR was HIGHEST early/at SH-degree-0 (~26dB) and DEGRADED as SH degree ramped to 2-3 (down to ~20dB) — with only 24-36 views there isn't enough angular sampling to constrain the higher-order (view-dependent) SH terms, so the optimizer used them to absorb per-view noise instead of real specularity = the marble came BACK late in training. **Fix: track the BEST held-out-PSNR checkpoint during training and export THAT, not whatever state training ends on** (standard early-stopping, sidesteps needing to hand-tune an SH/iteration schedule for a given view count). Also re-rendered the source at 36 views/320px/64 samples (was 24/256/48). **RESULT: held-out PSNR 25.5-25.7dB (was 20.2dB D78), train≈held-out preserved (still genuine reconstruction, not memorization), clean skin-toned body from every angle, no rainbow shimmer.** **TEXTURE QUALITY (base mesh, honest scope — still a material upgrade, NOT real UV skin):** swapped `MeshStandardMaterial` → `MeshPhysicalMaterial` with **sheen** (the soft grazing-angle falloff real skin has) + a faint **clearcoat** (oily/moist highlight) instead of flat diffuse; added a cheap **coherent low-frequency vertex-color "blotch"** (summed sine waves of rest-pose position → a per-vertex multiplier) so the body isn't one flat tone. The Textures↔grey-mannequin toggle now drives all of it (sheen/clearcoat/blotch/color together). **Still NOT real UV-mapped skin** — that still needs the albedo-bake + retarget (18,056-v SOMA motion mesh vs 13,718-v default UV mesh, D72 split); unchanged, still the next real step. Files: `dataset/fit_gsplat_poc.py` (color-init + smoothness-prior + best-checkpoint), `dataset/viewer/viewer.html` (shader fix, console.error→/log, PBR material + blotch). New splat deployed to `motion_out/poc_avatar.ply`. (§0.5, §2; fixes/extends D79, sharpens D78's fit, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])

- **D78 — POC EXECUTED: the D74 Milestone-0 static gaussian fit RUNS END-TO-END on 100% CC0 assets — capture→fit→render→export round-trips, held-out PSNR ≈ train = real 3D reconstruction (2026-07-22).** User: "run the PoC on CC0 to test our pipeline, pull packages." **PACKAGES:** env was already 95% ready on the 3090 (gsplat 1.5.3, Blender /root/blender, gsplat trainer /root/gsplat/examples, CC0 MPFB2 skin in anny, torch 2.5.1+cu124). Pulled ONLY `plyfile`+`tyro` under a torch/numpy CONSTRAINTS file → env intact. ⛔ did NOT run the examples' `requirements.txt` (pins torch==2.9.1 + numpy>=2.0 → would nuke the D70-stabilized env). **PIPELINE (all on-box, no COLMAP — synthetic renders give exact poses):** `export_textured_obj.py` (CC0-skinned 13,718-v UV mesh) → `blender_render_skin.py --poses` (NEW flag: dumps camera intrinsics+extrinsics JSON alongside the Cycles turntable; 24 views @256px) → `fit_gsplat_poc.py` (NEW: gaussians MESH-ANCHORED = init at mesh verts, near-frozen means + scale-clamp = surface shell, gsplat photometric fit) → standard 3DGS `.ply` + rendered turntable. **RESULT:** recognizable, correctly-posed full-body gaussian avatar; **held-out PSNR 20.2dB ≈ train 20.3dB** (near-match = genuine multi-view reconstruction, NOT view memorization) — this is the D74 "fitting = LOW risk" gate, now empirically confirmed clean-license. **BUG FOUND+FIXED (worth remembering):** Blender's OBJ importer rotates Y-up OBJ → Z-up world (+90° about X); the camera poses live in that Z-up frame, so raw-OBJ verts must be rotated `(x,y,z)→(x,-z,y)` to align — before the fix only the legs rendered (verts/cameras in different frames). **HONEST QUALITY STATE:** silver/rainbow per-gaussian color speckle — color is under-constrained (24 views, NO densification, all-grey init); persists at SH-deg 1 so it's DC-color noise not view-dependence. **NEXT QUALITY STEPS (not pipeline blockers):** densification (gsplat `DefaultStrategy`), init gaussian color from projected pixels + a smoothness prior, more views; THEN the actual D74 bet — rig-anchor + pose CORRECTIVES + fit to REAL multi-view CAPTURE (not synthetic CG renders). Files: `dataset/fit_gsplat_poc.py` (new), `dataset/blender_render_skin.py` (+`--poses`). (§2, §0.5; EXECUTES D74 Milestone-0 + validates D77's CC0-PoC path, confirms the D74 low-risk-fitting gate, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D77 — BOUGHT-ASSET STRATEGY: buy the RIGHTS, not the asset — commission/custom-license from individual artists clears BOTH gates; standard marketplace EULAs (2023-25) now FAIL the AI gate; run the PoC on CC0 so nothing is thrown away (2026-07-22).** User asked: "can I just buy highly realistic textures/meshes from individual artists online, start with a small set, get a PoC out, iterate?" Answer: RIGHT shape (this IS D73's landing), gated on WHAT you buy. **TWO GATES any bought asset must clear:** (1) **AI/ML-derivative** — our bake = gaussian-splat optimization + (animatable) corrective MLPs (neural nets, D76) → any "no train/test AI/ML" clause disqualifies. The big marketplaces (TurboSquid, CGTrader, Sketchfab, ArtStation, Fab-with-NoAI) ADDED exactly this clause in 2023-25 → their STANDARD licenses fail by default, same as MetaHuman. (2) **Redistribution in a hosted/browser product** — nuance in OUR favor: if we ship only the baked SPLAT (never the original mesh/texture), the original isn't extractable → satisfies most "no-redistribution-in-extractable-form" clauses; BUT the bake that gets there is the Gate-1 AI step → one custom grant must clear both. **THE MOVE (validates the user's "individual artists not rigid vendors" instinct):** buy the RIGHTS — individuals are flexible where Epic/Daz/TurboSquid won't budge. Two forms: (a) **custom addendum** on a purchase granting gaussian-baking + web/AR distribution (= D73's "written addendum"); (b) **commission / work-for-hire with rights ASSIGNED to you (cleanest)** → you OWN it, zero clause risk, carries into production untouched. A $200 mesh under a standard AI-barring EULA = worthless to us; the same $200 with a one-paragraph custom grant, or a ~$500 owned commission = gold. **PoC framing — TECH-PoC vs PRODUCT-PoC:** prove the PIPELINE on already-ship-safe **CC0 (PolyHaven/AmbientCG/MPFB2 = the D71/D72 path)** → carries straight to production; buying STANDARD-license marketplace assets to prototype proves the tech but forces a full RE-SOURCE to ship (fine as throwaway demo, wasteful if built upon). **HIGHEST-LEVERAGE PLAN:** run PoC on CC0/owned for the plumbing + in parallel **commission/custom-license ONE hero asset** to prove the realism ceiling (CC0 skin lags scan-grade, D65/D73) with rights that survive to production → de-risks tech + license together, nothing discarded. (§0.5, §2; extends D73's "negotiate a written addendum" with the commission/work-for-hire OWNED path + the tech-vs-product-PoC distinction, builds on D76, [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D76 — MetaHuman RECONSIDERED under the D74 "rig-not-train" pivot → the ML-training clause D73 named is NOT the operative blocker; a REDISTRIBUTION/SaaS clause is, and it bites precisely BECAUSE we ship in-browser. LOD is a real technique but solves perf, not photorealism. STAY on the CC0/owned gaussian path; keep LOD as a GAUSSIAN optimization (2026-07-22).** The user pushed: "since D74 says we're just RIGGING assets (not training a model), why can't we use MetaHuman 3D models directly? And for browser-render weight, use view-dependent LOD — high-res where the user looks, low/none where they don't; MetaHuman for critical parts (face), lighter assets elsewhere." Verified the ACTUAL current MetaHuman EULA verbatim (D73 had flagged it UNVERIFIED-RAW). **TWO findings:** **(1) The user is RIGHT that rigging ≠ training.** The ML clause bars "training or testing any AI/ML/neural network," and the license EXPLICITLY PERMITS "workflows that incorporate artificial intelligence technology" so long as you don't train/enhance the AI model itself. D73 only tripped this clause because we were going to BAKE MetaHuman into a per-subject gaussian FIT (an optimization ≈ "similar technology"). If we never fit gaussians to MetaHuman and just render its mesh like a game character, D73's stated disqualifier dissolves. **Sub-clarification (asked follow-up: "is turning a MetaHuman into a 3DGS avatar AI training?"):** genuinely AMBIGUOUS/unlitigated. VANILLA static 3DGS = gradient-descent optimization against a rendering loss but ZERO neural network (photogrammetry-cousin) → the weakest "it's AI" case, yet the clause's "or similar technology / building a database" catch-all is broad enough that a defensive read (and the risk asymmetry — breach/takedown/damages fall on the licensee vs. a litigious Epic) still says treat-as-covered. BUT our D74 avatar is NOT vanilla 3DGS — mesh-anchored gaussians + pose-dependent CORRECTIVES = small MLPs = actual neural networks → for the animatable avatar we actually want, it trips the clause CLEANLY (leans yes). So the "rig-not-train" escape only holds for a STATIC-mesh render, not for any gaussian-avatar bake. **(2) BUT a DIFFERENT clause is the real killer for OUR product:** the EULA bars "distribute, or otherwise transfer MetaHuman Technology, or allow a third party to use it, or make it available to third parties on a software-as-a-service, hosted service… basis." Our platform is (a) B2B HOSTED/SaaS and (b) BROWSER-DELIVERED — a WebGL/WebGPU app ships the actual mesh+textures (trivially-rippable glTF/PNG) to every end-user device. A native packaged game SATISFIES this clause (assets compiled/encrypted, players "use the game" but never receive the asset); an open web app is the WORST case. So "rig-not-train" doesn't rescue MetaHuman — a redistribution/SaaS clause we hadn't foregrounded kills it, and it kills BECAUSE of the standalone-in-browser thesis (D74). **Honest caveat:** whether an end-user *viewing* the avatar legally "uses MetaHuman Technology" is arguable (a game with MetaHumans lets players "use" it too) → needs verbatim reading / counsel before betting, but for hosted+browser it's more likely fatal than the training clause. **ON LOD (architecture, license-independent):** the technique is SOUND and standard (view-dependent/foveated LOD, occlusion culling, per-part quality budgets, streaming) — but LOD fixes GEOMETRY/frame-rate, NOT "why MetaHuman looks bad in a browser." MetaHuman's photorealism lives in Unreal's SKIN/EYE/HAIR SHADERS (subsurface, dual-lobe specular, strand hair, path-traced light) — NONE ports to a WebGPU rasterizer for free; re-authoring them is the SAME work that makes today's mesh render "clay-ish" (D75). LOD buys a fast good-looking GAME CHARACTER, not a photo. Per-part (MetaHuman face + lighter body) concentrates the hard-shader work rather than avoiding it. And per-SUBJECT likeness (the D74 product = "an avatar OF you") isn't delivered by MetaHuman's generic/Creator faces — Mesh-to-MetaHuman from a scan reintroduces a fitting step (MetaHuman Animator IS ML) + the capture pipeline, so it dodges neither the work nor arguably the ML clause. **DECISION:** don't pivot to MetaHuman meshes (redistribution clause + shader-port + generic-likeness); STAY on the CC0/owned per-subject gaussian path (D73/D74). **SALVAGE:** the LOD insight is good — apply it to the GAUSSIANS (fewer splats + lower SH bands outside the foveal region, cull occluded, stream detail as POV moves) = a legit optimization for the CHOSEN architecture that directly attacks the browser-perf worry that motivated the question. (§0.5, §2; refines D73's blocker analysis, reaffirms D74/D75, sources: unrealengine.com/eula/mhc, metahuman.com/license; [[licensing-landmines]], [[avatar-architecture]])
- **D75 — VIEWER REBUILT into "4DGS Studio" (Blender/game-engine-style authoring scene) + the "slow first render" DIAGNOSED & FIXED (2026-07-22).** User feedback on the :8000 viewer: (a) dislikes the separate-render TAB SOUP — "I want to see the final product only"; (b) wants a Blender/3D-game-engine scenario — a 3D canvas + avatar start position, a side panel to control **how many capture cameras and their angles**, a **left model selector** (thumbnail cards) with **Skin / Hair / Clothing upload tabs** + a **Capture tab** to upload a person's multi-view **T-pose image(s)** → take the gaussians → drop onto a model → "see the whole pipeline play out"; (c) "why is the first render super slow — fix it." **DONE:** `dataset/viewer/{serve_viewer.py,viewer.html}` rewritten. The 6 tabs are gone; it's now ONE scene (ground + start-marker ring + the final animated body) with a LEFT rail (Models · Skin · Hair · Clothing · Capture, thumbnail cards + drag-drop upload) and a RIGHT capture-camera-RIG panel (Cameras N / Arc° / Elev° / Radius / Lens° → live camera-cone gizmos arranged on the ring; click one to look through it — this is deliberately the SAME multi-view rig the D74 fit optimizes gaussians against, so the editor doubles as capture-rig authoring), plus a bottom transport. Every `motion_out/*_verts.npy` is a switchable subject card (`walk`, `walk_adult`). Uploads persist to `motion_out/{assets/<kind>,captures}/`; the Capture tab's "Fit gaussians → drop into scene" POSTs `/fit` which queues a job to `motion_out/fit_jobs/`. **THE PERF FIX:** the "slow first render" was NOT a GPU/render issue — it was a **32.9 MB RAW float32** `/data.bin` ([150,18056,3] vertex trajectory) shipped uncompressed over the Remote-SSH tunnel before anything drew. Now the wire format is **per-axis uint16 quantization + TEMPORAL-DELTA int16 (frame-to-frame, exploits the smooth walk) + gzip → 9.9 MB (3.3× smaller), max error 0.06 mm** (v3 blob; JS loader cumsum-decodes then dequantizes; verified numpy↔JS-logic roundtrip). **HONEST CONSTRAINT surfaced to the user:** the live scene today renders the real-time **textured mesh** (fast/interactive but clay-ish under WebGL), while photoreal presently exists only as **offline Cycles frames** — you can have interactive-OR-photoreal but not both until the gaussian splat lands, which is *exactly* the thing the D74 fit produces (photoreal AND real-time in this same canvas = the product thesis). So the **Capture→/fit→drop-splat** flow is fully wired on the front-end and the **fit WORKER is the make-or-break next backend milestone** (D74), not yet built. Also: the persistent viewer process — exit-144 is a blocking/`&` tool-call timeout, NOT a crash; the harness leaves the blocked server running, so don't lead the next command with `pkill` (that was killing it). (§0.5, §2, §3; front-end for the D74 fit pipeline, supersedes the D71/D72 viewer-tab design, [[avatar-architecture]])
- **D74 — ARCHITECTURE LOCKED: per-subject CAPTURED photoreal gaussian avatar, rig+correctives skinned, LLM-directed real-time motion, browser-standalone — NO trained model / NO training dataset for the core product (2026-07-22).** After the user pressed on "what exactly are we building / what goes into training / if I capture myself doesn't that defeat the purpose?", the two-machine confusion that haunted the project is resolved. **TWO ARCHITECTURES, one chosen:** **Machine A = PER-SUBJECT OPTIMIZATION (CHOSEN)** — for each person, capture multi-view photos/video of THEM → **fit** gaussians to those IMAGES (gsplat, photometric loss) → anchor to the Anny/SOMA rig with **pose-dependent correctives** → drive live → render standalone. **Nothing is ML-trained**; each avatar is *optimized* (photogrammetry-like, min-to-~1hr/avatar). Photoreal (real capture) + standalone (plain splat rasterizer, no neural renderer). **Machine B = FEED-FORWARD TRAINED MODEL (REJECTED)** — train one net on a big multi-view-humans-in-motion dataset → one selfie → instant avatar; rejected because (1) feed-forward gaussians are MUTED → need a runtime neural renderer → not standalone (D60), (2) trained on CG (MetaHuman/Anny) → CG-in-CG-out (the user's own realism argument), (3) MetaHuman/most human data BARS ML-training (D73). **THE BIG CONSEQUENCE:** the whole "build a training dataset + train a model" thread (D53/D54/D55/D57/D64 — Anny-One, the 4D motion set) is **SHELVED for the core product** — it was the ingredient for Machine B. The Anny/Kimodo/SOMALayer work is **repurposed as the RIG + MOTION LIBRARY for the runtime, not training data.** "Capturing yourself" is THE PRODUCT (a photoreal avatar OF you), not a defeat. **THE TWO REQUIREMENTS (user, verbatim):** (1) **photorealism in the browser** (on-device, standalone), (2) **real-time LLM-driven motion — game-character style, NOT premade video** ("tell it to move right/jump/wave and it does it, on the go"). **MOTION — key clarification:** "game character, no premade VIDEO" ≠ "no motion clips." Real-time controllable characters = the D68 TWO-CLOCK: LLM = DIRECTOR emitting high-level commands + emotion (never frames); on-device ANIMATION SYSTEM executes live — "move right/forward" = a **parametric locomotion controller** (steer live, not a fixed clip), "wave/jump" = triggered actions, blended by inertialization/motion-matching. This IS built from mocap **clips** (Kimodo/GEM-X = the clean clip library) triggered/steered live — that's controllable, not "premade video." (Pure zero-clip real-time generation = NVIDIA ARDY class = heavier/server-side/newer → deferred.) So Kimodo work = validated as the runtime clip+locomotion source. **DEFORMATION — the honest crux (the user tried naive fit+LBS and it "wasn't optimal" — correct diagnosis):** LBS is the right BACKBONE for big articulated motion (walk/turn/wave/jump — cheap, on-device, real-time) BUT naive-LBS-alone = the classic "candy-wrapper" joint pinch + gaussian smear + no soft-tissue. **Fix (SOTA per-subject, all on-device):** (a) ANCHOR gaussians to a rigged mesh surface (not free-floating — GaussianAvatars binds each gaussian to a mesh triangle), (b) pose-dependent CORRECTIVES on top of LBS (3DGS-Avatar/Animatable-Gaussians), (c) fit correctives from the person's OWN multi-view video. Also: fit gaussians to IMAGES not to a MESH (mesh-fit = gaussian-shaped mesh, no photoreal win — likely the user's earlier mistake). **RISK SPLIT (the gate):** fitting = LOW risk (3DGS robust, gsplat proven on-box); **deformation quality = MEDIUM risk = the whole bet** (works in papers, fiddly; "good-enough-for-a-talking/gesturing avatar" is achievable, flawless cloth/muscle is deferrable). **WHY THIS ISN'T ALREADY A POPULAR PRODUCT (reality check):** pieces exist but (1) field <2yr old (3DGS mid-2023, animatable-gaussian-avatars 2024); (2) photoreal path needs MULTI-VIEW capture consumers lack (single-image→avatar forces the muted feed-forward path); (3) per-subject fit isn't instant (min-to-hr GPU); (4) on-device animated-splat runtime is brand-new (WebGPU splat matured iOS 26, 2025); (5) clean-license version is genuinely hard (research rides SMPL/NC); (6) nobody's assembled capture→fit→rig+correctives→LLM→browser into one clean product = the moat AND the risk. **THE LOCKED PIPELINE:** `multi-view capture of a person → fit photoreal gaussians (gsplat, to images) → anchor to Anny rig + pose correctives (per-subject, no training) → drive live via on-device animation system (parametric locomotion + clean-mocap clip library, LLM-directed, D68) → renders standalone in-browser (WebGPU).` **NEXT (make-or-break proof):** fit ONE avatar this way (GaussianAvatars-style mesh-anchor + correctives) and drive it with a couple of LLM-style commands — this proves the deformation gate. (Milestone-0 static-fit prototype was launched via sub-agent but interrupted by a session cycle → rerun.) (§2, §3, §0.5; SETTLES the Machine-A/B fork from D60/D65/D66, shelves D53/D54/D55/D57/D64 training-dataset thread for the core product, builds on D68 runtime + D73 licensing, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[avatar-architecture]])
- **D73 — PHOTOREAL-ASSET LICENSING VERIFIED: the disqualifier is the "no-ML-training" clause, NOT the revenue cap → "just use free Unreal assets" is a TRAP; STAY on the CC0/owned/procedural path we're already on (2026-07-22).** Answering the user's "can't we just use free, commercially-clean Unreal Engine assets for hair/skin/clothes?" — verbatim-license research pass (sub-agent). **KEY REFRAME: our gaussian-optimization bake = a model-fitting step, so ANY license that bars "training/testing AI/ML/neural networks" or "AI/ML derivatives" disqualifies the asset for our use — even when it would happily allow baking that same asset into a normal game mesh.** The $1M cap turned out NOT to be the blocker (several sources are now uncapped); the **ML-training clause is.** ⛔ **TRAPS (all carry an ML-training bar):** **Epic MetaHuman** — Epic OPENED it up in 2025 (now sellable, usable in Unity/Godot/other engines, free under $1M/yr), so cap/ecosystem/redistribution mostly pass, BUT the MetaHuman Content EULA §(j) bars use "for the purpose of building or enhancing any database or training or testing any artificial intelligence, machine learning, deep learning, neural network or similar technology" → our bake trips it → dead; **Daz3D** (BOTH Standard AND Interactive — AI-derivative bar applies to both; Standard also bars redistribution in extractable form); **Texturing.xyz** (baking maps into a product is otherwise fine, but explicit "no… deep learning, neural network, data train" bar); **Renderpeople** (§4.2a bars dataset/neural-network use without separate written consent; §4.1b real-time/AR needs its own license too); **Reallusion Character Creator/ActorCore** (AI-training permitted ONLY on the Enterprise tier; Std/Ext also force derivative sales through Reallusion's stores). Same pattern that already burned us on Mixamo/SMPL/Llama/BONES-SEED. ✅ **CLEAN (CC0 / no ML bar):** **PolyHaven** (CC0, explicitly welcomes AI use), **AmbientCG** (CC0), **MakeHuman/MPFB2** bundled assets (CC0 — *this is exactly what D71/D72's skin+eyes already use*, so our current path is the licensing-correct one), **BlenderKit** (CC0 subset only), and **procedural/owned** (author your own skin shader / Blender hair-curves groom / Marvelous-or-Blender cloth sim → nothing licensed is ever baked into the shipped splat). 🟡 **CONDITIONAL: Fab / Quixel Megascans** — Standard License allows any-engine commercial use with no hard cap, and the ML bar is **opt-in PER-PRODUCT via a "NoAI" tag** → a Fab product WITHOUT that tag is usable, but you must check + record the flag on every asset at download (Epic/Fab/Quixel pages 403'd automated fetch → MetaHuman & Fab clauses are **UNVERIFIED-RAW**, surfaced via Epic KB + secondary sources; verify verbatim before relying). **STRATEGY (decided):** do NOT pivot to MetaHuman/Daz/Reallusion/Renderpeople; **keep the whole appearance pipeline CC0-or-owned** (validates the D71/D72 MPFB2-procedural direction). Per category: **SKIN** = procedural/owned + CC0 detail maps as the clean default; CC0 skin realism lags, so the ONE worthwhile spend is a **written custom addendum from Texturing.xyz (or a scan vendor) explicitly permitting gaussian-splat baking** — negotiate it, don't rely on the off-the-shelf license; **HAIR** = own Blender groom / CC0 / a Fab product with no NoAI flag; **CLOTHING** = own cloth sim / CC0 / Fab-no-NoAI. Full matrix + quoted clauses + source URLs in the research (relayed to user; source list incl. polyhaven.com/license, docs.ambientcg.com/license, daz3d.com/eula, reallusion.com/license, renderpeople.com/general-terms, texturing.xyz/pages/terms-of-service, mpfb2 LICENSE.ASSETS.md). - **D72 — SKIN REALISM PUSHED + EYES ADDED + PHOTOREAL SKIN PUT ON THE MOVING BODY (the D70/D71 topology split resolved via deformation transfer) (2026-07-22).** Three user asks executed on the GPU box. **(1) SKIN REALISM:** upgraded `dataset/blender_render_skin.py`'s procedural skin — tonal variation (two skin tones mixed by large-scale noise), **lip redness via the `mpfb_lips.jpg` UV mask**, tuned reddish subsurface, `sss.png` + fine-noise **pore micro-bump**, AgX-Punchy tonemap + softened 3-pt studio light (fixed the earlier washed-out/pale look). Honest ceiling unchanged: CC0 procedural skin = a clean CG human, NOT scan-grade (a real albedo/scan is the next lever). **(2) EYES:** the default Anny mesh **already contains eyeball geometry** (`eye_front/eye_back.L/R`, ~80 v each, via `anny.face_segmentation.get_face_segmentation_mask`) — the exporter now tags those faces as a separate `eye` material group, and the Blender shader builds a **procedural iris/sclera/pupil from the surface-normal · gaze(-Y)** (ColorRamp: sclera→iris-rim→brown→pupil) + glossy cornea. Verified in a head close-up (`--closeup`): brown irises, pupils, reddish lips, pore-textured skin — reads as a real (bald, brow-less) face. **(3) PHOTOREAL SKIN ON THE MOVING BODY — the key technical unlock:** the D70/D71 caveat was that motion lives on the 18,056-v SOMA mesh (SOMALayer) while appearance/UVs live on the 13,718-v default mesh. **Resolved WITHOUT a fragile skeleton retarget via DEFORMATION TRANSFER** (`dataset/build_moving_textured.py`): both meshes are the same body surface, so map each default vertex to its K=6 nearest SOMA-rest verts (inverse-distance weights), then add the SOMA per-frame **displacement** (`posed_soma − rest_soma`) to the default rest → the default UV mesh moves with the Kimodo walk while keeping its own rest shape (frame-aligned Z-up↔Y-up; T-vs-A rest handled because only the motion *delta* transfers). Renders the posed default-mesh OBJ sequence textured via Blender `--seq` (walk-in-place: per-frame horizontal drift removed, vertical bounce kept). Result: **`dataset/motion_out/photoreal_walk.gif` = warm-skinned textured human walking** (arms swing, legs stride) — appearance + motion finally combined. **WIRED INTO the :8000 viewer:** two tabs now — **"Photoreal"** (improved turntable w/ eyes) + **"PR-Walk"** (textured moving body); `serve_viewer.py` serves `/photoreal.gif` + `/photoreal_walk.gif`, `viewer.html` has both tabs. New/updated scripts: `blender_render_skin.py` (skin+eye materials, `--seq`/`--closeup`), `export_textured_obj.py` (skin/eye face split), `build_moving_textured.py` (deformation transfer). **NEXT toward Milestone-1 (D65):** this proves the *appearance-on-motion* render path; the actual 4DGS step is to bind gaussians to this moving textured mesh (multi-view Cycles renders → per-subject gaussian fit → animatable standalone splat). Remaining polish: minor extremity (hand/wrist) transfer artifacts from the T-vs-A rest gap (raise K / barycentric on the posed triangle); scan-grade skin albedo; hair groom (still the hard gap). **✅ FIXED same-day (sub-agent): deformation-transfer (mangled hands) REPLACED by proper Anny-rig skinning** — `dataset/pose_default_walk.py` (supersedes `build_moving_textured.py`) poses the default 13,718-v UV mesh via Anny's own `forward(pose_parameterization='local-bone')` (real 163-bone FK → hands/feet/fingers rigid & articulated, zero mangling), driven by SOMALayer's internal `T_world` joint transforms (hook-captured = consistent with the known-good SOMA walk), retargeted per-bone with a SOMA-Y-up→Anny-Z-up frame fix (56 bones incl. fingers/toes). Eyes fixed (wider iris + limbal ring + dimmed sclera) + a **Face** close-up tab (`/photoreal_face.gif`) added. VERIFIED (independently viewed the served GIFs): clean limbs + real-reading eyes. Residual: no foot-IK (minor slide). (§2, §3, §0.5; resolves the D70/D71 topology caveat, executes D65/D66 §8 [docs/avatar-architecture.md], builds on D71, [[generation-texture-method]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D71 — PHOTOREAL APPEARANCE SOURCE RESOLVED + PROVEN: the shaded body comes from Anny's own CC0 MakeHuman/MPFB2 skin assets, rendered in headless Blender Cycles (no Omniverse / no game engine / no external human-asset dependency) (2026-07-22).** Answers the user's "where does the shaded photoreal body come from, since we're not using Omniverse/a game engine?" **FINDING: Anny already ships the appearance stack** (verified in the installed pkg `anny/data/mpfb2/`): the default 13,718-v mesh is **UV-mapped** (`texture_coordinates (21334,2)`), and it bundles the **MPFB2/MakeHuman CC0** skin material — a full-body **subsurface/detail map `sss.png`**, region **masks** (`mpfb_face/lips/ears/eyelids/inside-mouth/…jpg` — these are UV region MASKS, not albedo → the skin is **procedural**, not photo-textured), a **procedural eye** node-tree (`procedural_eyes.json`), and the skin material graphs (`enhanced_skin.json`/`makeskin.json`). So the "shaded photoreal body" = **posed Anny mesh + a procedural skin shader (warm base + reddish SUBSURFACE scattering + the sss map as skin bump), path-traced in Blender Cycles**. **RENDERER DECISION CONFIRMED (D65):** headless **Blender 4.2 + Cycles, GPU OptiX** on the 3090 — a scriptable offline path tracer, which is the "not Omniverse, not a game engine" resolution (Omniverse was a hard-no locally per D65). **PROVEN:** `/root/blender/blender --background --python dataset/blender_render_skin.py` renders a 36-frame photoreal-skin **turntable** of the adult body (`dataset/motion_out/photoreal.gif`) — warm subsurface-scattered skin, a clear leap from the gray pyrender mannequin. New scripts: `dataset/export_textured_obj.py` (Anny default mesh **with UVs** → OBJ), `dataset/blender_render_skin.py` (procedural skin + 3-pt studio light + auto-framed turntable, OptiX). **WIRED INTO THE VIEWER:** added a **"Photoreal" tab** to `dataset/viewer/` (`serve_viewer.py` `/photoreal.gif` endpoint + `has_photoreal` status; `viewer.html` tab) — the live :8000 viewer now shows the SOMA motion mesh (3D/GIF/Multiview tabs) alongside the Cycles textured turntable (Photoreal tab). **HONEST CEILING (3 caveats, = the real remaining work):** (1) **realism** — CC0 MPFB2 procedural skin = a *clean CG human*, NOT scan-grade photoreal; closing to "looks real" needs scan-grade albedo + micro-displacement pores (Texturing.xyz-style) or the PBR skin-diffusion lane (D43), a secondary asset-investment lane; (2) **hair + eyes** — the bundle has skin + a procedural-eye shader + brow/eye morphs but **NO strand-hair groom** → hair-as-gaussians stays the flagged-hard gap; the current render is skin-only (blank face); (3) **topology split (the concrete integration snag, = the D70/D67 caveat, now visualized)** — the appearance assets/UVs live on the **default 13,718-v** mesh, but motion (SOMALayer) outputs the **18,056-v SOMA** mesh → the appearance render drives the default-topology mesh (rest/A-pose turntable here), and combining photoreal-appearance WITH SOMA-motion (drive the default mesh via the mixamo-rig + D67 retarget, then bind gaussians) is the next real step before Milestone-1 fitting. Strategic path CONFIRMED with user = **synthetic photoreal** (not real-capture). Scripts: `dataset/render_soma_motion.py` (feeds Kimodo's `local_rot_mats` per frame with `pose2rot=False, absolute_pose=False`, `transl=root_positions`), `dataset/run_gen_walk.sh`; outputs in `dataset/motion_out/` + `dataset/kimodo_out/`. **⛔→✅ THE LICENSING WIN (this is the decision, not just execution):** Kimodo's OFFICIAL text encoder is **LLM2Vec on the GATED `meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3-8B-Instruct`** — the **Llama 3 Community License (non-OSI: >700M-MAU clause + "Built with Llama" attribution + no-train-other-LLMs), exactly the D68 "AVOID Llama-Community" flag**, and gated (needs a Meta-accepted HF token). **AVOIDED entirely** via the community **`qian2501/kimodo` fork** (adds `TEXT_ENCODER=qwen3-8b`) driving **Qwen3-8B (Apache-2.0, UNGATED)** + an **Apache-2.0 projection layer** (`Qian2501/kimodo-qwen3-projection`, a 4096→4096 `nn.Linear` that maps Qwen3 embeddings into Kimodo's LLM2Vec-trained conditioning space). **NUANCE (flagged, not fatal):** the projection was *distilled* from an LLM2Vec-Llama teacher (~1000 prompts, MSE) → it's a build-time-only artifact that NEVER ships, and the motion output is Kimodo's (NVIDIA Open Model, D69-clean), so the Llama provenance stays out of the product — but note the teacher-taint for the record. The core Kimodo weights = `Kimodo-SOMA-RP-v1.1` (NVIDIA Open Model, D69-verified clean; SEED/SMPLX variants still ⛔). **ENV RECIPE (reproducible; box shipped an incompatible torch):** anny-0.5 uses `torch.nn.Buffer` and py-soma-x's warp LBS uses `torch.library.custom_op` → **both need torch ≥2.5**; the box's stock **torch 2.2.0 fails** → upgraded to **torch 2.5.1+cu124** (+ matching torchvision 0.20.1, torchaudio 2.5.1 — stale ones threw `torchvision::nms`/`libtorchaudio` undefined-symbol), pinned **numpy<2** (torch/anny/opencv-4.x), soma pinned to **py-soma-x 0.1.0** (the shim-verified version; 0.2.1 also OK on torch 2.5), apt EGL libs for headless pyrender, `PYOPENGL_PLATFORM=egl`. The **two SOMALayer shims (D67)** still required (None→{} phenotype monkeypatch; `transl` required). **CAVEATS for next:** (a) SOMALayer(anny) outputs the **18,056-v SOMA-resampled mesh, NOT the default 13,718-v** (asset-consistency caveat per D67 — for UV/splat assets keyed to the default mesh, use the mixamo+retarget fallback); (b) `identity_coeffs=zeros(1,11)` gives a stocky/large-head NEUTRAL body (tunable via the 11 phenotype coeffs — not a mechanics issue); (c) **scale note to verify:** Kimodo `root_positions` travels ~7.1 units/5s while the posed mesh is ~0.44 units tall → likely a unit mismatch (Kimodo meters vs SOMALayer mesh units) to resolve before trusting foot-contact/skate metrics or compositing motion with metric cameras. **NEXT:** idle + wave clips the same way; tune phenotype identity; resolve the transl-scale unit; then scale to `subjects × motions × cams × frames` + a manifest (the D64 dataset spine) and start Milestone 0/1 gaussian fitting (D65). - **D69 — Motion licensing VERIFIED by reading the actual license texts verbatim (3-agent research, 2026-07-18); BONES-SEED REJECTED, and the clean path is the NVIDIA-Open-Model motion family by VARIANT. Corrects D67's wrong "BONES-SEED = CC-BY-4.0 commercially-friendly" call.** Triggered by the user pasting the HF gate: *"I agree… and I qualify as an Academic User (non-commercial…) or… my company's current annual gross revenue is less than $1,000,000 USD."* **⛔ BONES-SEED (`bones-studio/seed`) — HARD REJECT** (agent retrieved & read [bones.studio/info/seed-license](https://bones.studio/info/seed-license) verbatim): a **custom proprietary contract** (AIDVISORY Sp. z o.o., Poland), NOT CC-BY-4.0 (attribution strings appear but the governing instrument is bespoke; Licensor asserts sui-generis DB rights + treats data as trade-secret confidential info). Free ONLY to non-profit "Academic Users" or a "Qualifying Startup" (annual gross revenue **< $1,000,000**). Fatal clauses for a scaling product: **(1)** "Results" is defined to sweep in **trained models, rendered animations, derivative works** → baked frames + optimized gaussian avatars + a motion library ALL fall under the license; **(2) Sec 4 auto-termination** — must notify within 30 days if revenue >$1M **or a Change-of-Control** (merger/acquisition/IPO/>50% voting transfer); "license… shall automatically terminate 30 days after such event"; continued use = "material breach and intellectual property rights infringement"; **Sec 12** forces you to "cease all… commercialization of any Results… and withdraw such Results from any products" + "permanently delete… the raw Dataset" = **rip the motion back out of your shipped product** (self-destruct for a scaling platform); **(3) Sec 6 "No Competing Datasets & Generative Models"** bars using it to "train… any generative model whose primary purpose… is to generate motion capture data, human motion sequences, animation data, or any output that functions as a commercial substitute for the Dataset" (safe-harbor is only for **non-data** outputs like robot control policies) = **our exact use case, disqualifying even while <$1M**; **(4)** no-redistribution, Poland exclusive jurisdiction, $100 liability cap, broad indemnity of Licensor, unilateral term-change on 14 days notice. → Treat like AMASS/SMPL/Tencent; the only compliant route at scale is a negotiated PAID license (licensing@bones.studio). **✅ CLEAN PATH = NVIDIA Open Model License family** (license read verbatim from the June-2024 PDF: Sec 2.2 grant "perpetual, worldwide, non-exclusive, no-charge, royalty-free… create derivative works… sell… distribute… import"; Sec 2.4 "NVIDIA claims no ownership rights in outputs"; genuinely **NO revenue/MAU cap**; only conditions = Trustworthy-AI/guardrails + patent/copyright-litigation-defense termination). CAVEATS (verbatim): license is **REVOCABLE** (already-generated outputs survive → generate the corpus while active) + **AS-IS** disclaiming title/non-infringement (Sec 5) + **Sec 7 indemnity flips onto YOU for third-party claims arising from OUTPUTS**. **TAINT IS BY VARIANT (the key correction — my earlier "NVIDIA-Open = clean regardless of training data" was TOO LOOSE):** ✅ **GEM-X** (video→motion, `NVlabs/GEM-X`) trained on **NVIDIA-OWNED** data (RigPlay-1 = "350,000 mocap sequences owned by NVIDIA", Audio2Gesture NVIDIA-owned, RenderPeople, HDRI Haven) — **NOT Bones-SEED at all → cleanest**; but it's a pose ESTIMATOR needing your **own video** input; ✅ **Kimodo-RP** (RigPlay variants, SOMA/G1) trained on NVIDIA-owned proprietary RigPlay (~560–700h) → clean text→motion (**use SOMA/G1 + RP ONLY**); ⛔ **Kimodo-SEED** (trained on the gated 288h Bones-SEED) → outputs arguably a "Result"/derivative of BONES-SEED + Sec 6 targets exactly a motion-substitute → **RADIOACTIVE, never**; ⛔ **Kimodo-SMPLX** = non-commercial (SMPL-X/MPI). Note (unsettled, flagged): NVIDIA's own right to train a generative model on the *public* SEED subset is inferred not documented; RP/GEM-X provenance (NVIDIA-owned) is the safe anchor. 🟡 **CMU MoCap** (`mocap.cs.cmu.edu/faqs`, verbatim): "may be copied, modified, or redistributed" + "You may include this data in commercially-sold products, but you **may not resell this data directly, even in converted form**" → no revenue cap, ML-training + baking OK, add NSF/mocap.cs.cmu.edu attribution; but the resale clause makes it **bake-into-avatars ONLY, NOT the standalone redistributed library**. 🟡 Truebones/Mixamo = same bake-yes/redistribute-no shape (Mixamo also bars ML-training corpora, D67). **PRODUCT DISTINCTION that changes what's usable:** baking motion INTO shipped avatars (looser — CMU + Kimodo-RP fine) vs selling a STANDALONE motion library (stricter — needs GEM-X-on-own-video or own mocap capture). **RECOMMENDED CLEAN CORPUS (ranked):** (1) **GEM-X on own self-shot video** — the only path clean for ALL uses incl. redistribution at unbounded scale; (2) **Kimodo-RP** for text-driven motion; (3) **CMU** as free bake-only bulk; (4) **own-capture** (mocap suit / work-for-hire actor) = bulletproof zero-dependency hedge against NVIDIA's revocability — all retargeted to Anny (Apache). **For SEEING natural motion now (clean, no GPU): CMU walk → CMU→Anny retarget (D67 kernel) → render locally.** Strategic note surfaced to user: clean scalable motion is a genuine hard MOAT of this project, not an afterthought (3rd licensing wall: Mixamo→BONES-SEED→now).
