- **D68 — Runtime AI-control architecture verified (survey of NVIDIA ACE / Inworld / Convai + primary sources, 2026-07-18): the puppet/data-packet model is the mainstream "two-clock director/animator" pattern; the user's LLM-director, separate-specialists, and DeepSeek-MTP intuitions are all confirmed correct.** Answers the user's "how does the AI drive the avatar at runtime?" question. **THE TWO-CLOCK SPLIT (the reference architecture, verified across every surveyed system):** (1) **DIRECTOR = the LLM/dialogue-manager**, runs **per turn** (never per frame), streams out: reply TEXT (sentence-by-sentence → TTS) + one EMOTION label + sparse gesture/action/clip-ID TAGS — it **never emits joint angles or blendshapes**; (2) **ANIMATOR = on-device @ 30–60 fps**: the **FACE is driven by the AUDIO** (audio→blendshape net) and the **BODY by the sparse tags** (clip library + state machine). "Audio-drives-face / tags-drive-body / LLM-drives-neither." **FACE (solved, clean, on-device):** every system emits ARKit blendshapes — primary pick **LAM_Audio2Expression** (`aigc3d`, Apache-2.0, Wav2Vec2 ONNX, real-time on CPU, audio→52 ARKit) which is already on the D57/D62 stack; higher-fidelity option **NVIDIA Audio2Face-3D** (code MIT / weights NVIDIA Open Model License, 30 fps ARKit + 11 emotions, v2.3 CNN & v3.0 2-step diffusion); **AVOID NeuroSync open weights (CC-BY-NC = non-commercial)**. Blend the director's emotion label onto the audio-driven face. **BODY (the honest reality):** **NO shipping product LLM-generates joint angles** — body = curated real mocap (D67, retargeted to Anny), triggered by the director's tags, blended by a state machine (NVIDIA ACE Animation Graph exposes exactly this via `posture_state`/`gesture_state`/`facial_gesture_state`/`position_state` HTTP knobs; Inworld/Convai fire `<action>`/emotion tags → predefined clips). Generative co-speech gesture (EMAGE, DiffSHEG, LiveGesture, MotionGPT) is **authoring-time desktop-GPU research, NOT phone-real-time**, and **almost all are trained on non-commercial data (SMPL-X/FLAME/AMASS/BEAT2) → cannot ship** — the **only clean generative body model is Kimodo-SOMA-SEED-v1.1** (NVIDIA Open Model, trained on the *open* 288h Bones-SEED; note the "700h" figure was the proprietary RP variant — the clean set is 288h; offline ~2–5 s/clip on a 3090 = an authoring tool, not a runtime). **Non-robotic look comes from technique, not a bigger model:** INERTIALIZATION on state transitions (decays the pose offset, preserves momentum — a mid-wave→idle stops naturally instead of "finishing the wave") + MOTION MATCHING for foot-planted locomotion + always-on ADDITIVE breathing/idle-sway + procedural gaze/head-IK. **LATENCY (two distinct clocks, don't conflate):** response-START latency (endpointing + STT + LLM TTFT + TTS-first-chunk; target user-stops→avatar-starts p50 300–500 ms) vs streaming THROUGHPUT (decode tok/s once talking). **The dominant, usually-omitted latency term is ENDPOINTING** — rule-based trailing-silence VAD waits 200–700 ms; semantic/"smart-turn" VAD cuts confident endpoints to ~300 ms → this is the #1 lever, ahead of model choice. **DeepSeek-V3 MTP / speculative decoding (user's idea — directionally RIGHT + 1 correction):** a small draft proposes K tokens, the big model verifies in ONE parallel pass, provably **LOSSLESS** (identical output distribution) → full strong-model quality at ~1.8× (V3 MTP: predict-next-2-tokens, 85–90% 2nd-token acceptance). **Correction:** it speeds SUSTAINED STREAMING (keeps TTS fed so long turns don't stall), **NOT** the initial response-start (first token still needs a full target forward pass), and it is **LANGUAGE-LAYER ONLY** — motion/lip-sync are frame-clocked diffusion/regression nets, nothing to speculate. DeepSeek-V3 is a 671B cloud MoE (doesn't run on-device) — the *technique* transfers to any LLM. **SPECIALISTS-over-monolith (validated):** each model on its own clock; **latency isolation** — the audio→face net runs straight off the audio and never waits on the LLM, so lips stay synced even while reasoning is slow; independent swap + clean per-component licensing; tiny deterministic on-device models fit the frame budget where a joint end-to-end model can't. **LLM placement:** cloud reasoning-LLM as director (turn spec-decoding ON) + on-device SLM as instant-ack/offline fallback — clean-license picks **Phi-3.5-mini (MIT)** or **Qwen2.5-1.5B (Apache)**; AVOID Qwen2.5-3B (custom Qwen license), treat Llama-3.2 (Community) + Gemma (Gemma Terms) as non-OSI; **Nemotron-4 4B** = purpose-built on-device digital-human SLM. **THE DATA PACKETS, made precise:** per frame ≈ 52 ARKit floats + 163 joint angles ≈ <1 KB → **~25–30 KB/s** total control signal = 3 orders of magnitude below streamed video = the entire quantitative justification for the on-device standalone-gaussian (§2/D50) thesis. **Full data flow:** Mic → on-device VAD/endpoint → STT → text → [cloud] LLM director (spec-decoding) streams text + emotion + clip-ID tags → TTS (ElevenLabs) audio → on-device LAM audio→52 ARKit + motion controller {clip ID + emotion}→163 joint angles → phone renders the splats. (§2, §3, §0.5; builds on D50/D57/D62/D67, elaborates [docs/avatar-architecture.md](docs/avatar-architecture.md) §2, [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D67 — Motion source decided (license-verified research, 2026-07-18): replace hand-authored curves with a real clean-license motion library/generator — Kimodo/GEM-X → SOMA-X → Anny — via a near-drop-in `SOMALayer` that outputs posed Anny vertices.** Triggered by the user correctly flagging the hand-written sine-wave walk as broken (inverted knees) + doll-like. **Root cause of the doll-look (biomechanics research):** the toy rotates only 8 limb bones on a frozen, non-translating torso → it's missing everything that makes gait read as real — **#1 root forward translation locked to foot contacts** (mine walks in place → foot skate), pelvis yaw(±4–8°)/obliquity(±5°)/tilt, COM lateral sway(~5cm, 1×/stride) + vertical bounce(2×/stride, high at mid-stance), heel-strike→toe-off foot roll, **contralateral** arm swing (mine were wrong-phase), thorax-vs-pelvis spine counter-rotation, and a **double-peak knee** (loading ~15–20° + swing ~60–70°) not one symmetric sine. **Knee inversion = flexion-axis sign error:** a real knee bends POSTERIORLY (heel rises up-and-back toward the glute); fix by negating the mediolateral-axis flexion, verifying BOTH knees (L/R bones mirrored → handedness differs, a global flip can fix one and break the other). **Real mocap contains ALL of this automatically** (captures the real skeleton + per-frame root trajectory) — which is why hand-authoring can't compete. **Motion sources, license-verified (primary):** ✅ **Kimodo** (`nv-tlabs/kimodo`, TEXT→motion diffusion, 77-joint SOMA skeleton, 30fps, npz = joint pos + rotation matrices + foot contacts + root traj; Apache code + NVIDIA-Open-Model weights for the SOMA/G1 variants; trained on ~700h commercial non-AMASS mocap; **promptable** — the recommended PRIMARY; synthetic so can foot-slide → use its foot contacts to clean) — **AVOID its SMPL-X checkpoint (NVIDIA R&D license)**; ✅ **GEM-X** (`NVlabs/GEM-X`, monocular VIDEO→SOMA motion; Apache + NVIDIA-Open; NVIDIA-owned data, non-AMASS) for capturing a specific real motion from own video; ✅ **CMU MoCap** (`mocap.cs.cmu.edu`, ~2,500 free real clips, commercial-OK — re-verify faqs.php before ship; older ~31-joint skeleton → needs retarget); ⛔ **MIXAMO = RESTRICTED** (royalty-free for game/film, but its FAQ/TOS **bars using content to train ML models / bulk-download for ML** — our pipeline renders frames that train gaussian weights → disqualified; prototyping-only); ⛔ **AMASS + all SMPL/SMPL-X-derived = non-commercial** (MPI/Max-Planck license) → always drive Anny through its **`soma` or `anny` topology, NEVER `smplx`** (Anny marks smplx NC). **Retarget path (the win):** SOMA-X's `SOMALayer(identity_model_type="anny")` consumes SOMA motion (poses (N,77,3) axis-angle + root_translation) and **outputs posed Anny `out["vertices"]` directly** — `03_render_motion.py` already consumes exactly that, so it's a contained swap of `walk_pose()`; **`py-soma-x` is already installed** (Anny dependency); install extra via `uv pip install "soma-x[anny]"` / `pip install "py-soma-x[anny]"`; code Apache-2.0. **Fallback** (only if you must render the exact DEFAULT 13,718-vertex mesh / reuse UV/splat assets keyed to it): `anny.Anny(rig="mixamo")` + the verified delta-rotation retarget kernel `ΔR_world = R_cur·R_restᵀ; P[b,:3,:3] = R_rest_world[b]ᵀ·ΔR_world·R_rest_world[b]` (the generalization of our swing-axis trick; re-derive bone indices from `bone_labels` since the mixamo rig is NOT (1,163,4,4)) — feed Kimodo's `global_rot_mats` (no FK needed) or a BVH via FK; also flagged: `rig="mixamo"` confirmed, `game_engine` rig UNCONFIRMED (verify the repo rig-asset dir before relying on it). **Caveat regardless of source:** retargeting reintroduces foot-skate/knee-pop from leg-length mismatch → apply foot-contact locking / foot-IK on the Anny target. **Minimum procedural fallback recipe** (ordered), if ever needed: root-translation-locked-to-foot-plants → correct knee direction/timing → pelvis yaw + lateral weight-shift → heel/toe foot roll → contralateral arm swing → 2×/stride vertical bounce. **Next:** install SOMA-X[anny] + a Kimodo-SOMA checkpoint, generate a walk/idle/gesture set, swap `03_render_motion.py`'s `walk_pose()` for `SOMALayer` output → real natural motion in the render pipeline + Blender playback. (§2, §0.5, §3; builds on D57/D60/D61/D64, corrects the SESSION_HANDOFF "native mixamo/game_engine" note, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D66 — CLARIFICATION/CORRECTION of D65's realism framing: SYNTHETIC photorealism is valid (the user's Omniverse vision works); "real capture" is the ceiling, NOT the only path. The user's unified vision is coherent and adopted (2026-07-18).** The user pushed back on D65 reading as "photoreal ⇒ real capture only." Correction: **the one rule is `output realism = training-image realism`.** Photoreal training images can come from (a) real capture (max realism, needs a rig, privacy) OR **(b) high-quality SYNTHETIC renders (Omniverse/Cycles/MetaHuman-class) — realism ceiling = asset/shader quality (skin scans, strand hair, path-traced light, cloth sim); fully automated + privacy-clean.** D65's "render the motion set GRAY" was a COST shortcut **specific to the real-capture branch** (photoreal render ≈ 100–1000× costlier/frame than gray, so if appearance comes from capture you render motion cheaply). **It does NOT apply to the user's chosen path** → on the synthetic-photoreal path we render **photoreal-AND-moving in one pass** (appearance + motion baked together), NOT gray. So D65's gray recommendation is conditional; D66 selects the synthetic-photoreal branch. **"Appearance is separate from motion" was misleading** — in the user's plan they come together in the same render; the ONLY thing genuinely "separate" is the **customization LAYERS** (D63): to SWAP a garment/hairstyle each part must be its own gaussian group → optimize **base body + each garment + each hairstyle SEPARATELY** (photoreal, multi-view, multi-pose), compose + recolor at runtime on the phone. **This is what makes synthetic-photoreal affordable:** you render a handful of base bodies + a wardrobe of parts *each once* (NOT body×outfit×hair combos) — the D63 combinatorial-collapse. **"The model" clarified:** there is NO single feed-forward net avatars pass through — it's **PER-SUBJECT OPTIMIZATION** run once per avatar/part → gaussian set → library (why not feed-forward: muted/soft standalone gaussians that need a runtime neural renderer, D60 — kills on-device). **Driving:** finished avatar = skeleton + ARKit blendshapes → ElevenLabs/voice → **Audio2Face/LAM = lip-sync DRIVER (not an appearance source; it animates the face, the render supplies its look)** + LLM picks motions; phone renders, tiny control signals stream (the puppet/data-packet model, D62). **Cost check (per-subject, synthetic-photoreal):** ~300–600 poses × ~8 cams Cycles-rendered ≈ tens of GPU-hrs ≈ ~$7–30/subject on a 4090 — fine for a CURATED hero+wardrobe library (not 100k avatars; you don't need that). **Net product direction (adopted):** fixed base (body+skin+rig) + swappable/recolorable clothing/hair/eyes → riggable avatars driven by an LLM/voice agent; user picks body+look then wardrobe, game-character-creator style. Updated [docs/avatar-architecture.md](docs/avatar-architecture.md) §8. (§2, §3, §0.5; corrects/builds on D65, builds on D60/D62/D63, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[asset-library-architecture]])
- **D65 — Training economics + realism VERIFIED (5-agent primary-source research, 2026-07-18): the per-subject-library path is cheap, no full dataset needed to start, Omniverse is out, and photorealism comes from capture not the renderer.** Answers the user's cost/time/GPU/quality questions. **(1) COST/GPU/TIME (minimum):** the cost fear assumed the *feed-forward* regime; D62's **per-subject-optimized library** fits each avatar independently on **ONE cheap consumer GPU** — measured: GaussianAvatars 11GB/2080Ti/~40–60min, 3DGS-Avatar ~30min, GART 30s–2.5min; VRAM 11–16GB so a **24GB RTX 4090/3090 is ample, NO A100/H100**. Cheapest: RTX 4090 ~$0.25–0.35/hr (3090 ~$0.12–0.20, A6000 48GB ~$0.40) on **Vast.ai/TensorDock spot**. **Per avatar ≈ $1–3 GPU / $5–15 all-in** (fit is NOT the cost driver — data render + tuning re-runs are); a **100-avatar library ≈ $100–1,500**. The dropped feed-forward path (regime B, e.g. GS-LRM) = **8–24× A100/H100 for days = $1.5–8k/run** — correctly out of the main path. **(2) NO full dataset needed to see results** (per-subject = one-in-one-out; overfitting one first de-risks every failure mode cheaply): **Milestone 0 (~$1–3, ½ day)** = fit a *static* 3DGS to ONE already-downloaded Anny-One scene on a rented 4090 (proves gsplat builds/trains/renders; verify a scene's views share one static pose); **Milestone 1 (~$5–15, a few GPU-hrs)** = render 1 subject × ~8 cams × ~300–600 pose-diverse frames → bind gaussians to the 163-bone Anny rig (LBS + face blendshapes) → optimize (~10–60min) → drive with a **held-out** motion clip = **first ANIMATABLE avatar** (and the true unit cost). Data/subject ≈ 8 cams (→16 for the face) × 300–600 poses ≈ 2.5k–10k images; binding constraint = POSE COVERAGE (echoes D54 motion=coverage). **(3) OMNIVERSE = hard NO on the AMD-iGPU laptop** (official reqs: NVIDIA RTX ≥3070, CUDA/OptiX/RT-cores — no AMD path) → local viewer = **Blender viewport / browser gsplat viewer (SuperSplat/Three.js)**; and even on the rented NVIDIA box **Replicator is the wrong tool** (forces a USD migration + a render-engine change vs the Blender-native Anny-One domain) → use **headless Blender Cycles + OptiX**, which gives the same photoreal look AND depth/normal/segmentation passes + exact camera poses. **(4) REALISM CRUX (the key mental model):** photorealism = f(the input pixels the gaussians are optimized against). The per-gaussian degree-3 SH color is fit by an L1+D-SSIM photometric loss = a *reproduction* mechanism, not a source; **real capture in → photoreal, CG renders in → CG look.** → **MAIN texture path = (b) PER-SUBJECT DENSE CAPTURE** of real people (multi-view photos/video, even neutral light) → real appearance baked into per-gaussian SH on the Anny rig = simultaneously the photoreal source AND the exact standalone on-device deliverable (GaussianAvatars/3DGS-Avatar/GART/Codec-Avatars lineage on gsplat). **Anny-One's Cycles/HumGen3D renders = geometry/rig/coverage supervision ONLY — never the skin-appearance source** (caps at CG + sim-to-real gap). Secondary lanes: **(c) mesh-conditioned multi-view PBR texture diffusion** (D43; TexDreamer-class) + **(d) UV skin libraries** = generate capture-free *fictional* library members (premium/R&D on-demand path) and supply albedo priors for unseen regions + a later *relightable*-PBR-gaussian upgrade. Relighting caveat: captured appearance is baked under capture light → v1 = capture neutral + bake; relightable = later. **(5) RENDER OUR MOTION DATASET GRAY** (pyrender/nvdiffrast, ~$3 or free-on-laptop for a 100-subject set) — its job is the geometry/motion/coverage signal (silhouette/depth/normal/camera/pose→deformation GT; gray is a *cleaner* geometric signal than a lit render). **Cycles is ~100–1000× costlier** (~$1.8–3.7k for a 100-subject set) to bake appearance that's discarded on this path → reserve Cycles for a *small photoreal validation set* and the *explicitly-funded fully-synthetic premium path*; **Omniverse essentially never** on the D62 path (its domain-randomization value is for the dropped feed-forward regime). **CONDITION the whole gray-render rec rests on:** the trainer must route **appearance from the capture/canonical source** and **deformation from the rig**, NOT force an RGB photometric loss on the gray animated frames (else → gray avatar). **STRATEGIC FORK surfaced for the user:** a *photoreal* library ⇒ **real per-subject capture** is required; a synthetic-only Anny/Anny-One library will look CG, not photoreal — a conscious product choice (real captured humans vs stylized synthetic characters). (§2, §3, §0.5; builds on D54/D57/D62/D64, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[generation-texture-method]], [[asset-library-architecture]])
- **D64 — 4D-dataset build kicked off: platform = pure-Python headless (no game engine); Anny-One verified clean-but-static → our contribution is the 4D/animated set only (2026-07-18).** Lost access to the shared RTX-5090 box (SESSION_HANDOFF §5/§6 box is gone) → **rent a GPU** (RunPod/Vast/Lambda; SSH-only, headless). **Platform decision (resolves the user's "Unreal? Blender? engine?" question):** the dataset pipeline is a **pure-Python headless render script, NOT a game engine** — Anny is a PyTorch parametric body (`naver/anny`, `pip install anny[warp,examples]`, class `anny.Anny` v0.5, uses NVIDIA Warp; **default/`soma` topology ONLY, `smplx`=NC per D56**), so posing + multi-cam rendering is code, not GUI work, and SSH-only is the native environment (no engine to download, no viewport). Dataset renderer = **pyrender + trimesh (EGL offscreen)** — non-differentiable is fine because differentiable rendering is a *training-time* gsplat concern, not dataset gen; PyTorch3D / Blender-Cycles / Omniverse are deferred realism upgrades that don't change the rest of the pipeline. **Anny-One VERIFIED** (resolves the SESSION_HANDOFF §8 open question): **Apache-2.0, ungated** ([download.europe.naverlabs.com/humans/AnnyOne](https://download.europe.naverlabs.com/humans/AnnyOne/)), **800k images / 1280² / Blender-Cycles / ≤40 cameras per scene / FOV 30–130°**, annotated with camera params + 3D pose/shape + segmentation — **but STATIC, no temporal data** (body poses sampled from **AMASS**, hands from **GRAB**; characters are **HumGen3D**-clothed with **Anny params as the GT label**), per the paper (arXiv 2511.03589). **Reframe of "the dataset we build":** Anny-One already supplies the static multi-view appearance/shape/pose backbone → **our contribution is the 4D (animated) multi-view sequences ONLY** — same subject, same cameras, moving over time (`subjects × motions × cams × frames`, far smaller than 800k). **Honest limit:** raw Anny is untextured → our pure-Python renders are **geometry/motion supervision** (multi-view silhouettes / depth / normals / deformation-over-time), **not photoreal RGB** — photoreal appearance stays with Anny-One or a later textured/Cycles path (matches D54 "dense views + mesh GT = fidelity levers; motion = coverage"). Clean-motion rule unchanged (self-authored / procedural / audited-Mixamo / D61 GEM-X·Kimodo·SOMA-X — **never AMASS**). **Two license flags to verify before commercial reliance** (though NAVER released the whole set Apache-2.0): Anny-One's poses are AMASS-derived and its characters are HumGen3D — we sidestep both by driving OUR animation with clean motion and rendering raw Anny geometry, not Anny-One's HumGen3D pixels. **Starter artifacts written** (`dataset/`): `README.md`, `00_bootstrap.sh` (rented-box setup — EGL libs + `anny[warp,examples]` + pyrender/trimesh, verifies GPU), `01_probe_anny.py` (introspects Anny's real API + a headless render smoke test — its output grounds the Phase-1 harness since Claude can't reach the box). **Next:** run the probe → render one vertical slice (1 body × 1 motion × N cams → contact sheet) → scale to the dataset + manifest → verify Anny-One license / HumGen3D provenance. **Two-environment split (verified this session): DEVELOP on the user's Windows laptop (AMD Ryzen 5625U iGPU, no CUDA), RENDER-full + TRAIN on the rented NVIDIA box.** The laptop's local device is **CPU-only** — its Vega `gfx90c` iGPU is unsupported by ROCm on *every* OS (RDNA3/4-only) and torch-directml is stale (no cp313 wheel, pins torch 2.2) → CPU is correct and sufficient for Anny posing/skinning (`torch 2.11+cpu` on py3.13 verified working). **Env gotcha:** Python 3.13 fights the graphics wheels (pyrender/PyOpenGL, Blender `bpy`, Open3D all prefer ≤3.12) → dev in a **conda Python-3.11** env. **Same pyrender code runs both places** — Windows uses its default hidden-window GL context (desktop session present; do NOT set `PYOPENGL_PLATFORM=egl`, which is Linux-only and breaks on Windows), the Linux box uses EGL; **Blender `bpy` Cycles-CPU is the fallback** if the AMD GL driver misbehaves. **Where to render:** the dev SLICE (≤ tens of GB) local is fine (uploads in <1 min); the FULL set renders **on the box** — at ~260 GB–1 TB it won't fit in the laptop's 357 GB free and would take ~0.5–5 days to upload (crossover: render-on-box wins past ~50–100 GB). Windows-dev scripts added: `dataset/00_bootstrap_windows.ps1` (conda-3.11 env) + `01_probe_anny.py` made platform-aware. (§7 handoff, §2, §3; builds on D53/D54/D55/D57/D60/D61, [[licensing-landmines]], [[humanoid-4dgs-status]])
- **D62 — FACE/EXPRESSION LAYER decision: the lip-sync/expression ceiling is the FLAME expression basis (a SUPERVISION problem), not the renderer → drive the face from AUDIO + ARKit blendshapes, not FLAME-jaw; faces train the same synthetic-multi-expression way the body uses multi-view-motion; the composite avatar is puppeted on-device by tiny LLM-authored control signals (2026-07-13).** Follows the user's product reframe — go **photoreal + standalone, DROP feed-forward** → per-asset optimization builds a **LIBRARY** of pre-baked animatable gaussian avatars, phone renders on-device, generation-on-demand is a premium async / separate R&D path (matches [[asset-library-architecture]] + D32; and this reframe retires D61's "standalone-at-feed-forward-speed" risk since the library isn't feed-forward). **The face is a SUPERVISION/REPRESENTATION problem:** the current FLAME+mask path caps quality — LAM's own paper (`aigc3d/LAM`, SIGGRAPH-2025) states the limit verbatim ("expressions FLAME does not account for, such as sticking out the tongue" + "reliance on accurately estimated FLAME parameters"), so lip-sync is mushy and cues are missed regardless of gaussian quality. **Key mental model — the face is a body-analog:** body pose = skeleton joint angles (SOMA); face pose = a blendshape "expression vocabulary." The user's insight is CORRECT — faces train the SAME way the body does (many avatars × many expressions → model learns expression→gaussian-deformation), and the ONLY non-obvious part is choosing the expression vocabulary (the "skeleton for the face") + the drive signal. **Decisions:** (1) expression vocabulary = **ARKit's 52 blendshapes** (proper visemes + eye/brow/gaze; phone-native; unencumbered coefficient convention), NOT FLAME's ~50 speech-agnostic scan blendshapes; (2) drive **lip-sync from AUDIO** via **NVIDIA Audio2Face-3D** (`NVIDIA/Audio2Face-3D`, weights `nvidia/Audio2Face-3D-v3.0`, open-sourced Sept-2025, **NVIDIA Open Model License = commercial-clean**; audio→ARKit blendshapes/mesh-deform; authoring-time on NVIDIA GPU) or **LAM_Audio2Expression** (`aigc3d/LAM_Audio2Expression`, Apache, realtime on-device audio→ARKit) — NOT audio→FLAME-jaw retarget; (3) give the **face a disproportionate gaussian + supervision-resolution budget** (uncanny-valley sensitivity); (4) explicitly model **tongue/teeth/inner-mouth + eyes/gaze** (neither FLAME nor ARKit covers the tongue); (5) for LIBRARY hero avatars, **per-subject dense-capture face optimization** (GaussianAvatars/Codec-Avatars/VHAP lineage) sidesteps the synthetic-FLAME ceiling entirely — optimize the real person's expression space, drive at runtime with Audio2Face/ARKit. **Composite avatar stack (all pieces already on disk):** Anny body (GEM-X/Kimodo motion, D61) + **LAM**-style head (Apache; audio/ARKit-driven, not FLAME-jaw) + **MM2** clothing. **Runtime / LLM control plane (the user's "data packets"):** the server streams only tiny CONTROL SIGNALS — body skeleton joint angles + face ARKit blendshape coefficients + audio — authored/selected by an **LLM**; the standalone gaussians live ON-DEVICE and deform to those signals (the §2/D50 motion-data-only streaming). This is exactly WHY standalone-on-device matters: you can't cheaply stream a server-rendered avatar, but you CAN stream a few hundred numbers/frame. **Caveats:** compositing seams (esp. neck) within the phone gaussian budget (D57); tongue/inner-mouth still needs explicit geometry; Audio2Face runs on NVIDIA GPU → authoring-time driver, on-device runtime uses LAM_Audio2Expression or pre-baked ARKit tracks; keep FLAME to **FLAME-2023-Open (CC-BY)** ONLY where the canonical topology still needs it (migrating canonical→ARKit reduces license exposure). (§0.5, §2, §3; builds on D50/D57/D60/D61, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D61 — NVIDIA open-source sweep: a commercially-clean "SOMA ecosystem" covers most of Stages 1–2, `nvdiffrast` (already in use) is NON-COMMERCIAL and must be replaced, and every pipeline stage now has a clean option (2026-07-13).** Triggered by evaluating `NVlabs/GEM-X` (video→whole-body pose): a license-verified fan-out over NVIDIA's 115-project open-source catalog + the `NVlabs`/`nv-tlabs`/`NVIDIAGameWorks`/`NVIDIA-RTX` research orgs (all licenses read from primary `LICENSE`/model-card sources). **License model clarified:** the **NVIDIA Open Model License = permissive COMMERCIAL** (grants reproduce/sell/distribute the model + derivatives; claims NO ownership of outputs → **outputs usable as training data**; obligations only: attribution + license copy on redistribution, don't bypass guardrails, no litigation vs NVIDIA, Trustworthy-AI/export compliance) — NOT to be confused with the **NVIDIA Source Code License** (the non-commercial research license on nvdiffrast et al.). **🎯 KEY FIND — the "SOMA ecosystem" is a deliberately-clean, near-complete Stage 1–2:** **GEM-X** (`NVlabs/GEM-X`; Apache code + NVIDIA-Open-Model weights; "trained on NVIDIA-owned data only"; outputs 77-joint SOMA whole-body motion; no SMPL-X at inference) = clean **video→motion**; **Kimodo** (`nv-tlabs/kimodo`; Apache + NVIDIA-Open-Model for the SOMA/G1 variants; trained on Bones RigPlay/SEED optical mocap, **NOT AMASS**) = clean **text→motion**; **SOMA-X** (`NVlabs/SOMA-X`; Apache) = the topology hub where **Anny is a NATIVE backend** → the SOMA→Anny retarget glue (Warp LBS). This maps directly onto SESSION_HANDOFF §7.3's "Anny→pose→clean-motion" and was engineered to dodge the SMPL/AMASS trap ([[licensing-landmines]]). Clean **IF** you avoid: Kimodo's SMPLX variant (NC R&D license), SOMA-X's SMPL/SMPL-X backends (gated NC files), and `NVlabs/GENMO` (self-labels "GEM", SMPL-based, NC — the name-trap). GEM-X input video must itself be clean (self-shot/public-domain/CC — the tool is clean, the input is not automatically). **⚠️ URGENT existing-dependency landmine:** **`nvdiffrast` = NVIDIA Source Code License (1-Way Commercial) = NON-COMMERCIAL**, and it sits in `generation/server.py`'s texture-bake path → REPLACE before commercial ship (Kaolin **DIB-R** / **gsplat** / PyTorch3D). Same NC family (skip): kaolin-wisp, nvdiffrec/3D-MoMa, diffusion-renderer, GET3D, XCube, LION. **Clean option per stage:** Stage-3 render harness = **Omniverse Replicator** (turnkey multi-cam RGB+depth+seg+normals+camera params; **free-for-production since May-2026**; clean for own-asset renders; NVIDIA-GPU-only) OR lightweight **Kaolin** (Apache DIB-R + differentiable camera API) / **Warp** (Apache) — recommend lightweight-first for the MVP dataset; Stage-4 model = **Lyra 1.0** (`nv-tlabs/lyra`; Apache code + **commercial** NVIDIA-Open-Model weights) = feed-forward image→**standalone `.ply` gaussians, no runtime neural net** = the cleanest reference for our exact target shape (scene-level → add rig+LBS), plus **L4GM** (arch ref, weights NC — retrain clean) + **GAvatar** (paper-only, pose-driven-primitive Gaussians = our skin-to-rig idea); Stage-4 data-gen = **Cosmos**/**GEN3C** (outputs usable as training data; GEN3C carries an unresolved Stable-Video-Diffusion upstream-provenance flag); Stage-5 = **Slang** (Apache — author LBS+splat shaders once → GLSL/WGSL/Metal) + **vk_gaussian_splatting** (`nvpro-samples`, Apache — **sort-free weighted-sum rendering** directly attacks the per-frame depth re-sort cost of moving splats, the D50 Tier-2 gate / [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]] catch). No NVIDIA phone/WebGPU splat runtime exists → the mkkellogg viewer stays the runtime. **Full findings + sequenced plan of action (Phases A–E) in [research/nvidia-open-source-scan.md](research/nvidia-open-source-scan.md).** (§0.5, §3, §2; builds on D53/D55/D56/D57/D60, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D60 — COURSE-CORRECTION: the LHM++ raw splat is muted (neural-renderer dependency) → wrong for on-device standalone photoreal; refocus on the ACTUAL core = building our own training DATASET (not started) (2026-07-04).** After deploying the D59 avatar to the phone, user observed it looks blurred/monochrome + upside-down. Diagnosis: (a) upside-down = display bug (Y-down vs viewer Y-up; fixed by 180°-about-X PLY flip, redeployed); (b) muted color = REAL — **LHM++ is feed-forward + a NEURAL RENDERER** (`featbacksplat`: gaussians carry *features*, a per-frame neural net decodes them → image; that net holds the quality). The exportable **raw splat is soft/desaturated** (RGB per-gaussian std ~0.09 even on a colorful in-distribution input; first test was also a bad input — an all-black anime side-profile). **A neural renderer at runtime = GPU-per-viewer server-side streaming = expensive + doesn't scale + not on-device → REJECTED by user.** User re-anchored the goal (correcting my drift): **on-device splat render, photoreal, animated, ONLY motion/bone data streamed — GS for photorealism** (= §2/D50 architecture; NOT mesh-fallback, NOT neural-streaming). **Key reframe:** the neural renderer is an LHM++ property, not a GS property — GS *can* be standalone-photoreal + on-device-animatable. The muted-standalone problem is the **fast-feed-forward** tradeoff; **per-scene optimization** (minutes/avatar) yields photoreal standalone gaussians (GaussianAvatars/3DGS-Avatar/SC-GS family, rebuild on gsplat+Anny), OR a feed-forward arch *designed* for standalone quality (D55 levers). **So: do NOT retrain LHM++'s arch as-is** (inherits muted standalone); the target model must output good STANDALONE gaussians. **BIGGER correction (user caught the real drift):** we detoured into LHM++ *inference/playback* (Phase 0) for hours and **never built the actual core — our own training DATASET.** Honest state: **dataset-creation setup DOES NOT EXIST** — Anny (parametric body) cloned as a building block, but **Anny-One NOT downloaded** and **zero dataset-gen scripts written.** The LHM++ work wasn't wasted (proved the clean Blackwell stack builds/runs — [[licensing-landmines]], BLACKWELL_BUILD.md — and surfaced the neural-renderer finding that rules out its arch), but it's a detour. **RE-FOCUS = build the dataset setup:** (1) free disk (99% full), (2) download Anny-One (~800k synthetic multi-view humans, clean, STATIC poses), (3) build the **Anny → pose → clean-motion → multi-camera render pipeline** (our 4D temporal-supervision generator; clean motion NOT AMASS), (4) pick the standalone-quality architecture, (5) rent GPUs to train. Full concrete state + pointers in **`SESSION_HANDOFF.md`** (written this turn for the next session). (§0.5, §3, §2; builds on D53/D54/D55/D57/D59, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]])
- **D59 — LHM++ RUNS END-TO-END on the Blackwell 5090 → first clean-path humanoid avatar generated (160k-gaussian 3DGS PLY, SMPLX-FREE) (2026-07-04).** After a long Blackwell build slog, `to_gs_ply.py` produced a valid **160,000-gaussian standard 3DGS PLY** (xyz/opacity/scale/rot/SH-deg0, 11MB, no f_rest) from a sample image via `LHMPP-700M` — and it **ran in SMPLX-FREE mode** ("DO NOT USE SMPL-X PRIOR ... disabled"), i.e. already the clean-path variant. Full reproducible recipe in `LHM-plusplus/BLACKWELL_BUILD.md`. **The 5 Blackwell keys (reusable for any sm_120 build):** (1) compile ALL CUDA exts for **`TORCH_CUDA_ARCH_LIST=9.0+PTX`** NOT `12.0` — CUDA-12.5 nvcc can't target `compute_120` (D44 lesson; I initially mis-set 12.0 and hit "nvcc fatal: Unsupported gpu architecture"); (2) **`spconv-cu126` (cumm 0.7.11) NOT `spconv-cu120`** — cu120's cumm 0.4.11 SIGFPEs in `implicit_gemm`/`from_numpy` on sm_120 (this was THE final blocker; faulthandler pinned it in the Sonata encoder's sparse conv); (3) **xformers→torch-SDPA monkeypatch** (no sm_120 kernel; reused D52 SV4D fix) via `_compat/sitecustomize.py`; (4) **chumpy numpy-alias shim** (numpy≥1.24 removed bool/int/float aliases) same sitecustomize; (5) **huggingface_hub 0.34.4 forced** + patched LHM++'s `model_download_utils.py` self-downgrade-to-0.23.2 hack. Source-built for 9.0+PTX: pytorch3d, bundled lib/pointops, torch_scatter, diff_gaussian_rasterization (Inria NC — audited clean, eval-only, swap→gsplat for ship), simple-knn. **Prior-bundle gotcha:** the tool's mid-run fetch pulls only small files → must fully `snapshot_download 3DAIGC/LHMPP-Prior` (voxel_grid/cano_1_volume.npz 931MB + voxel_192.pth 779MB). Peak ~20GB VRAM (fits idle window; the crash was spconv, never OOM). **Disk:** freed via removing orphaned sv4d env + generative-models (D58); ~13-20GB free through the build. **STATUS:** Phase-0 asset (a real 160k humanoid avatar splat) is READY at `/tmp/lhmpp_test.ply`; **Phase 2 clean-retrain base validated** (SMPLX-FREE path works). NEXT: deploy the avatar PLY to the D50 GitHub-Pages phone-test repo → on-device fps/appearance check (static first; animated-deformation = the real Tier-2 gate). (§0.5, §3; builds on D58/D52/D44/D50, [[licensing-landmines]])

Caveat: LHMPP-700M base needs SMPL-X model files (gated/NC) + priors at runtime — fine for internal eval; the SMPLX-FREE path avoids that but needs weights we must train. **Remaining GPU-gated:** Blackwell env reconcile (LHM++ pins torch2.3/cu121 → won't run on sm_120; rebuild on the trellis2 torch2.11/cu128 combo per D44/D51) + prior/SMPL-X deps + run inference → export .ply → deploy to phone-test repo. (§0.5, §3; builds on D57/D55/D50/D51, [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D57 — HUMANOID/AVATAR track CHOSEN as the first 4DGS-generation spike; Anny-One dataset + LHM licenses web-verified; compositional-attribute design adopted; privacy resolved (2026-07-01).** User chose to start with humanoids (over general objects) — justified now that D56 gave a clean foundation. **Two web-verifications that make it viable:** (1) **Anny-One = ~800k PHOTOREALISTIC SYNTHETIC humans** (full-body poses + hands + faces, multi-env, w/ 2D/3D joints, pose params, seg masks, camera intrinsics/extrinsics, hand/face keypoints), positioned privacy/license-unconstrained for COMMERCIAL use → **the clean humanoid training set largely EXISTS** (answers "do I build the dataset?" = mostly NO for humanoids; contrast the object path's ~200-GPU-day render). Caveats: verify the dataset's own download license (may differ from code Apache), and it's HMR/STATIC-pose so **4D still needs MOTION sequences generated by driving Anny with a CLEAN motion source (self-authored/procedural/Mixamo-audited, NOT AMASS=NC).** (2) **LHM (`aigc3d/LHM`, Alibaba, ICCV 2025) = Apache-2.0 CODE**, feed-forward single-image→3DGS animatable avatar (handles face+hands) — **but its released WEIGHTS are trained with SMPL-X + real human video → reference-only/tainted;** clean path = fork the Apache arch, swap SMPL-X→Anny(default/SOMA) in data-gen, retrain on Anny-One. **PRIVACY (user asked): resolved at the foundation** — Anny+Anny-One sever the biometric↔mesh link (synthetic geometry + WHO population averages, zero real scans), so GDPR's "3D vertex cloud of a real person = sensitive biometric" problem doesn't touch the foundation; residual is app-layer only → 3 rules: (a) don't hoard user uploads (process in-memory, delete, no silent retrain w/o consent), (b) train on synthetic (Anny-One) not scraped reality, (c) no re-ID/surveillance use (engineering summary, not legal advice). **COMPOSITIONAL-ATTRIBUTE DESIGN adopted (user idea, endorsed):** user sets hair color/style, clothing, skin tone, body size via described options; build as **disentangled LAYERS / separate modules** (beats monolith for control) — body shape=Anny semantic sliders (free), skin/face=texture layer, **hair=separate module (body models don't do hair)**, **clothing=separate garment layer (the hard one: drape over varied bodies + deform under motion)**, text→attributes=small conditioning model/structured UI. Honest hard parts: garment fitting across shapes, hair/cloth motion deformation, compositing multiple splat layers within the phone gaussian budget (D50). **ROADMAP:** Phase 0 (cheap gate, FIRST) = animated LHM-sample avatar through the phone splat test (D50 Tier-2) — kill/greenlight before training; Phase 1 (no-train) = stand up Anny+Anny-One+fork LHM, run reference weights for the quality bar, close the 2 verifies; Phase 2 = clean retrain (SMPL-X→Anny, on Anny-One) = single-image→animatable avatar; Phase 3 = 4D/clean-motion + on-device playback; Phase 4 = hair/clothing/skin as controllable layers. Start Phase 0 + Phase 1 in parallel. **Still a DEFERRED-PREMIUM R&D track relative to the D35 mesh-first platform MVP; the humanoid avatar generator is not the lead product.** (§0.5, §3, §0.9; builds on D53/D54/D55/D56/D49/D50, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D56 — Anny confirmed clean AND a hidden-NC TOPOLOGY TRAP identified (web-verified, 2026-07-01).** Verified the D55 Anny finding + a critical sub-license landmine the user surfaced. **Anny (`naver/anny`, Apache-2.0, arXiv 2511.03589) is genuinely clean because it's SCAN-FREE** — built from MakeHuman/MPFB2 (CC0) + WHO anthropometric calibration (semantic age/height/weight/muscle sliders, infant→elder, native Mixamo-rig compat), so it never touches the proprietary 3D scans that bind SMPL/SMPL-X/FLAME to Max-Planck NC terms. **THE TRAP (D41-class — headline-clean, downstream-NC):** Anny's **`smplx` interoperability topology is download-for-NON-COMMERCIAL-use-only**; its purpose (drop Anny into existing SMPL-X benchmark codebases) is exactly the tempting path that silently re-introduces NC. **SHIP RULE: build the LHM/HMR pipeline on Anny's DEFAULT (13,380-vert/163-bone) or `soma` topology (Apache-2.0, adapted from NVlabs SOMA-X) ONLY; NEVER enable the `smplx` flag in any code path touching a shippable artifact** (dataset-gen, tracking, or released weights). Verify per-download notices + SOMA-X's own NVlabs terms at integration. **Payoff:** Anny is a fully-differentiable PyTorch mesh → passes gradients to an image encoder like SMPL-X → **Anny(default/SOMA) + clean-retrained LHM = the first fully commercially-clean, end-to-end, single-photo animatable-avatar path this project has found** (still a deferred separate track per D55, but now legally viable end-to-end). - **D55 — Deep-research VERIFIED the L4GM numbers, the fidelity levers to beat it, and a clean-license humanoid path (Anny + LHM) (2026-07-01).** 5-angle deep-research, 23 primary sources, 24/25 claims confirmed 3-0. **L4GM exact (verified):** LGM asymmetric U-Net (6 down/1 mid/5 up, ch [64,128,256,512,1024,1024]) + temporal self-attn after each cross-view attn (~0.4–0.5B backbone; papers report architecture NOT a headline param count — param count is not the metric these models optimize); **hard-fixed 65,536 gaussians/frame (128×128×4), 14 params each**; **256×256 input, 512×512 supervision**, 16-frame clips, 0.3s/pass. **License = weights CC-BY-NC-SA-4.0 "research only" + trained on non-commercial Objaverse-4D → commercially DEAD; code Apache-2.0 → architecture copyable, retrain-from-scratch-on-clean-data required** ([[licensing-landmines]] updated). **Blur root-cause CONFIRMED:** 256/512px caps high-freq + fixed 65K budget + single-pass pixel-aligned from a 128×128 feature map. **DATASET SCALE BAR (sobering):** Objaverse-4D = 44K objects × 110K animations × 48 views → 12M videos/300M frames, rendered Blender-EEVEE in **3 days on 200 GPUs** — i.e. ~200 GPU-days just to RENDER before any training (reframes D53/D54 "rent GPUs no problem"). **FIDELITY LEVERS to beat L4GM (verified, = the architecture the dataset must feed):** (1) **untie gaussian budget from a fixed set** — per-pixel unprojection (GS-LRM 2–4 views 0.23s/A100; GRM 4 views ~0.1s) scales budget with input res × view count; (2) per-pixel's own flaw (duplicated gaussians, tied to pixels not scene complexity) fixed by **F4Splat** (predicted per-region densification, budget controllable at inference w/o retraining); (3) **decouple appearance-res from geometry via per-primitive textures — LGTM (Apple+HKU) hits 4K with few primitives, LPIPS −23–75%** (the "raise resolution not gaussian count" lever); (4) **near-optimization quality at feed-forward speed ALREADY EXISTS — DGS-LRM (Meta, NeurIPS 2025) = first feed-forward DEFORMABLE 3DGS from monocular video, "comparable to optimization-based methods," ~+3dB PSNR over L4GM** (validates hybrid init+refine AND confirms **target a DEFORMABLE rep [canonical+deformation], NOT the D53 "per-frame 3DGS then stitch"**; verify DGS-LRM license). → **Dataset spec: per-pixel/adaptive budget, MULTI-VIEW input (2–4), high-res supervision (≥512→4K via textures), deformable target, gsplat (Apache) rasterizer.** **MIXED-MODALITY (your any-combo input goal): decoupled, not monolithic** — multimodal front-end (text/image→synthesize views/video via diffusion) → sparse-view reconstructor (GRM: "4 views can be generated from text or a single image"; L4GM: image→video-diffusion→reconstruct); GaussianAnything (ICLR2025) does shared-latent point+text+image but true shared-latent/modality-dropout training was thinly evidenced → **build ONE reconstructor, swap front-ends per modality.** **HUMANOIDS — verdict UPGRADED from D54's "avoid":** parametric composition confirmed right + SMPL/SMPL-X/STAR (academic-only, commercial via Meshcapade)/FLAME/MANO/AMASS all NC — BUT a **clean path EXISTS: Anny (NAVER Labs Europe, Apache-2.0) = commercially-clean parametric human body model** ([[licensing-landmines]]), and **LHM (single-image→animatable 3DGS avatar, 2–6.5s, 0.5/0.7/1B) = the humanoid-specific feed-forward architecture** to retrain clean on Anny (verify LHM's own license). → **humanoids = a SEPARATE, DEFERRED but now-VIABLE track** (clean foundation exists), still not the v1 starting point (perceptual bar + real build). **Open (unverified in this pool):** exact hybrid feed-forward+refine wall-clock/quality for 4D; exact realistic multi-GPU cost to reproduce the 300M-frame blueprint clean; LHM/DGS-LRM own licenses. **NET recommendation: start NARROW + DEEP** (few object categories, per-pixel/deformable multi-view architecture, hybrid feed-forward+short-refine) to prove quality BEFORE industrializing the 200-GPU-day render — and still behind D49's phone-playback gate. (§0.5, §3, §0.9; builds on D53/D54/D47/D48/D49, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]])
- **D54 — Multi-modal "full-context" dataset idea + L4GM-quality diagnosis: the two real FIDELITY levers are dense views + mesh GT; quality is capped by ARCHITECTURE not dataset; L4GM is blurry by design, not from a pixel cap (2026-07-01).** User proposed enriching the D53 dataset so each object carries **full context** — self-authored motions, dense angle images (more views than the video), physics (where applicable), 3D mesh, and text describing object/motion/POV — asking if it yields better 4DGS; separately observed **L4GM looks bad** and asked if they "limit pixels to keep motion smooth," concluding a bespoke dataset means "train our own model, rent GPUs, no problem." **DIAGNOSIS — why L4GM is blurry (architectural, NOT a dataset problem, NOT a deliberate pixel cap):** (1) it's a **feed-forward amortized reconstructor** (~1s/asset) → trades fidelity for speed *by design*; the same input optimized per-scene (4D-GS ~30min) looks far better — this is the fundamental quality/speed axis, L4GM sits at the fast/blurry end; (2) **fixed low gaussian budget tied to LGM's limited-resolution pixel-aligned feature grid** → detail is capped *before* data enters; more data can't lift an architectural cap; (3) **single input view** → hallucinated unseen sides come out soft/wrong. **On "limit pixels for smooth motion" → NO:** smoothness comes from **temporal interpolation between keyframe gaussian sets + a temporal-consistency layer**, not throttled resolution (grain of truth: low output res makes things blobby which *hides* flicker — a side-effect of low capacity, not a technique). Sharpness (gaussian budget + supervision resolution) and smoothness (deformation/interpolation model) are governed by different things. **DATASET MODALITIES RANKED by real FIDELITY impact:** 🟢 **dense angle images** = biggest lever (more view coverage → less under-constraint → sharper unseen sides); 🟢 **3D mesh GT** = strong lever (depth/normal/occupancy supervision + regularizes gaussian positions, kills floaters); 🟡 **custom motions** = coverage + clean license (broadens motion distribution, doesn't sharpen a frame); 🟡 **physics** = capability not fidelity (plausible trajectories, orthogonal to splat sharpness); 🟡 **text** = control/conditioning for the text→4D input path, not a quality lever. → of the five, only **two are fidelity levers (views + mesh)**; the rest add capability/coverage. **THE REFRAME (critical):** a rich dataset is **necessary but not sufficient** — L4GM would NOT become sharp fed this data; its ceiling is architecture. Quality is actually capped by **(a) representation & budget** (more gaussians / higher-res or deformable-canonical rep vs per-frame), **(b) supervision resolution** (high-res rendering loss + LPIPS + geometric losses vs mesh GT — supervise at 256px → get 256px quality regardless of data), **(c) input constraint** (multi-view *input* is far easier to make sharp than single-view — decide if the product is single-image→4D [L4GM's hard mode] or multi-image→4D), **(d) optimization vs feed-forward** (biggest jump = **hybrid: feed-forward init + short per-scene optimization refine** — near-opt quality without the full 30min). The hard/uncertain part is designing an architecture that can EXPLOIT dense views + mesh, not collecting the data. **SCALE CHECK on "rent GPUs, no problem":** training GPU-hours are ~a third of the real cost — the underestimated parts are (1) **dataset generation** = a multi-TB rendering+storage pipeline (dense views × motions × frames × physics), itself large compute + months of engineering; (2) **architecture R&D + many training-run iterations** (L4GM was a team+NVIDIA-compute effort, not one run); (3) an **objective eval harness** ("is this actually sharper than L4GM?"). Doable, and the proprietary clean 4D dataset is a genuine moat/asset — but it's a research-team-scale commitment. Runtime/product gates (D47/D48) unchanged → still deferred-premium; D49 playback test still first. **Offered a focused deep-research pass:** (a) L4GM's exact architecture / gaussian budget / training resolution (pin *why* it's blurry), (b) current fidelity levers in feed-forward 3D/4D recon (GRM, LGM successors, hybrid init+refine) — so the model gets designed, not just the data. (§0.5, §3, §0.9; builds on D53/D47/D48/D49, [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D53 — Synthetic-data plan to train a clean-license feed-forward text/image/video→4DGS model EVALUATED: feasible (it's the L4GM recipe) but improves only the generation axis, and the cleanliness bottleneck moves off the render engines (2026-07-01).** User proposed: rig Objaverse (or bespoke) objects, animate them in **Unreal / NVIDIA Omniverse Replicator / Unity Perception**, hang multiple cameras for a multi-view dataset, turn each motion frame into 3DGS, stitch → 4DGS, and train a feed-forward `text/image/video→4DGS` model — motivated by the lack of a clean commercial dataset (vs SV4D's "research purposes" flag D51, L4GM NC D47). **VERDICT — feasible, and it's exactly how the SOTA feed-forward 4D models were built:** **L4GM was trained entirely on multi-view renders of animated Objaverse objects** (TRELLIS/LGM/GRM likewise on Objaverse MV renders) → the user independently re-derived L4GM's methodology (its paper = the blueprint AND the failure-mode list; read first). **The strong insight:** synthetic rendering gives *perfect* ground truth, so multi-view **AND temporal consistency is true by construction** — this dissolves the exact "the research problem" D49 named (SV4D/CAT4D exist *only* to enforce consistency from real monocular video; synthetic makes it free). **Where "commercially clean" actually breaks (the bottleneck moves OFF the engines):** the three tools are the least of it — Replicator is purpose-built for synthetic data (your renders of your assets are yours; avoid NVIDIA SimReady asset libs), Unity Perception = Apache-2.0, Unreal = per-seat for non-game industrial, free pre-revenue (verify current terms). The real exposure: **(1) MOTIONS = the unflagged landmine** — SMPL/AMASS mocap is NON-COMMERCIAL ([[licensing-landmines]]), Mixamo is gray for *training*; procedural/self-authored motion is clean → audit the motion source with render-stack rigor; **(2) Objaverse** must be filtered to **CC0/CC-BY** (§4a; mostly static+unrigged, so auto-rig via UniRig adds quality variance); **(3) the per-frame fit must use gsplat (Apache), not the Inria rasterizer** (D41 trap); **(4) patents ≠ copyright (D48)** — clean data clears copyright, NOT freedom-to-operate on the 4DGS/deformation method. **Technical weak points:** (a) **"per-frame 3DGS then stitch" is the wrong supervision** — independent per-frame fits have no correspondence → flickering flipbook, huge on disk (the D48 63MB/frame failure mode); prefer a **deformable rep (canonical + deformation field)** as pseudo-GT, or better skip pre-fitting and **train with a rendering loss vs the GT views** (LGM/L4GM style — the MV video *is* the supervision); (b) **sim-to-real domain gap** → object-centric, fragile on real user photos/video (L4GM's documented weakness; Replicator domain-randomization narrows but won't close it); (c) **motion diversity/naturalness on arbitrary auto-rigged Objaverse is itself a bottleneck** and caps output quality; (d) **compute** — foundation-grade feed-forward 4D training = multi-GPU-weeks, NOT realistic on the shared single 5090 (can't even fully occupy it without evicting shnri's qwen) → a fine-tune/distill is realistic, from-scratch foundation is not. **STRATEGIC RE-ANCHOR (the crux):** this improves the **generation/licensing axis** (real value — a plausible route to a clean-license 4D generator, which SV4D-research-flag / L4GM-NC don't give) but **touches NONE of the runtime gates that actually decide shipping** (D47/D48: iOS renders-in-canvas-but-can't-world-anchor, 5–30× mesh weight, mesh-first governs) → a perfect clean generator still lands as a **deferred-premium un-anchored web hero feature**, not an MVP unblock. **And D49's action item still comes first: prove ONE 4D output plays back on a real phone BEFORE building any generator.** **RECOMMENDATION:** read L4GM's data pipeline; don't train from scratch — use synthetic to build a clean eval/fine-tune set and distill/fine-tune a backbone; if fitting pseudo-GT target a deformable rep with gsplat (or train with rendering loss, no fit); audit the motion source; sequence the whole thing behind the D49 playback test. Open verify items (offered a deep-research pass): current 2026 commercial terms for Omniverse Replicator / Unreal-industrial / Unity Perception, and L4GM's exact training-data recipe + license. (§0.5, §3, §0.9; builds on D47/D48/D49/D51, [[licensing-landmines]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D52 — SV4D 2.0 Stage-A RUNS end-to-end on the 5090 — first generated 4D output (2026-07-01).** During a GPU window (qwen idled out → 31GB free, grabbed it), SV4D2 completed `camel.gif` → **4 novel-view videos** (`generation/sv4d2_out/000000_v001..v004.mp4`, ~7 min, clean exit, VRAM released). Backed up into the repo (durable) + a side-by-side `view.html` viewer (localhost:8098). **The reusable technical win = the Blackwell (sm_120) attention fix:** SV4D2 uses head_dim-512 attention, which xformers CANNOT run on capability-12.0 (flash needs ≤256, cutlass needs ≤sm9.0) → the fix is a monkeypatch routing `xformers.ops.memory_efficient_attention` → torch native SDPA (math backend handles any head_dim), and it must be **rank-aware** (spacetime attn passes 4D `(B,M,H,K)`, sgm CrossAttention passes 3D `(B*heads,M,dim)`). Lives in `generative-models/run_sv4d2_patched.py` — same monkeypatch philosophy as D41's gsplat swap; **applies to any sgm/SVD-family model on Blackwell.** **Stage A = DONE (proof SV4D2 works on our HW).** Remaining: **Stage B** (multi-view videos → dynamic splat, gsplat-rasterized 4D fit — the real deliverable), then the image→video front-end for single-image input. Still gated by the shared GPU (opportunistic windows only; don't evict shnri's qwen). Supersedes D51's "validated to model-load." (§0.5; builds on D51/D41, [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D51 — SV4D 2.0 self-host build COMPLETE on the 5090 (validated to model-load); blocked only by shared-GPU contention; key finding: open release = multi-view VIDEO only, splat needs a Stage-B recon (2026-06-29).** Per user's "build out SV4D" go-ahead, stood up **SV4D 2.0** (Stability, `stabilityai/sv4d2.0`, `generative-models` repo): env cloned from `trellis2` (preserves the D44 Blackwell torch 2.11+cu128 / xformers 0.0.35 combo), inference deps installed UNPINNED (skipped the repo's ancient `triton==2.0.0`/`transformers==4.19.1`/`torchdata` pins that would break Blackwell), `sgm` + deps import clean, `sv4d2.safetensors` (12GB) downloaded (HF token from `generation/.env`, user `yyousef4u`, access OK). Ran end-to-end to model-construction — only failure = CUDA OOM. **KEY FINDINGS:** (1) **SV4D2's open release outputs novel-view `.mp4` VIDEOS, not a splat** — the "4D asset generation" reconstruction is NOT in the repo. Getting a playable dynamic splat needs a **Stage-B 4D-gaussian fit** (joint spatio-temporal opt over the ~5–9 views/frame, since per-frame is too sparse), which most 4D-GS code rides the **Inria NC rasterizer** → must swap in **gsplat (Apache)** like D41. So "SV4D" = Stage A (video→multiview-video, set up) + Stage B (multiview-video→splat, the real remaining work). (2) **License flag:** SV4D2 README says "for research purposes" — verify the model-card's actual commercial terms (Community License vs research-only) before treating it as a production generator; if research-only it's prototype-only (reinforces D48 clean-room/alternative). (3) **Infra constraint:** the box is a **shared multi-user server** (users `shnri`, `sov1`, `sov2`); the single 5090 is occupied by **`shnri`'s live, publicly-tunneled qwen3.6:27b (24GB via Ollama, `epic-birthd-ai`)** — can't coexist with SV4D2 (~14–20GB) on 32GB. Per user: **do not stop/evict anything not ours** (even opportunistic idle-grabbing risks OOM-ing shnri's service on its next reload). SV4D run is **parked, fully ready, resumes instantly** when the GPU frees (a `nvidia-smi` watcher is armed to notify on ≥20GB free). Build lives in conda env `sv4d` + `/home/sov2/projects/generative-models`. (§0.5; builds on D47/D48/D49/D50, [[licensing-landmines]])
- **D50 — Tier-1 phone render-floor test PASSES empirically: 200k-splat object @ DPR 2.0 holds 45–60fps sustained over 2 min on a real phone, no thermal decay (2026-06-29).** Built a phone playback benchmark (`generation/phone_splat_test.html` + a deployable copy at `~/4dgs-splat-test`, repo github.com/yousef-yy4u/4dgs-splat-test) — a real 200k-gaussian 3DGS splat (`benchmark/assets/robot_crab_200k.ply`) rendered via mkkellogg GaussianSplats3D (WebGL/three.js), **auto-orbited to force a depth re-sort every frame** (the documented mobile bottleneck + the per-frame work a moving/4D scene imposes), with a live FPS/ms HUD, ×1/2/3 copy multiplier, and DPR control. **Result (after controlling for a low-battery throttling confound that initially pinned both devices to a stable 30):** laptop = 60fps stable; **phone (iPhone 14, A15, 2022 — mainstream not flagship-latest) = 45–60fps fluctuating, SUSTAINED over 2 min with no decay, at "max settings" = 3× copies (~600k gaussians) @ DPR 2.0 with auto-orbit** (full native res + continuous re-sort = the heaviest case tested). **Interpretation:** the render floor (rasterize + continuous re-sort of ~600k gaussians across 3 objects) is empirically NOT the wall D47 feared — and clears with HEADROOM via plain WebGL (not even WebGPU), on a 3-yr-old phone, at a count that exceeds §2's "100–300k/object, 750k=diminishing-returns" budget. **Refines D48's "rendering wall overstated" from argued to MEASURED.** Caveats (do not over-claim): (1) this is the FLOOR — a true 4D asset adds per-frame deformation eval on top (cheaper than the sort, but nonzero) → real 4D lands somewhat below; (2) ONE device (iPhone 14 / Safari) — weaker Android mid-range will do worse → LOD/quality tiers still mandatory (§2/§2a); (3) streaming/download size (.spz/.sog) untested + separate (a network question, not GPU). **Deploy lesson:** static splat viewers need permissive headers — Railway's default CSP blocked GS3D's blob: web worker AND its WASM sorter; fix = `worker-src 'self' blob:` + `script-src … 'wasm-unsafe-eval'` (see `~/4dgs-splat-test/server.js`), or just use GitHub Pages (no CSP). **NEXT (de-risk ladder): Tier-2 = regenerate a skinned animated splat + run `poc_splat_smooth.html` (per-frame LBS deformation = the real 4D cost); Tier-3 = compare compressed-4D file sizes to the download budget.** Floor passing keeps the D48 verdict intact: 4DGS animation is a credible PREMIUM un-anchored WebGPU/WebGL-device hero feature worth the spike — now with the first empirical evidence the runtime is reachable. (§3, §2a, §0.5; builds on D47/D48/D49, [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D49 — Two concrete image/video→4D papers evaluated (SV4D, CAT4D); user's proposed pipeline IS the SOTA architecture but its crux is cross-view consistency; de-risk PLAYBACK before building generation (2026-06-29).** User proposed `single image → multiple views → per-view videos → 4DGS core` and asked "can't we just use" arXiv 2407.17470 + 2411.18613. **Identified:** **2407.17470 = SV4D (Stability AI + Northeastern)** — monocular video/image → *unified* diffusion → novel-view videos → optimize 4D; **weights under Stability AI Community License (free incl. COMMERCIAL under ~$1M ARR, Enterprise license above; non-OSI, revocable, attribution) → actually usable today for a pre-revenue startup (yellow flag, not red); verify exact HF model-card terms + check SV4D 2.0**. **2411.18613 = CAT4D (Google DeepMind)** — single image/video → multiview-video diffusion → per-scene opt (deformable 3DGS); **NO code/weights released (project page only) + rides Google's proprietary unreleased diffusion model → NOT usable, it's a quality north-star not a tool**. Both ride the 4D-GS/Inria lineage (gsplat substitutes for rendering). **User's pipeline shape is CORRECT — it's literally what these papers do — BUT the "videos from each view" step is THE research problem:** animating each view *independently* yields cross-view temporal inconsistency (arm raises at frame 10 in one view, 14 in another) → 4DGS fit produces floating-gaussian garbage. SV4D/CAT4D's whole contribution is enforcing multi-view AND temporal consistency JOINTLY (SV4D = unified diffusion over view×time; CAT4D = alternating MV/temporal sampling) — you can't glue independent off-the-shelf parts; you need a consistency-enforcing core = use SV4D's model OR retrain your own (clean-room, D48 pt2). **Two invariants regardless of model:** (1) these are per-scene OPTIMIZATION, **minutes/asset** (SV4D opt; CAT4D ~25min/A100) — an async premium tier, NOT free/instant feed-forward; (2) generation quality does NOT touch the D48 runtime gates (60fps on a phone + iOS=canvas-viewer-not-AR). **RECOMMENDATION — de-risk in REVERSE pipeline order:** before building any generation, take ONE SV4D output → a WebGPU mobile splat player → **test on a real mid-Android + iPhone** (fps? thermal throttle after 2min? compressed size? AR-placeable on iOS or canvas-only?). Only if playback passes do you build the single-image→consistent-MV-video→4DGS pipeline. Generation is the part that provably works (published); phone playback is what decides if it ships — build the test that can KILL the idea first. (§3, §0.5; refines D47/D48, builds on D34, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D48 — D47 REFINED after user due-diligence (2 GitHub repos + a streaming-cost analysis): the rendering "wall" was overstated, but 4DGS stays a deferred PREMIUM R&D track, not a pivot (2026-06-29).** Three corrections/confirmations to D47: **(1) "Apple SHARP" identified — and it's STATIC, not 4D.** [apple/ml-sharp](https://github.com/apple/ml-sharp) = "SHARP: Sharp Monocular View Synthesis," single-image→**static** 3DGS (<1s) — same category as TripoSplat, NOT dynamic. License = **Apple ML Research Model License, non-commercial ("commercial exploitation prohibited")**. The [AndriiShramko/4DGS-Video-Generator](https://github.com/AndriiShramko/4DGS-Video-Generator) "4D" repo fakes 4D by running SHARP **per-frame** and stacking PLYs (no temporal model → flicker; **~63 MB/frame, 1.18M gaussians/frame → ~19 GB uncompressed for 10s**; the worst-case representation for streaming; MIT app code but NC model → unshippable). **(2) Clean-room "copy the model not the code" = legitimate but a real build, gated on PATENTS not copyright.** Copyright protects code (expression) not the paper's method → reimplementing from scratch is generally non-infringing (precedent: **gsplat Apache = a clean reimpl of Inria's NC rasterizer**). BUT you must retrain weights from scratch on commercially-clean data (real project) AND clear **patent freedom-to-operate** (NVIDIA/Apple file aggressively; "we wrote our own code" is no defense vs a patent). So 4D-gen clean-room = a months-long R&D commitment, not a loophole — the exact thing self-host-TRELLIS.2 + clean components was chosen to avoid. Static splats need none of this (TripoSplat MIT + gsplat Apache already clean). **(3) Mobile rendering — D47 OVERSTATED the wall (correction owed):** WebGPU GPU-radix-sort is the real fix for the CPU-sort bottleneck and is **no longer desktop-only — iOS Safari shipped WebGPU in iOS 26 (2025)**, Android Chrome has it; D47's "WebGPU desktop-only" came from *Gracia's product matrix*, not a platform limit. So dynamic-splat mobile rendering is "hard/bleeding-edge," NOT "impossible." And the streaming-cost nightmare ($10.8k/mo, 13.5 GB/viewer-hour) **models the WRONG usage** — that's continuous volumetric-video streaming; OUR asset is a **short looping object, download-once-cache-loop** (~20–80 MB for a 5s clip with a true 4D codec), so egress is "MB/view" on a free/cheap-egress CDN (Cloudflare R2 ≈ $0 egress, Bunny ≈ $0.01/GB), NOT a per-hour bleed — a CDN-choice problem, not fundamental. **What still gates it to deferred-premium (not pivot):** (a) **iOS can render a splat in a canvas but canNOT world-anchor it in AR** (no WebXR; AR Quick Look = USDZ/mesh) → on iPhone 4DGS = turntable/embed VIEWER, not "view in your space" — fine for un-anchored web, fatal for the anchored-marker surface on ~half of users; (b) asset still ~5–30× a mesh GLB + sustained-60fps/thermals on LOW-end phones unproven → ship with MESH FALLBACK regardless; (c) tooling is assemble-the-research-repos, not an SDK like model-viewer that works on every phone today; (d) generation still NC → see (2). **UPDATED VERDICT (supersedes D47's "research demo, no"):** 4DGS animation is a **credible premium, un-anchored, WebGPU-device hero feature worth a real spike AFTER the mesh MVP ships** — gated on a clean-license gen path (likely self-built), iOS=viewer-not-AR, and a true 4D representation + mesh fallback. **Mesh-first MVP still ships first because it works on EVERY device today off-the-shelf.** D46 plan unchanged; this only re-grades the animated-splat track from "deferred/fragile" to "deferred premium R&D with a clearer worth-it gate." (§3, §0.5, §0.6, §0.9; refines D47, builds on D33/D34, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]])
- **D47 — 4DGS-animation pivot EVALUATED and DECLINED; runtime playback (not generation) is the wall — mesh-first D46 holds (deep-research, 2026-06-29).** User proposed pivoting from skinned-mesh animation to a **pure 4D Gaussian Splatting** generate+play pipeline (text/image→GenAI-video→bg-cut→4DGS engine→"pure 4DGS web viewer/splat asset"), with **L4GM** (feed-forward, ~1s) as a free tier and **"Apple SHARP"/4D-GS** (per-video optimization) as premium. Research verdict (5 converging primary/secondary sources; adversarial-vote step cut short by a token-limit but search/fetch completed): **the proposal optimizes Latency A (generation, on our 5090) when the wall is Latency B (playback on the customer's phone) — the exact trap §3 names.** **Generation = feasible:** L4GM is real (single-view video→4D gaussians, ~1s) but trained ONLY on synthetic Objaverse → object-centric, fragile on arbitrary real user video; output is 4D gaussians not mesh. 4D-GS optimization is **~30 min/scene** (paper figure on a 3090; user's "3–5 min" optimistic) and **built on the Inria `diff_gaussian_rasterizer`** (the D41 non-commercial trap). **Runtime playback = a brick wall for our mobile-browser distribution:** (a) 4D-GS's "real-time" 82fps is 800×800 on a DESKTOP RTX 3090, not a phone; (b) **Gracia AI** (most advanced *commercial* 4DGS streaming) **requires a WebGPU DESKTOP browser — smartphones explicitly unsupported — at ~80 Mbit/s** for 120k splats/frame; (c) the web-splat viewer ecosystem (SuperSplat/PlayCanvas/three.js/Babylon/Gauzilla) is **static-oriented**, no mobile dynamic benchmarks; (d) 2026 industry state: dynamic 4DGS is early-commercial, **confined to film/sports broadcasting, not consumer mobile**; (e) **iOS has NO path** — WebKit-only, no WebXR, AR Quick Look is USDZ/mesh. **Licensing = non-commercial at every layer** (L4GM = NVIDIA, almost-certainly NC; 4D-GS = Inria NC rasterizer; Gracia = proprietary) — **no clean MIT/Apache end-to-end dynamic-splat gen+playback stack exists.** **Could NOT verify (token-limit, don't change verdict):** L4GM's exact license (treat as NC blocker until proven), and **"Apple SHARP" — I could not find a 4DGS framework by that name from Apple; likely a conflation, do NOT architect a tier around it.** **DECISION: do not pivot to pure-4DGS output** — it breaks the every-phone distribution that IS the product and the licensing is dirty top-to-bottom. **Animated splats stay deferred R&D (D33/D34)** — revisit ONLY when BOTH a mobile-capable dynamic-splat web renderer AND a clean-license gen+playback stack exist. **D46 mesh-first plan stands**; the "wow" premium tier available TODAY is **STATIC splats (TripoSplat, single hero object)** which at least render in current web viewers, NOT animated. (§3 two-latencies, §0.5, §0.6, §0.9; builds on D33/D34/D46, [[licensing-landmines]], [[rigged-gaussian-splatting]], [[generation-pipeline-reality-check]])
- **D46 — Generation architecture LOCKED: self-host is the user-facing ENGINE, the API is a back-office spare tire; MVP animation = presets + custom-upload; 2D = billboard + 2D→3D (2026-06-29).** Resolves "which vendor + what do we build" after D45. **The reframe (the real answer to 'which one'):** the user-facing flow (*user uploads → we generate → they publish*) runs ENTIRELY on the self-hosted stack — not just for $0 cost but because routing end-users' generation through Meshy/Tripo IS the "make the Service available to third parties / resell access to the Service" both ToS restrict (D45). So **local = the engine, Tripo API = back-office overflow/quality spare tire on OUR account, never wired into the user path** (and even that wants Tripo's written OK at resale scale). **Meshy is DROPPED** — its only edge was cheap rigging, but its rigger needs textured *humanoids*, while self-hosted **UniRig (MIT) rigs arbitrary categories** for free; Meshy adds nothing the local stack doesn't do better + cleaner. **Final stack:** (1) **Mesh = default "Standard" lane** → TRELLIS.2 self-host (every user-facing gen); (2) **Splat = premium "Photoreal" lane** → **TripoSplat (MIT) self-host**, single-image feed-forward (up to 262k gaussians, no per-asset optimization/cleanup = inherently low human-error), **kept as static hero/premium tier NOT the default** (mesh-first D34 still governs: splats fill-rate-expensive on phone/glasses, animated splats deferred). One knob, two lanes, same single-image input. GS is self-host regardless since neither API sells splatting (D45). (3) **Rig/animate** → UniRig (MIT) self-host. (4) Tripo API = spare tire. **Animation MVP scope (user decision):** **presets + custom upload** — Tier 1 plug-and-play: auto-rig (UniRig) → curated motion library (idle/wave/spin/bounce/walk) + transform anims (rotate/bob/pulse/float) on ANY asset incl. flat 2D signs (no rig needed); Tier 2 escape hatch: users upload their own rigged/animated GLB/FBX (validate+ingest). **Keyframe STUDIO deferred to post-MVP** ("we can build a studio later"); **AI-assist (text→motion, video→mocap→retarget) deferred further** (research-grade per D42/findings). Animation = mesh LBS (cheap to render); animated splats stay deferred (D34). **2D-drawing scope (user decision):** **billboard + 2D→3D** — (a) 2D drawing → flat animated BILLBOARD (transform anims; perfect for the storefront-signage beachhead), (b) 2D drawing → 3D object (image-to-3D) then animate as 3D. **Live2D-style articulated 2D-character rigging DEFERRED** (separate deep feature; revisit only if signage demand pulls it). Refines §0.5 (animation editor → presets+upload for MVP; splatting → TripoSplat two-lane). (§0.5, §0.9; builds on D34/D42/D43/D44/D45, [[licensing-landmines]], [[generation-texture-method]])
- **D45 — The Tripo-vs-Meshy "buy comparison" (D43/D44 open item) is now done via deep-research (mid-2026, 5-angle fan-out, 24/25 claims 3-vote-verified). Two findings reshape the make-vs-buy call; net = KEEP self-hosted TRELLIS.2 as default, buy only for overflow.** Context: user proposed "scrap local generation entirely, offload everything to Meshy or Tripo incl. splatting." **Finding 1 — splatting CANNOT be bought:** neither Meshy nor Tripo sells Gaussian-splatting as a billed API task (both pricing pages are mesh-only). Tripo's **TripoSplat** (single image→3D Gaussians, .ply/.splat, up to 262k gaussians) exists ONLY as **MIT-licensed open-source weights you self-host** (HuggingFace `VAST-AI/TripoSplat`, ComfyUI-native) — clean commercial, but a self-host job regardless of vendor. So "offload everything incl. splatting" is impossible; splatting stays self-hosted. **Finding 2 — our reseller model bumps both vendors' anti-resale clauses:** paid tiers grant the ACCOUNT HOLDER (us) full ownership/commercial rights to output (free tiers = CC BY 4.0, attribution-to-vendor, unusable), BUT **[CC scope clarified from the live ToS, 2026-06-29]: the CC license attaches to the OUTPUT (generated model) and is triggered by the FREE TIER — NOT by uploading. Your INPUT never becomes CC just by entering the platform; uploading grants only a narrow service-operation license (Meshy §3.2 "as necessary to provide the Service"; Tripo §5.2.2 service-provision-only + "will not use Inputs/Outputs as training data"). On a PAID account both input (private) and output (owned, full commercial/resale) are clean — nothing is CC. Free-tier traps: Meshy free output = CC BY 4.0 even for a derivative of YOUR OWN uploaded asset; Tripo free (§5.2.1) is harsher — Tripo retains broad rights over your INPUTS too; and Meshy Community publishing (§3.3) invokes CC0 (gives the asset away). → Production = always a PAID account, never publish to community.** Separately, **Meshy ToU §2.6(v)** bars "resell or redistribute the Service or access to the Service," §2.6(iv) bars competing products, **§2.6(xi) bars using generated assets to train/improve a competing AI model**; **Tripo terms** bar making "the Generative Service available to any third party, incl. end users, without prior written authorization" + bar building a competing product. Reading: we may **resell finished ASSETS**, but our "customer uploads image → we generate → they own it" flow likely needs an **explicit enterprise/white-label agreement** on either vendor; and §2.6(xi)/Tripo's compete-ban directly threaten using purchased output to train/improve TRELLIS.2-class self-host (must NOT). **Pricing (both ~$0.30/textured image→3D mesh):** Tripo flat $0.01/credit — H2/H3 textured 30cr ($0.30), P1 50cr; no-texture 20/40cr; standalone texturing 10cr; **rig 25cr + animation 10cr/retarget = 35cr**. Meshy — textured 30cr (Meshy-6/low-poly) or 15cr (other models), no-texture 20/5cr; **rig 5cr + animation 3cr = 8cr (4× cheaper than Tripo on the animated step)**. Subscriptions: Meshy Pro $20/mo→1,000cr, 10 concurrent; Tripo Pro ~$14–20/mo→3,000cr, Max→25,000cr, Team→45,000cr (more credits/$ + scales higher). Gaps NOT published by either: API rate limits, max texture res, per-asset latency, named volume discounts (only Meshy "10 concurrent" + Meshy output formats glb/obj/fbx/stl/usdz/3mf surfaced) → require a sales conversation. **RECOMMENDATION (refines D43/D44): do NOT fully scrap local.** (1) **TRELLIS.2 stays the default generation backend** — $0/asset, no licensing strings, no anti-resale exposure, quality already validated (D44); buying is for quality/throughput OVERFLOW only. (2) **If buying one mesh vendor, pick Tripo** — transparent $0.01/credit maps onto per-asset cost accounting, larger volume bundles, and its ecosystem gives the MIT TripoSplat self-host path (one mental model: mesh-buy + splat-self-host). (3) **Meshy only as a cheap rig/animation add-on** IF its rig quality holds — but its rigging needs a *textured humanoid* GLB with clear limbs (likely too narrow for arbitrary signage/product assets; verify before relying). (4) **Splatting = self-host TripoSplat (MIT) regardless** — no one sells it. (5) **Before any contract, get white-label/reseller terms in writing from both** — our exact flow needs it, and that's where unpublished volume/throughput discounts live. Net stack: **TRELLIS.2 (self-host default) + TripoSplat (self-host splat) + Tripo API (on-demand overflow/premium mesh)**, Meshy as possible rig/anim lever. The "offload everything to a managed API" premise doesn't hold: splatting can't be bought + the reseller model needs an enterprise agreement either way → self-host's clean-license + no-anti-resale advantages get STRONGER, not weaker. Verify pricing/ToS live before contracting (time-sensitive, frequent promos). (§0.5, §0.9; builds on D43/D44, [[generation-texture-method]], [[licensing-landmines]])
